O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, three dear sons, I have completed this book which is the end of the science of medicine in full, and have made an end through its explanations and through its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in vision that I accomplish this with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is strengthened in our region and is strange throughout all, so it has perished the science and has been cut off, and there is nothing left of its forces than the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this came the errors and the vanities, and minds are closed and science is banished.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems to me that I will revive it along with the order of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation.  
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	And I will come along with the forms of the implements of cautery and other instruments of the work, with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as it is necessary.  
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason of those that no good masters of hands are found in our time, is the art of medicine lengthened.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who deals with it to ascend in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the articulation of the members, and the forms and the conjunctions and the separations of veins, and have knowledge of the bones and nerves and brains and the number of vessels, and the movement and of moving and resting veins, and their place of origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this Hippocrates says that the name alone with the name is much, but with the work little. 
et meismement en l’art de main.	and similarly in the art of hand.  
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you in the introduction of this book that whoever is not acquainted with the things previously mentioned, should beware lest he fall into error and injure men.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	As many times as I have seen, more than those who meddle in this science and abandon their science and experience. 
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a fool cut an abscess of scrofula or goiter from a woman's neck and cut her arteries in her neck. 
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	Because so much blood came out that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And see another case who treats a stone from a man's age, and the stone was great; 
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	if he carried it out with a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.  
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been called for the treatment, and see the disposition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I well know that if one cut it he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And see another case who took care of the duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the fracture there was a wound; 
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the ignorant surgeon brought the fracture over the wound to the stars with a very strong ligature, and did not leave any ointment on the wound, and left him thus in the end;
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commanded him that he should not untie it.
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and so the leg remained swollen, and the foot, and came to ruin. 
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and hurried to come loosen the leg; 
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I loosened it he was at peace and felt no pain.  
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all ways the corruption had already been confirmed in the limb, and I could not heal it; 
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and did not cease the corruption to go through the limb until the limb was altogether lost. 
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see another wound that opens an abscess, and then inflames because of the malice of its master.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a sore, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it is not fitting that one touch it with iron unless in such a place where one can completely remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for this reason, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into II divisions: 
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, work where there is danger in many dispositions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and peril. 
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For which it is necessary that you guard yourselves, so that the foolish onlookers cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take your weapons in caution, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and be praised; 
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave the diseases treatable to good health;  
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	And remove your weapons from that which makes you doubt, and have faith in yourselves so that you may come from this world to the other one of glory.  
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Gaulish says in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take care of any illness, unless you are called a fool." 
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatise according to III chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are about fire cauteries and medicinal cauteries, and the chapters are ordered from the head to the feet; 
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and of the forms of the instruments, and of the handles of the cautery, and of all that is necessary in the work.  
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and probing, and about blisters and wounds, and extracting arrows, and similar things. 
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and the chapters are ordered and the forms of the instruments.  
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; 
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it is ordered from the head down to the feet, and the forms of the instruments.  
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus as we remember from the work, it befits me to say the quality of the aid and of the discomfort of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of help, and of harm, are the longest speech and most subtle science and the secret replies; 
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and of this they spoke the most wise men, and agreed to it;  
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and I suffice myself with few words, because I fear length. 
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery helps universally to all complexions or it has matter, except for those complexions: 
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	This is to know hot constitution by means of matter, and dry constitution by means of matter. 
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In hot and dry constitution altogether matter, they said none and said that cautery there is great help;  
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the other said the contrary: 
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery does not worth to disease that comes from heat and dryness.  
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is so hot, and should not be cured of a hot disease by heat, nor by dryness; 
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and said he who says the contrary that cautery does great help to a hot and dry disease that comes in the bodies of men.  
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you examine the body of a man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it never once by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in every way, let no one intercede besides he who has proved it, and who knows by long use the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of complexions of men, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and space of time; 
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	Of other complexions we have no fear, even in cold and moist diseases. 
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the masters assembled and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, sons, that fire cautery together is of the secrets of cures, and of greater goodness than cautery of burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire is simple, and does not come out further than to the member that is burnt, and does not harm any other member except for this one.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	The hot medicines come from one limb to another by distancing, and bring to the limb diseases of grievous healing; 
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and perhaps it harms the patient.  
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire because of its height and the goodness of its substance does not do this, if there is no superfluity. 
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found through experiment and the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it was on the truth of things; 
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for this I excuse myself from the length of the speech, because it does not please me that I keep you from the secret which is answered in fire, and the quality of the work, how it displaces the diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; 
or le recevez en vos pensees.	receive him in your thoughts. 
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that it is agreed upon in what time the cauteries should be made, and how long they are held.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is suitable at all times because the harms coming from it are lessened by the help of the cautery. 
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And even if the cautery is for necessary pains, outside and until they cannot endure the time that greater harm does not come to the limb. 
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think about it, dear child, as foolish people do;  
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	because the illness that is cured by cautery has no return;
et il le dient ensi;	and they say thus; 
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they think, because cauterization is only a medicine that changes the complexion and dries the humors that are the cause of pain, and is more valuable than medicine for the haste of its value, and for the virtue of its work and its authority. 
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is a most important thing that the patient comes at some point according to the complexion of the sick person and the location of the illness and its virtue; 
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	And are gathered in him the superfluities by the acquisition of meats and similar things, if it is not cauteries administered in their place where there is little superfluity and moisture, as cauteries of teeth for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return; 
mais ce avient poc.	but this happens rarely.  
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand at all for what reason cautery is called the last of medicine, and it is true; 
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cautery is worth after medicine, but their understanding is false, and it is cautery the last of medicine because when we administer ways of cures in any disease and they are not worth, then we administer our cautery, and it is worth. 
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clear that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intentions of foolish men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cautery instruments of gold are better than those of iron, and they said this because of the quality of gold and the height of its substance. 
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the burns of the cautery do not cause rot, but this is not true because I have tested it, and I have found that it is true in some men. 
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and gold cauteries are worth more than those of iron, as they say.  
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	But nonetheless when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools very quickly.  
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if one heats it too much;
si font au feu;	as they do to fire; 
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus there is enough risk of hindrance.  
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this we use our fire cautery which we have proved useful to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or I have ordered this chapter of the head to the foot, so that the way is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and cold on the head, and there are two kinds made because of a sickness called "soda," and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and ears, and for multitude of dreams and tooth pain and throat pain, and also for all maladies which come from cold such as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by medicine solutive modifying the dose III or IV, according to what the virtues and the age and the custom of the patient can endure. 
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make go back the head of the sick one.  
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then make him sit crossed between your hands, and put his hands over his thighs; 
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	after put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes;  
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and where your two thumbs will come, if it bleeds then scavenge the cautery which is called “olivare,” for this is its form;
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And put it on the place marked with ink, and do descending and pulling your hand peck and peck turning; 
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then lift your hand slightly, and return to the place if you see the bone one small;  
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, then begin the cautery again until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	after take one peck of sail, and put in soft and moist cotton inside, and put on the place, and let him leave it for 3 days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	After place on top of the leg soft in butter; 
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave on until the burning is gone;  
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treat the wound of the ointment which is called "tetrafarmaçon", as long as it is healed.   
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And they say the ancients, that when more stays open the wound, more it purges;
et por ce si aide mues.	and for this reason so help moves.  
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said any of these that one must leave the cautery so that part of the bone is burned, and then one should reset what is burned of the bone, and be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And they say the other one must the cautery so leave on, and push so hard that it lowers the bone as wide as the whorl that women put in their spindles for those that the humors come out moved;
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must leave the wound long open; 
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	after that one must cure and soothe.  
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two manners of cauteries do not seem to me to be good at all, except in some men where there is a way of fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and I seem to him that I should leave it; 
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	because the head is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we witness in other members;  
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and even when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is more salved and quicker for me, and from this I operate in these matters altogether salvation. 
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When throughout the head comes chronic pain, and lasts for a long time, then the patient must use herbs and pills that are called "cochie", and of purging of the head and oils and plasters; 
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one does to him the cauterization that we have said before, and it is not effective.  
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take ward if the head of the sick person is of strong nature, and that it is not too cold; 
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	therefore the cauterize those below that cautery we have said above. 
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After make cauterize on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make the cauterize where it is called "vessels"; 
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and there are them in which one puts suction cups; 
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and align your hand so that you do not see up to the bone;  
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels much more great pain in this cauterization than the others, and I will speak of it later; 
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is necessary that the cauterizations of the horns be more subtle than those where one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is the form; 
dou cautere dou chief	Of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When in one part of the head comes sudden pain, and it extends to the patient up to the eye, and the head is purged by medicinal fluids, and one has made the other cures that I have said in the division of the diseases, and all this does not help; 
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Therefore I make cautery in two manners, that is to say of hot medicine and of fire. 
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cautery of hot medicine is that you take a piece of alum, and remove the bark and cut it into two pieces, as small as the head of a pin, and then make a hollow in the temple where the pain holds, in such a manner that you can place the piece of alum beneath the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	And when it is placed, bind it well and leave it thus for twelve hours. 
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	And then unbind it and carefully remove the piece of alum, and leave the wound thus for two or three days.  
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	Then place a poultice soaked in butter on top until it heals. 
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After this, cure with ointment until it is healed.
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	And if you see that it needs any other medicines burning which I have written or otherwise treated of burning medicines.  
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is made in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery with this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closed" because the head is made in the shape of a cloak or it has the point of curvature, and in the middle there is a small appearance. 
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	And place it in the painful place, and hold your hand and press the fire a little bit, until the half of the thickness of the heart is burned. 
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is outside, and flows an abundance of blood.  
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	After put cotton in the shape of wool, and place it on the spot for three days. 
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then you put cotton moistened in butter, and then cure the spot with ointment until it is healed.
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	And if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery that is called "cultellare," at all the tip, and you keep from covering the artery in this migraine which is not ancient. 
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you cure migraine as we have said before in the divisions of maladies, and it profits not, and see that the cauteries before said of the medicine and of iron do not suffice him, then it is necessary that you heat up the cautery which is called «cultellare» until it be white; 
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	And thus rule upon the place ailing a line of half a digit of long, and remove your hand once, and strain that you do not cover the artery and that you do not come until the bone; 
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	And guard the mandible that moves when one manipulates it, and the nerve not be irritated except only to the moving and that spasm does not come to the patient, and guard against flowing of blood from the artery when it shall be cut, or cutting has great fear and especially to him who does not know it, and who is not studying and experienced;  
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and let the work be in mid way; 
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to restrain blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it appears in this book. 
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery does not suffice to the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the center as well as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed;  
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cautery which has two blades; 
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.  
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When in the ear comes pain from cold, and one has applied medicines solutives and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pains do not move, then use this cautery which is called “point”, for this is its form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After prick all around the ear of the sick person, or where the pain is held in both, and move away a little above the root of the ear once you have marked the place to burn; 
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and have X points near each ear; 
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	after curing the place until it is healed.  
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Torments that must be cured by cautery are few except for those that move phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; 
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not make cautery on likenesses that come from dryness and nerve spam.  
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you cure this likeness of torment that moves phlegm from the eyes and expulsions of the head and gargles, and this is not enough, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with III cauteries:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, and the other a point outside the temple, and the third at the adjustment of the II lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cautery in the part that opens healthy, and let it cauterize the place on the head of the ear above a point below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as one thumb;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and let the cautery remain so long as the middle of the heart is burned. 
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery: 
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is the likeness of the cutter that we have put before, but it is a little more subtle and it should be that the blade is a little larger; 
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	after care its place as I have said before, as long as it is healed. 
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is old and you cure it as we have said, and it does not benefit, and the patient has no fever, then I make IV cauteries: 
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two on the two horns of the head, and I remove the head, and I put it where it is called "vessels" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and be cured as we have said before. 
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness, it is necessary to give the patient large doses and pills that modify the brain;  
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	After the king has treated the head of the sick person completely, and he places on the back of the head a cataplasm of mustard as is written in the treatise of plasters; 
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	And this is the manner of the cautery:  
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if the fire if done as I have said.   
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If it is healthy this way, good is; 
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if it isn't, then do three cauteries of the head, descending to the neck, and have a space between each cautery one finger-width thick;
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and cure it as the others, and if you see it needs to be added, and the patient is suffering, then do one cautery in the middle; 
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it is necessary, II others on the II horns, and treat until it is healed. 
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cautery which is called 'olivare', as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the chief be purified of herbs and things that we have said before; 
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	after having anointed the head of the sick man, then make cautery at the center of the head and on each horn, and the last one and III on the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the illness is advanced, then make IV cauteries on the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and leave it until the most of the heart is burned, and lift your hand; 
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after treatment until it is healed, and let the cautery which is called 'olivare' that we have said before
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should not use fire cautery except the one who is phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to modify the brain with herbs and other remedies that we have said in the division when the patient is great and suffers from bad medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot bear it, make gargarismes for them and chewing, often changing the brain with good meats. 
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After the king's head in the middle, and I make the cautery according to what we have said before, and the cautery on the vessel, and on each horn. 
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if the patient is weak and suffering, make cautery as I have said to him who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olive according to the manner that I have said. 
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is feverish, make the cautery subtle according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholy are the superfluities or the humors corrupted and phlegm thick, then the cautery of teals cauteries as we have said to him who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the superfluities are declining to melancholy, and the body of the sick person is moist, then give him to drink something by which the brain may be purified, according to what it is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After the king's head of the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	After that, make a poultice of flax well done, also as the circle, put it in the middle of the head.  
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	And the patient sit crossed, and be well held on all sides
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	After present the linen, and worths moves of butter of goat ancient. 
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	And the warmth to fire temperately, so that the two if one puts him may suffer.  
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	After empty the circle by within remove the chief, and let it cool; 
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And do this to patient each week once with other good government, until it be healthy.  
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you see him being cauterized by making more than one burn to all of the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This manner of cautery moistens the brain importantly;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	And then puts above cotton moistened in butter and grease of gelling.  
de l’awe des eulz	of the opening of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the ache comes first to the eyes by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and give the patient something purifying for the head, and guard him from all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe more times fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After he commands to rear his chief, and he does cautery removed the chief, and he does II cauteries on the II temples if the descending of the awe is at the II eyes together, or in I if the descending is in I;
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	And cut at all the cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the heart, and be the cautery long according to the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	And guard against bleeding, and if you see too much blood issue, then staunch it with the power as you have.  
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in incision the caution how to staunch it. 
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and at no time is cautery or a hatchet used below the two bones behind.  
dou cors des larmes	From the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins or beside the arteries that are in the appearance of the head outside.  
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and one sees that these are cold phlegmatic superfluities, then I make the cautery that I said at the beginning of the work descending to the eyes. 
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I cauterize in the middle of the head, and two cauterizes on the two temples, and two cauterizes where a hatchet is used below the two bones.  
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if need be more, cauterize it carefully above the eyebrow with a small cautery. 
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	From the body of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you medicate him according to what we have said in the division, and he does not benefit, then give the patient three crushed nuts to drink; 
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	afterwards make an incision on the head, and do a cautery or middling olive-oil cautery;  
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two cauteries of the cautery which is called 'clavilis' on the two eyebrows, one slightly under the hair. 
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and beware of the artery so that you do not cover it.  
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the parchment of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then the cauterization of this cautery which is called «olivare».
de coi ci est li forme:	of this the form is
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see, make two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are; 
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not let go of your hand except until a third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said. 
dou poil qui point l’oil	Hair which pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	At times it happens that the hairs of the eyes are converted to the eyelids, and prick the eye, and one does cautery according to two manners: 
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is to say, of fire, or of burning medicine.  
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; 
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow. 
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they have grown and are equal, then put the patient in a sound place; 
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	after which upon the paper of the eyes draw a figure like that of the leaf of myrtle, and let it be the beginning of the sign next to the hairs;  
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then put moistened cotton in egg white and parsley juice on the eye, then heat the cautery of which this is the form: 
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cauterizing on the figure that you have marked point and point many times, so that the hairs are burned at the place. 
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	And the signs of the healthiness of the work is that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs raised to the height of the eye. 
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	Then lift your hand, and leave it so for three days, then place moistened cotton in butter until the burn is removed; 
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the ointment cure until it is healed.  
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if after these, the hairs come, and the paper is softened then begin again the cauterizing on that same place, just as you did first;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if the hairs are burned out, then cauterize until the paper is lifted to its natural place, and is even, and does not prick the hair the eye. 
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The cauteries of medicine burning is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make parchment in the shape of the myrtle leaf.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	Then take French soap and live coal, of each one ounce, and grind together well. 
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	And make it hot, so that it does not cool down, then spread on the form as you have made it like the leaf of myrtle, and put on the paper over the eyes. 
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	And if the patient holds only in one eye, then one should work in that one, and if in both.  
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	And put under the eye cotton moistened in water of an egg; 
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	And the head of the patient be in your healthy hand and put your back showing over the medicine, and press it and  squeeze all times that the patient feels a burn from the medicine, because he feels a burning as of fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then take the medicine to your right.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the burning will have passed, then lift the place of the eye, and look if you see the paper lifted as if it was lifted by constraint of fire or by incision.  
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if so, then so much the better. 
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, it is again put in the medicine on the place where the medicine has not worked, until your works are equal, and your eyes are set. 
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on moistened cotton in butter until the burns are closed, then treat the place of the ointment which is called “diphanos” and others, until it is healed. 
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary, that you be careful with your work, by great care that it does not fall of the medicine into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hair pricks in the eye, then begin the medicine on that place which is softened by the paper properly, just as you have done before. 
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed.
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And this is the form of the leaf of myrtle. 
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	Know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to these be your constrictions; 
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and let not the right way be restored to him whose is the study of this art.  
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the cure of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments are not beneficial, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put his head in a sound position. 
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	And hold his head between your hands in such a way that he does not move or tilt his head.
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	After, put moistened cotton in the white of an egg or in juice of parsley on the eye; 
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	After, heat the cautery that is such.  
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	And when it is heated, put it to the head like the form of a quill feather, so that the cautery is together. 
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	If you see it, so be pointed from one head to the other, and if you see it, so be as a tent. 
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	But nonetheless, this which is shaved is worth more for your work.  
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After press the fistula if it is opened, and clean out the rot, and dry it. 
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	And if it is closed, so work it, and clean out fiercely the bowel.  
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	After put upon the hot cautery, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part of the skin under the eye, that your hands do not make folly.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	And put the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.  
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If this is not, so begin again the cautery once more, and another if you have need of it, and leave it for three days.  
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	After I put on cotton moistened in butter, and the cure of the desiccant ointment until it is healed, and if 40 days pass that it is not healed, then put on corrosive medicinal ointment until the bone is uncovered.  
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and the king according to what he would come in his chapter. 
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Listen to a fistula, and cut it open.
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	After put in the split a subtle camel of which this is the form: 
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and it is made to the quantity of one third of an ounce;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand or camel firmly, and let the patient not move in any way that the melted lead does not run into his eye;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary to put on the eye of the patient cotton moistened in vinegar or in honey; 
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the ulcer if it is in its place of fistula, and the whole by miraculous health.  
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, it is necessary to administer ointment to the nose, and bring the fistula back to the body of the nose according to what is proper in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	of the punctures in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, there are crevices in lips called "hairs," and also in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these wounds of those that we have said in divisions, and the cure does not benefit, then apply the small scalpel cautery according to this form.
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And he places it carefully in those crevices until it comes to the bottom. 
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	After curing the place of carbuncle until it is healed.  
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes in the root of the tongue or in the uvula, or palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has rotted and grown and is emptied and becomes a fistula; 
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said in the divisions, and it does not profit at all.  
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then it is necessary that you have the cautery according to the quantity of the fistula. 
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the bot or opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron cauterizes to the bottom of it, and its last place. 
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do thus once or II, after the cure of what we have said in cures, as long as it is healthy; 
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is cured thus, it is good;  
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if this is not the case, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in your chapter. 
dou movement des dens	of the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine and that is not effective, then put the chief of the patient in your hand; 
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after sharpen the cautery whose form will come after here in this manner that you put a chain on the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and put inside the cautery hot carefully, and hold so long that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth;  
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	after lift your hand and repeat the cautery according to your will; 
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	after fill the patient's mouth with saltwater, and let it stay for an hour and rinse well. 
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in such a manner the tooth that was moving is thus confirmed, and the softened gums are restrained, and the moisture corrupted dries.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When toothache comes from cold, where there is cold or dampness, and the cures of medicine are not helpful, then there is need for cautery according to two ways: 
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and cautery of butter and cautery of fire.  
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cauterization of butter is such that you take butter of calf fat, and the end in a spoonful of iron or steel; 
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	after take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a tent, and moisten it in melted butter, and place it on the aching tooth gently and hold until it is cooled; 
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and thus do often until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see so moistened wool and cotton in butter cold, and place it on the aching tooth, and put on top the hot iron until the fire comes to the end of the tooth. 
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The cautery assembled with fire is such that you prick a piece of iron or steel, and it should be large so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the sick person. 
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After heating the cautery, because its shape will come later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools. 
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, because the pain will be removed that day or the next.  
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in the heat of this cautery, and then raise it forcefully. 
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery of whatever shape you want, and according to what you are able.  
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the shape of the iron:
des scrophules	Of the scrofulous ulcers
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrophules are of phlegm and cold moisture, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then cauterize the head with fire as it comes after this form, and let it have openings for the fumes to issue from the cautery to the other part. 
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	And put the hot cautery on the abscess once, where it is necessary, until it comes to the bottom of the abscess.  
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	And if the abscess is small, put cauterization according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it so for III days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	And put on moist cotton in butter as long as the burn is removed.  
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	After care the place with ointments and bandages until it is healed. 
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the dog:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When the humors overcome on the channels of the body, and even when this comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be purged first by dissolving medicines;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	After the fire cautery is done at the root of the throat, and you guard that you do not come near the throat, and burn only a little bit. 
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After the fire cautery is done at the junction of the neck to the head of the spine, and be the cautery which is called "clavicle" as we have the form before. 
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure the place as we have said before until it is healed.  
de la toust	of the pain
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all and illnesses of the chest are of cold moisture, and the patient has no fever nor dryness, and is the illness ancient, if it be done. II cauteries on the  forcele in their veins; 
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and the other cautery removes the pain between II nipples; 
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and be the cautery which is called "clavicle" according to the form which is said before. 
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see it, make cautery by pricking the whole cautery which is called "point" because its form is as before in the illness of the ears;  
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And let the points be up to XXX, or wherever it reaches. 
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treatment of the place according to what has been said before, and let the cautery be at III reins according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for this reason, the cauteries are lighter, because you make them three cuts deep.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Afterward, make the patient lie on his back and side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	after lift the kernel which is inside the little one with the two fingers of your left hand; 
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated inside, then remove the cautery which has two nerves in its place as shown here. 
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the kernel until it pierces to the rib, and the figure of the cautery should come together with four cauteries;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this one is made cautery with the cautery which has three nerves, so that the figure of cauterization consists of six cauteries. 
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	And the nerves are according to the fineness of a tent, and it is the form of the cautery which has three nerves:  
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes is adjusted on this nerve for which there are VIII cautery.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After put on the cautery pricked with sail; 
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After make rest the patient, and let not the limbs be moved by long time until it is well fortified.  
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated upward, which rarely happens, then apply a cautery on the thick part of the clavicle or many cauteries in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come colds and much moisture until it is estranged from its complexion, and are multiplied the catarrh to him, and the ways of cures accustomed and he does not profit at all, therefore it is necessary that the patient be treated on his back, and extend his legs and his hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	Of this then after make him three cauteries one below the shoulder blade by the quantity of an ounce, to all the cautery clavicle, and two cauteries outside the two ribs until the figure of the cauteries be at three angles, and have such space between one another that they not be joined together when they will rot;
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	And let the cauteries be so well done that they will reach the two parts of the heart, and let the figure of the cauteries be according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see to cauterize with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form; 
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and he who will have fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and reigning upon the stomach here, in point according to the quantity that you see of incisions; 
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize with all the cautery which is called "point."  
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure of the cure that we have had before, as long as it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When it comes to the liver pain from cold and moisture and great windiness, as long as it is forcibly removed from its natural complexion by superfluities;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is cured of those things that we have said in divisions, and he does not benefit from it at all, if it is necessary that the patient be treated upon his bed; 
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and sign of incisions III cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity upon the liver, defier the hypochondria, there where the  ribs of man come;
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and there must be space between each cautery the size of a finger. 
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cauteries be long along the body, and do not press your hand too hard on all the cautery; 
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and burn only the middle of the kerf, and let the patient lie straight on his feet;
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, then lying down, extend his legs, and raise his arms; 
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form: 
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if you desire it, you may cauterize these cauteries with the scalpel, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and take care that you do not burn the whole kerf, for you would dry out the whole body;
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and that it does not come to boiling, because the kerf is very subtle there, and you know how to see. 
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When it has an abscess on the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: 
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	If it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too strong; 
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	And if it is in the membrane, he feels pain sharply.  
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And then when this treatment fails to heal, it is necessary for the patient to be laid on his head; 
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then apply a poultice to the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar in shape to the sun, because of this it is shaped as follows: 
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize with the cautery until the skin is burned and it reaches the white beneath, until the wound is completely closed. 
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	Afterwards, treat according to the treatment of wounds until it is healed.
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it is not proper that of this cautery use none others than those who have studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have been corrupted no time. 
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore he may boldly work, and everywhere it seems to me better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the cautery of blisters
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one must do to weeping cauteries of roots of aristolochia, and in such manner:  
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a root of aristolochia long, the greatest that you will be able to find, and whether dry, and as thick and long as your fingers. 
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and soak it in oil, and press it into the fire, and cauterize the cautery between the handle and the neck, and II small cauteries a notch going down in the part that is below the beard; 
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and II cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining behind a notch; 
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and I cautery removes the pain, and I other on the stomach, and I between II shoulders, and II as II ribs down from the cautery which is between II shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	And do not press your hand tightly, but rather make it open as if smelling.
