Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And they said that no old man uses a fire cautery resembling a razor, and they heat it and place it between the ribs, until it comes to the abscess. 
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	and jump out the pain, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.   
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of mice with what we have said in the divisions of treatments, and it does not benefit, then there are III ways of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	Of which some manner is that you make III cauteries, or IIII, in lining according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the cautery of the liver that we have said before; 
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	and do not press your hand to all the cautery, and let the patient be lying on his back.
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	and another manner of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has II nerves, as we have shown it in the dislocation of the shoulder; 
et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and lift the heart which is positioned in the mouse, or the cut of the patient comes from the left side, and let the elevation that you lift the heart according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cautery be according to the width of the body. 
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII.	After he puts the two nerves inflamed until the heart is pierced on the other side, and then removes the cautery, and thus there will be four.  
Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	And if you see, cauterize all the cautery to three nerves. 
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has gotten rot for a long time, and this is worth more than the other cures before said.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not good for edema, except for the method called “asclytes.”
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	When you treat it according to the ways that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not benefit at all, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the belly, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the mouse, and two behind the back on the spine, and one in place of the breast; 
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	and let the cautery be close to the space of the heart. 
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	After leave the cautery open for a long time to get pus, and let not the wound of the patient after the cautery.
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	and healing would hasten, and will be together the two intentions with the help of God. 
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	The form of the cautery for the belly is the keyhole that we have before shows; 
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	and that for the back is olive-shaped, according to what it is previously put.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	When the feet are swollen in those who are hydrophic, and are full of yellow-white fluid, it behooves you to cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; 
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	and raise your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deep with it, thus close the opening around the white, and be the cautery according to this form.
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	After make on II legs II cauteries on each leg at the point of the knife. 
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	And let the cautery be long, one below the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg. 
et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse;	And leave the cauteries open lengthwise without curing, that they remain open there;
aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After the curing of the other cures that we have said. 
de la menoison	of the hand
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	When a solution of belly comes from cold and moisture, as long as the virtues retentive and digestive that is in the stomach and in the intestine are depleted, and cannot be cured by means of cures;
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	And you see the patient suffering greatly and of great virtue, so make a great cautery on the stomach according to what has been said here before about the cautery of the stomach, at the circulating cautery;
et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	And four cauteries around the head subtle to all the cautery clavicle subtle, and two cauteries on the hips. 
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the humors abundant and the patient suffering, make cautery on the groin, and I cautery on each flank, and II small cauteries on the stomach near the great one, because the cure is profitable when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	When the hemorrhoids are or foundation, or one or more, and are old and are of large cold and moist humors corrupted, and are cured as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit if you do cauteries:  
III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois;	Three on the spine of the back, this which is all outside under the alar bone point and point in triangular shape, and one cautery under the head two. 
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile;	And if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then the face one makes the great cautery on the stomach, as it has been said before, and the other on the liver, and the other on the mice to all the cautery clavicle;
et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	and let the cautery remain open long time 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure the place until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the cartilage which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;	When you cut the skin, heat the cautery which seems like a razor, and then put it all burning upon that skin cut; 
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;	and let it remain as long as the cautery comes to the origin of the vein, so that the blood stops;  
fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;	do this once or twice, and if there is much skin, cauterize each one as we have said;
aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez;	after the cure of openings beneficial until they are healed;
et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	and if you cauterize with a large cautery on  the skin, it will have more help. 
de plaie mal curee	of wound poorly cared for
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear cutting or opening, which we will recount in its place, there comes such a disease that can be healed only by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When to any comes fistula, and is filled and cast putridity and corrupted moisture, so the should prove at once a fine tent, and guard that you know at once the tent how much it has of width.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;	After heat the cautery which seems like a razor, and put it into the fistula according to the quantity that the thing entered there, and restart the cautery until that flesh and corrupted are burned, once, or twice or three times, according to the quantity of  need.
et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	And guard against damaging the nerves that are within, and the large veins.  
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans;	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestine, guard those parts, and make no incisions except in the fatty tissue, and think that it is not a perforation. 
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	After curing the area until it is healed, and if the lesions are cleansed, and the materials are removed for a long time, then know that the lesion is completely healed.  
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	And if the materials are not removed, know that the lesion is corrupt, and the bone at its base is corrupted. 
et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	And thus as one of these that we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;	When pain from cold comes to the reins, and from great flatulence, and does not take any form (or doesn't come in shape), then it is necessary that you make a cautery on the reins on one side and the other with the cautery clavile that we have said before. 
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	And if we cauterize it in the middle, then there will be three cauteries in a line, and they will be more helpful. 
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce;	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then I make a cautery in the part outside above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic begin, and there on the right and on the left, and each cautery as long as my finger. 
et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing;	and I make the cautery outside on the back, where it is needed. 
et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	And let the cauteries be made according to the form previously mentioned. 
de la marris	of the wound
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde;	When the uterus is cold and moist, and does not allow conception for this reason, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends lag behind;
et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:	and when they come, there is great pain. 
adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos;	Therefore it behooves one to make three cauteries around the head, as we have said, or cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries outside the back; 
et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	And let the cauteries be clavicle-like, as we have said.  
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;	When the viscous moisture descends to the hip joint, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together.  
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;	And it is found that the place of the viscous department is viscid, so it behooves you to cauterize the patient on the hip joint with a cautery resembling a circle, and mark before the place around the joint as it turns, so that the joint is within the circle. 
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	And let the cauteries be like those with which the stomach was cauterized.  
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;	And if this cautery is not present to you, make three cauteries of large olive wood, and let the cautery be as deep as all the others. 
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure until it is healed.  
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	When pain comes in the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division and the cure does not work, and the illness is old:  
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	then it behooves you to purge the patient of the thick humors with fetid pills, or other pills that resemble good things.  
Aprés li fai cautere;	After this, make a cautery; 
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	and the manner of the cautery is according to two manners:  
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	that is to say, together burning medicines, and fire cautery. 
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	Fire cautery is done in many ways, some of which are as follows: 
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	that you cauterize on the hip bone III triangular cauteries according to this form, and make a good depth and large, and there be between each cautery of space the size of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive;  
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on the top of the hip bone, for which there are IV according to this form: 
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	And if you see, cauterize with the cautery of the circle that we have said before in the dislocation of the hip. 
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	but make in such manner that the circle contains the whole hip, and all the spaces of the marrow be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the manner in which it is done for sciatica, when the pain holds in the hip and does not reach to the thigh nor to the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	And if it comes up to the thigh and leg, then you make II cauteries where the patient says that pain holds him, and one cautery above the ankle IV fingers, on the left side a little;
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	And let the cautery curette be, and let it burn the thickness of the heart.  
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if the patient feels that the pain extends to the two feet or near it, cauterize there where he feels the pain three points or four with the cautery which is called “points.” 
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	And if it is necessary, if you do more. 
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then make cauterization with the curette or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave so much of the cautery that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more nuisance and contraction. 
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who had cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they left them so that the leg was entirely swollen, and the foot also, and it was pierced and corrupted throughout the foot.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a solution of belly from which he had death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cautery in one and in the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	And the sage say in the cautery of the hip, for this is how it should be done, make a iron such as and as large as a thimble, or a little less, and either from the interspaces and either between interspaces up to the other with spacing the quantity of a knuckle;
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	and let the instruments be over to part, and let them also be like nuts, and there be the iron hand well made; 
et c’est li forme:	And this is the form: 
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	And be heated until it is all red and gives off heat, and then put it on the bone of the ill hip, and be turned over the sound side;  
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	and cauterize once the cautery is red and let it for three days;
et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens;	and then make a plaster of butter, and let the wound be covered long time; 
aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of ointment until it is healed.  
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its harm, and it is seen little who uses it; 
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	and nevertheless these are good cauteries, which the one who can suffer it and where it is needed.  
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	The cauteries of medicine burning is that you make the instrument in between chatterers in which descends the edge of the door, and be of iron or of a length to one side, and in the height have two, and between each the quantity of the thickness of a coin.  
et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	And be open downwards and upwards, and they join together according to this form: 
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	After put on the bone of the hip on the patient lying on his side healthy, and after your hand very high on the bone of the hip. 
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After throw between the two circles of the hot awl which is heated to the fire the spot, and let him one hour ten, and suffers the patient the heat and the burn of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	For there it finds medication also as of fire; 
et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit;	And when the medication is passed, lift your hand with the instrument and lift the hip of soft awl, and leave thus three days, and put on butter as long as that which is black of the burn is taken away. 
et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait;	and leave it for three days so that it may rot; 
et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	and this would be the last aid after the cure of dressings as long as it is healthy.  
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or to the leg, then do you make an instrument that is held as according to what you have done in the hip augmentation; 
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	and this is the manner of the hot awl, and I have written it or treated of the rectification of medicine.  
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	where there is a small opening that the point of a razor can enter into;
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	and place one pot above the other well sealed, and put alkali and charcoal and sweet awl above, until there is the right amount of powders on top as you have well grasped it in your hand.
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	and let him so until it descends down its fever and excrement or as much as it can fall, then take all that  sickness and place it on hot embers and on alkali as before. 
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And then if will be much fever and is administered in the form of works of medicine and cauteries of other members. 
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	Because it does the work like fire, and if to other medicines with which one cauterizes well the hip thus as turpentine and honey of cashew nuts and hot embers with soap, all these things mixed together. 
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Gaius tells us about a cure of which one man was cured of the pain in the hip and sciatica vein, and he spoke well, and said that no other cure was made, and that he was healed at once when this cure was done, and he bathed as he teaches afterwards.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And say in this manner that you take the green fresh and dry litharge, and grind it very well with a little fat, and put it on the hip and on the thigh and on the leg where the pain holds, and bind it; 
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	and let it for three hours and by the quantity that the patient does not feel anymore the burn.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter into a bath until the body is a little bit aroused, and put him in his bed, and the pain will go away entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use cauteries of such medicines, unless after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with fire of sheep, it helps a lot; 
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and it must be done the cautery in this manner. 
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take a linen cloth and wet it with old oil, and put it on the socket which is between the thumb and the foot, and the other called fossa.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	After take sheep's wool, and grip it in fire until it is charcoal, and lay it on the vein, and let it for as long as it is steaming; 
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	and repeat thus, and do not cease to do thus until you think by sense that it comes up to the hip, and that the pain is ceased. 
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	and this manner of cautery is called "cauterization of sheep".  
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or percussion or by too much evacuation, or by similar matter spread cold, none of these appearances is worth cautery, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	It is necessary after that the patient is emptied of fetid pills or other similar things, that one make upon his back, where the pain holds, three lines marked with ink, and in each line V cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure;
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	and let the cautery be made according to the cautery called "point"; 
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	and if you see it, make three or four cauteries on the middle clavicle cautery according to this form:  
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	Many times this illness comes to little children, and the signs of the beginning are that they have tight throats when they lie down, and fear; 
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes above the other spines.  
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see these and you want to treat them, cauterize it with the cautery of this one according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery pricks each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see it, so cauterize around the spine with a cautery that stings two or three lines, and let the points be near each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After curing the wound as long as it is healed according to what we have said, and guard that you do not administer cautery in a place that is in the space of nerves.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When pains of joints are from moistures that are spread to each limb of the body, and when pain comes in feet, which the people call "gout" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and cures of medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in such manner: 
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	make the most cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form: 
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you take hold upon the face of the foot, then do cauterize to the whole cautery as one claims "point."
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains come to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then make cautery on each knee three cauteries or four of each part, with all the olive cautery. 
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you need more, make more, but do not hold your hand there beyond when the point of the heart is burned. 
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery that we have said in our chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the wrist two lines; 
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	and if any pain remains in the hands, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand;  
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	and if the pains come to the shoulders or as far as the armpits, cauterize each part and give good governance to the patient and proper medicines.  
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good governance and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the thigh
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When a rupture comes in the groin and the bowels descend to the groins and it is new, then when you see to cure it, he must not urinate that day.
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and let him use things that loosen his belly so that the fire descends from his belly.  
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	after the fire sits on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his arm as long as the boils are repaired, and move them to your sides, and place an incision beneath the rupture on the bone of the finger, and every sign that seems like half a circle above the body; 
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then examine the cautery of this form: 
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and it feels soft.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then move the boils to their place.
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and the ministers hold his hand so that they do not return backward; 
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and work well the thighs of the patient, and put beneath him a cushion and a bandage on the thighs, and another on the leg that holds his hands; 
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	then put the cautery on the sign with all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it as long as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, then repeat it again until you come to the bone. 
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	And guard carefully that the boil does not burst when you make the cautery; 
que tu ne le brulasses;	that you do not burn it;  
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	and that through this the patient does not die, or other evils. 
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come close to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And it is necessary that the cautery of children be subtle according to the measure of them, and of big people also great according to their measure; 
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	after three days' care the place of the cautery with butter until the burning is removed;  
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	after the care of other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie for forty days on his back until the wound is well joined;
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	and it is necessary that his nurses be diligent for a long time, so that the boil does not burst when he wants to go to chambers. 
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, if it is administered a good band, and wear it for forty others days;
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	and let him have good rest, that he work little and guard himself from too great repletion of drinking and eating, and from too high braiding; 
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And when he does this teaching so is he whole healed.  
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here after the cure of tailoring in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When wounds come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, then to them you make the cautery of the cautery according to its quantity, and either burns it a third of the heart; 
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	after the cure according to what we have said.  
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and none of the ancients said that it must be cauterized with the cautery at three angles according to this form; 
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first sign the place of the joint and make a line through the width above the rupture, and another below, and hold your hand amidst all the cautery clavicle
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and more mobile.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from a fall or a blow, and this pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine is of no avail, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called «poins», and let the cauterization be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and of its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	if he is healed by the first cautery, it is well;  
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	if those, commence the other cautery upon that one, because their custom is that it must be moved to the member which is near, for which it is necessary that you make the cauteries as long as the patient is healed.   
de meselerie	of mashery
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The wounds are aided at times by cautery with great help, and even the illness that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	When you see the cautery being used, take heed if the patient is at the beginning and if she has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and neither sends nor remains, and you doubt that corruption will spread throughout the sick person, then make V cauteries on their head.  
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	And one at the crown, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hairs; 
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	and II on the II horns, and I behind on the heater. 
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	and I keep your hand so that the cautery comes as close as to the bone, and until the bark comes out so that the vapors of the gross humors may escape. 
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	and cauterize on the mouse according to what it is in front.  
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the swelling is everywhere spread;
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and if it manifests clearly, then it is necessary that you cauterize it with these cauteries that we have said or chief, and I cautery on the top of the neck, and II cautery on the spine of the neck, and VI cauteres on the spine of the back, and I great on the crupie and I other below, and II on the II shoulders;
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and II on the cuts, and II on the tendons of the leg, and I on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; 
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and guard the nerves that are on the last bone of the foot so that you do not burn them. 
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and sometimes a cautery is made on the bone of the finger, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver. 
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And know that when more cauteries are made, the more help is done, and the more it benefits.  
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the patient feels no pain from the cautery as a healthy person does, because the body is already totally corrupted. 
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauteries be great and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After care the place with flour of eggs with honey and other cures until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When a swelling comes in any limb and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then I make cauteries on the limb according to the size and smallness of the limb.  
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	and let the cautery be a little bit deep in the thickness of the flesh.   
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the care of dressings until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And at times one makes cautery by hand and foot and back, at the end of the nerve that numbs the limb, and thus is removed the inflammation. 
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And nonetheless no one should interfere with it unless he is knowledgeable of the members and the exits of the nerves moving the body. 
de albaras	of  bars
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the illness called "albaras" is severe, and the engine of medicine is of no avail, then cauterize with a cautery a point thoroughly, according to the quantity of the species of the heart, until the blanchour is removed, and its color changes. 
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	Then the cure of flour of chickpeas and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood from colon and blood from alondre, of each one part; 
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be well all together, and be bound with a cloth, and be aired to the place as long as it is sound. 
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of the sore by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a sore comes at the beginning, and you see it arrested, then cauterize it with the cautery which seems like a circle, all around the border of the sore.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And nonetheless the wise say that one should also make cautery in the middle of the ulcer;  
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	And nonetheless those do not seem to me good, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never wanted it to happen any time; 
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	and more straightforward is that it be cauterized outside, with the cautery which is called 'circle', as we have said in much of cauteries. 
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot be moved
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When someone has a malady called 'adubelati', and it lingers in dying or because of the superfluity that it makes or because of the water of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and has little blood, or because of the heat; 
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you see it haste to die: 
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	therefore cauterize it around with many small cauteries, by pricking; 
aprés le laisse ensi.	afterwards let it be thus.  
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced through the whole cautery, so heat the cautery of this which is the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of the sickness which is called “adubelati” until the cautery has pierced the heart, and be such the cautery that the patient feels it burning in such a manner that the course of the rot be lessened.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of illness there is called "corroding," and it is nothing else than a corruption of the limb, for it consumes the limbs like fire consumes dry vines.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this illness in a place that can suffer cautery altogether with fire, then heat the cauteries, small and large, according to what is fitting for the place where the illness is;
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	After the cautery of all parts as long as you eradicate all corruption, and there remains nothing of it, that all that is corrupt be removed. 
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for III days, and put on the cauterized places softened crushed with oil until the scabs of fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of ingrowing flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if you see after 3 days that hairs do not grow back, it is good.  
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	and if they do not, restart the cautery on those that remain corrupted. 
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this manner has sometimes been cured with sharp medicines instead of fire cautery.  
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	But nonetheless, the fire cautery is more helpful, and I have already said the cure of sharp medicine in the section. 
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Take it when you need it.  
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the splints which come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that by fire a sickness is born which is called “closed” according to our understanding, and it is a great thing that hinders the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know fire cautery, and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	Fire cautery is that you heat the iron rod as if it were a reed of lead, and it is made from good iron to the extent that it can point at every angle, and that there are subtle edges.
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	Afterwards, put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand around the nail as long as it reaches the end of the nail.
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	and let him leave it so for three days until it begins to fester. 
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	then make a poultice of wild mallow ground with oil, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots. 
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the place with ointment, hindering flesh until it is healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are converted by fire the body, and often happen in hands and feet, then you must bring them a cautery of hot water;
et est en teil maniere:	and it is in this manner:  
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	Take a piece of iron or steel, or the tip of a needle, and place it on the nail and the other things, that is to say warts. 
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	And place the piece on so that it wraps around the whole thing, then put a drop of hot oil on it, and hold your hand well and press down with turning so that the edge of the piece comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot oil going deep to the root.
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	And the patient endures a bit of the hot water sting for an hour. 
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	Then let him be, and it will loosen from all its roots.  
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another, until you have reached all those that are on the body, then cure the sores that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The cure of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When some tremble from cold, or from quartan fever or another, then it is necessary for you to make four cauteries or four on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine. 
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and one cautery or weight, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery.
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	If you let him tremble, and hasten his health from the cold disease. 
des pustules puans	of pus-filled pimples
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	At times, by fire, the body appears with baths, or puss-filled pustules that come from large, corrupted matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	Then it is necessary at first when they appear that one makes cautery on the head of each pustule:
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	A subtle cautery of myrtle wood, so that the point is seized by fire, or from a long aristeologe root, or at the lentil cautery. 
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And sometimes the cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow from them forward, but are broken the superfluities from which they come, and are healed. 
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.  
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Many times there are great discharges of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the outside, or in the incision of the abscess, or in the cauterization of the limb, and similar things.  
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	and it is very grievous thing to prolong. 
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And nonetheless when this happens to anyone, immediately hasten to put your finger index on the wound of the vein, and strain it very much until the bleeding be appeased under your finger, and that no drop comes out anymore. 
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	Then put the olive cautery irons, several small and large, to fire until they are all red. 
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Then grasp it, large or small according to the wound and its location where the artery is visible, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there as long as the blood is restrained.  
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your arm above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, so take hastily another from the cautery which are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the blood is stopped. 
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	And guard that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that another evil does not come upon the patient;
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	And know that when blood runs from the artery, it cannot be well stopped even when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways we have said: 
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by tightly tying a thread, or by medicines placed on top which have the power to stop blood.
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	and it be bound and held firmly.  
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring it to rest by tightening with straps or putting hot things on it, or other similar things, if it does not profit him, not at all.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if this happens to anyone and they have not yet used any present medicine, then he must place his index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and bind it well until it is secured over the wound and over the vein. 
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	and do not move it, but moisten it with cold water frequently until the blood is congealed and thickened and secured. 
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	and make inquiries beforehand about those who need cautery and medicine.   
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the care of stones.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have told you in the first chapter about every illness where it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicines, and the incisions and causes and instruments and forms of the cauteries.
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	and I have set this chapter of them up to the foot, and in this chapter I will go by the same way for those who are found more easily those who desire it.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin these things, it is necessary, dear reader, that you learn that in this chapter there is more peril and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for this reason greater caution is needed.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things. 
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	where there is doubt and fear, and many die.  
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come to cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	There come those who are so afflicted with their illness that they die easily due to the ignorance they find in their disease, and the greatness of their wickedness. 
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	and from these one should have fear. 
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And among these there are some who give you their meaning, and say:  
«atendez, je sui garis»;	Wait, I am healed"; 
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the illness is deceitful. 
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	It is not right that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more trust in your honor than in your greed, and do not open yourself fully but wisely to those whom you are certain of, and whom you can have trust and profit from.  
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	And use divination and indication in the treatments of your patients so that health may be converted.  
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And this will help you to acquire a good reputation, and glory, and long memory. 
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Three dear friends, our Lords give you good understanding and straightness, and if you will desire to be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered you this chapter by chapters, according to what it is before, the chapter of cauteries, that I have devised from the head down to the feet, so that you may find them more easily those which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	Know that this sickness comes many times to children at birth, and when the midwife pulls too hard on the head of the child.  
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	And sometimes it comes from a reason that is unknown. 
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I have never seen this sickness outside of children, and in all those that I have seen it hastened death. 
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And for this reason it seems to me that it is better to leave the work of these treatments.  
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw a child whose head was full of water and it grew each day until he could not bear it.
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and believed so much the moisture that he was dead, and this moisture is assembled under the bone on the scapula, between the heart and the bone. 
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and this work is such if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make in the middle a wide split.  
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and let it also be as long as two of us, as long as the moisture flows.   
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and see here the form of the spatula.  
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more abundant, and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see the corners of the head open on each side, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand inside, and it doesn't return to you:
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	then it is necessary that you make in the middle three splits according to this manner. 
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision extract the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	After strain the fissures of cloths and powders, and put wine and oil on it, and leave so until the fifth day; 
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	then unbind it, and treat the wound with coverings and ointments, and leave the main dressing to be strained, and then feed the patient dry meat of little moisture until the limb is fortified and healed. 
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another way of incision is that you look where opens the size of the abscess, and its assembly of liquid; 
car aucune fois est elle devant;	for never once is it in front;
aucune fois derrier;	never once behind;
aucune fois en destre;	never once on the right; 
et aucune fois en senestre.	and never once on the left.  
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Therefore, cut where the abscess opens, and its filling of liquid, and make it according to what you have power to do.
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and guard that you do not cut the artery;  
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and vein blood flowing, so that the patient dies from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture. 
de reume	of rheumatism
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens to someone a disease which is called «catarrh» in the eyes or in the chest, and the illness is old, and the cure of medicine does not help at all, then the last cure is cauterization with this one which covers the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	Therefore, when you see it necessary to cut them, that the patient makes his head go back;  
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	after rub their place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then stretch the patient's neck to the whole cloth;   
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	then look where the vein beats, and its location on one and the other is after the ears, and so are put back;
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	then mark the locations with a pencil, then cut both of them with a sharp spatula from the side, until the tail vein comes to the bone, and this is through the width of the head.  
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, put the spatula under the artery and the cup above, cutting as I do across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood leaps out from above continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery does not appear at the touch, then it is necessary that you measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then mark with a pencil and make until the bone;   
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	And as for the blood to be let out, it is six inches, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the fullness of the artery. 
puis regarde la plaie:	then look at the wound:  
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If it remains on the bone without suppuration, then cover the wound with a poultice so that no abscess comes, then restrain the wound and bind it, and cure it with ointment until it is healed.  
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When migraine old comes, and acute catarrh, because of the moistors of tears and the heats in the temples and ancient forehead and similar things, and it is medicated by means of cures of medicine and all that does not benefit him, if we drain the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the manner of their extraction is that the patient lays back the hairs of his temples, and attends to the artery which opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and is little deeper than in some men who are too cold; 
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	and if it is deeper, then strain the patient's neck with some cloths, then rub the place with some rough cloth, and raise the place with hot water until the artery appears manifestly.  
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Then take the spatula of which this is the form: 
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	Then scrape the skin lightly until you come to the artery, then treat it on top with pincers, and well depart from the webs that are under each part; 
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	And if the artery is subtle, turn it with the point of the uncine, then cut it from that part according to the quantity of the two shoulders. 
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it does not jump out all of itself at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And treat with blood of the VI c, up to III; 
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	And if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in II lengths of a strong double thread of silk so that corruption does not come before the healing of the wound, and blood flow occurs.
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	Then cut the superfluity which is between the II liens in that same hour, and then, if you see fit, so do cauterize with the cuticular cautery up to the bone as long as the shoulders are cut; 
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	and this is the best work if the patient doesn't have a fever and is of hot constitution. 
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For the cautery helps to finish the moisture:  
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	for that reason it is of more great help against moistures. 
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fill their place with old cotton and put a tight bandage over it well made;
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and when they are untied, so be cured with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow and with bandages until it is healed;
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	and if you lack the artery cord as much as you work on it, then hasten to cover with cautery, or you employ the place of vitriol and the strain to your hand that the blood be stained. 
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	and if you lack those presently, then put upon the place your finger until the blood be coagulated, and raise the place of cold water as long as the blood ceases, and be strained as it is proper; 
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	and that which is quicker and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting from two parts, but the cuts be well thickened to keep longer their heat. 
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments is too hard, it holds less its heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And must have between the two knives one finger of thick spacing, and then when you have singed the two places, and you put the red hot iron upon it as long as it comes just to the bone, and cut the vein in two places;
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	and let them be spaced apart between the two shoulders because it is not entirely welded by this cautery at all. 
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:  
des larmes	of tears
