Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes are flowing down the veins that are on the side of the head above, and no cure from medicine helps, and you see the face of the patient being rolled up, and feels or forehead walking as if from tremors; 
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and where they are wet and moist so that the hair of the eyelids falls out, and the eyelids are inflamed, and scorched by the heat of the tears, so there is a need for this cure.  
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And the ancients called it "contused cure," and that you do in reverse to the patient who has this illness.  The hairs that he has on his forehead, then make III cuts on his forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; 
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	And let one of the incisions be also as II should all remove the forehead in swallowing down until the eyebrow, and the others II as II ribs above the papers, and you guard the incision of the arteries that are as II ribs above the papers; 
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	And keep your hand from the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of III should across the joined; 
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths to wipe the blood, then put the spatula sharp from II parts of which is the shape: 
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	From the incision that is over the temple until the second incision; 
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	And scrape all the marrow that is between the two incisions to all the tissue that is on the bone, then make another part from the middle incision until the other second, and then extract this spatula. 
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put in the first incision the instrument which is called “cultellaire”, and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side it is blunt, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the rib cutting towards the flesh near the heart, and the rib edge towards the bone, and the point until it comes to the middle fissure.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head toward the eyes as long as the incision is continuous to where it opens to the heart, and then on the other side make in the middle fissure to the other end. 
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	And then extract the blood evenly, and express its quantity for the taken blood.  
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	Then put in each fissure a tent of old cotton, and put above cloths moistened in wine and oil and honey, and guard that an abscess does not come there.  
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And on the third day untie the ligature, and then administer a strong potion of boiled water, then the cure of oil of basil with rose oil, and other cures that one uses for wounds, until it is healed. 
dou reume des eulz	Of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When to any vein comes acute catarrh by custom, and you see the eyes dimmed and small, and weakening the sight, and the whites burned;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hairs fall out, and where it pierces causes sharp pain, and the patient sneezes.  
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	Therefore, you know from these accidents that these materials and this cautery come only from many veins, and the cured wound that is there, such is this one.  
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to retract his forehead, then make a wide cut between the eyebrows, and another one at the width of I eye.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And beginning from the split of the left temple to the right temple, and be the incision up to the bone; 
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move at the eating. 
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then carefully between the two lips of the split put old cotton, and bandages of linen;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then bind above with cloths moistened in wine and oil, and keep yourself from a hot abscess; 
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is removed, it is proper that you rub the bone until skin begins to grow, then treat it with drying things that cause skin to grow back.  
En teil maniere:	In such manner: 
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice. 
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	And administer it on these wounds to prevent the flesh from rotting. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	Everything that falls into ears is one of four things:  
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or grains, or beast, or piece of stone or similar thing like iron; 
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	Or seeds such as peas, beans, lentils;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Or flowing things like water and honey and similar things. 
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear stone or another thing that does not join with the ear, nor grows in the ear, put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, instill a drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	And make them sneeze with a condiment, and plug their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and is the ear upwards. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Much of the time comes force by this cure;  
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come force, then he administer extraction as pinches subtle, from which is the form: 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it jumps force with the pinches, it is good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not those, then administer extraction to the  bone subtle of small fold; 
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not jump by those, then make a caine of iron and put the head of the caine or hole in the ear strongly, and stop those who are around the caine with soft wax so that the veins cannot enter with the caine;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then the treatment must be strong because many times it comes as we have said.  
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come strong in this manner, then take glue of that which takes the birds, and put it into some instrument which is sharp for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton around it; 
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	then press the glue onto the stone or whatever thing it may be, and treat strongly.  
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if she does not follow all these things that we have said, then hasten to open the ear in such a way that an abscess boils there, and spasms; 
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	And the manner of opening it is that you first make the patient healthy from the head, and extract blood according to the measure of his virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small opening at the root of the ear in the fat where they depend; 
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	And let the opening be like a crescent moon, as far as you come to the stone, then break it according to your strength, and suck it diligently with your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And care for it until it is healed. 
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is grains that are inside and it swells, then administer an extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it cannot issue, then administer a spatula thin according to this form: 
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision in that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think the grain is wet due to moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it. 
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	Then extract it with subtle pincers and a suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned. 
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water therefore that falls into the ear, it is appropriate for the patient to use a first external dressing, and widen the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it has leaped forth by means of this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If this is not the case, then take many grains according to the length of your finger, thin and light, and cauterize them a little with fire; 
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and put them in the patient's ear where it is perforated, and let it come out on its side, and fire another grain on top of the grain which is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not cease to do this with grains upon grains until the water comes out entirely, and thus it will all come out entirely;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	And if you see, then take some reed and put one end in the ear, and hold the other end in fire until the reed burns down to a point;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then do again another part of other joints until the water is all out, as we have said in the stone.  
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of the beast, if it is small-bodied, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division. 
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is large-bodied and one can feel it, then administer extraction of pincers.  
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and this is the thing easiest to remove that is in the ear. 
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and where we treat distillations, and the treatment is not helpful, then it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sun: 
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	if there appear no worms, then treat them with subtle pincers, and if they do not appear, then take the instrument of which this is the form: 
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And put the most subtle chief in the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then succeed gently throughout the chain. 
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Do this often until all the worms come out.  
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to come out, then stop plugging the chain with cotton as I said in the stone; 
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not come out forcefully as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the excision of worms, and you will find them or treat with distillations; 
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and if you distill your oils and your medicines in the ear to all this instrument, of which this is the form as you see;  
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And let it be of silver or of arain [perhaps 'iron'] three parts under the small hole, and above over to distill; 
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press within the distillation the instrument of iron well made for this purpose, and if you see take the razor and wrap around the point conveniently cotton; 
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then throw in your oil or your juice, and that which you see of your medicines in the channel, and the channel be in the ear; 
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then put within the razor all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil be distilled or the end of the ear;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and he feels it within the patient, and let the distillations I a little be heated by fire then one puts them in the ear. 
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and keep that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.  
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born without a hole in their ears; 
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and this same thing happens to men because of a wound or  flesh growing inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes come from within the ear, if one cannot see it. 
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and sometimes one can see the hole clearly,
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	Those that come from within and cannot be seen, are of great healing in more situations, and for this reason you should put the ear of the patient to the sun. 
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	If you see the hair growing back, if the work has all this spatula of this form: 
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And be both sharp and deep in front and behind, so that it does not cut the ear;  
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	If the hair growth is from flesh or cartilage of the ear, if then hold it with subtle pincers, and cut it lightly, until that flesh be all removed. 
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the ulceration is in the ear, take a fine light razor and warm it a little at the fire, then put it in the flesh of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the hair growth where the patient feels great pain in the ear, pierce lightly, and keep that you do not strike the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	Then put into the ear a tent according to the width of the opening, and moisten it in Egyptian ointment.  
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this for no day until the wound be healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder upon pounded vitriol;  
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	And if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you draw out the tent and move another moist tent in cerote which should be made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed. 
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it until it is healed.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the bleeding which are or treatments of distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the sheet of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This athlet that comes in papers of the eyes when they are moist and are dry, then it is necessary that you extend them with forceps and pincers, and the cope of a spatula from its roots.  
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then put on their place powdered vitriol. 
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if without it decorticate, then cauterize with the subtle lentil cautery, and the cauterizer after the incision should move. 
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and many times they return, since nothing remains of their roots.   
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And when they are cauterized by fire, then those roots are burned and do not return at all. 
de la gresle	of the groin
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times come in papers the eyes some things that seem brittle in its shape and in its hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "Hail," and it is an assembly of moisture large in the paper above and below;  
li ovraiges est telz:	The works are such: 
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	Take heed if the hail moves on one side and the other, and it is a light thing to know.
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Do then the wide, then the eschar of each part lightly, then take it with tweezers, and cut it. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot cover it without feeling a little the paper, so it does not harm the patient.
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	And if the fissure is large, assemble it with a suture, and cure it until it is healed. 
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	And if it is small, do not make any force, for the ointment restores it soon and prevents flesh.  
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the stone is descending into the ear towards the upper part, then turn the paper over, and hold the stone with pliers, and press it from both sides. 
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	And if the paper is pulled away by the incision, it does not matter.  
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And when the stone is cut, leave the eye of salt water, and cure the place of those who cause flesh until the patient is healed. 
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a grease that is generated in the tissues of the paper above, and this happens more to children than anyone else, and it hurts their eyes, and they get cataracts in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears rush into their eyes; 
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	And because of this, they lie on their faces down, and sleep on it, and are their papers below their eyebrows moist that the swelling and appearance have covered with exinach which appears in the eye. 
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your thumbs and feel the excoriation between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head on your healthy; 
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then takes the linen sheet, and prepares a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains each side, then puts it on him;  
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and presses with his two hands from one side and another, so that the sides are assembled within the circle; 
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then makes in the middle of the moisture with the sharp spatula a slit of wide size, and not be more than the wound one makes on the vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and make the skin in part as far as you come to the sides; 
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And in more places comes the opening from the slit, according to the form of a piece of white fat.  
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Extract then with a whole piece of cloth between your two hands at the outside, and turn your hand to right and left as long as it is spread; 
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and guard that you do not add to the split, that you do not come to all the spatula until the eye, that you do not blind it. 
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the exit does not open at the beginning of the split, so carefully widen the split slightly until it opens.  
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then extract it as we have said, then moisten drapes in hot and cold water, and put it on its place, and restrain with bandages. 
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if to such men who grind grain and put it on top to corrupt that moisture which is lodged.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the place hot, so its cure with plasters soothing until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When hairs are attached to the eyes other than natural ones and are enflamed, they harm the eyes and bring about various illnesses such as habitual tearing and softening of the eyelids and clouding, as much as it is a cause for the destruction of the eyes; 
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and its treatment follows FOUR ways: 
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	either by cauterization with fire together, or by sharp medicine according to that which is before or the chapter of cauterization, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by forceps, according to what I will say. 
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient on your healthy side, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand.  
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If it is converted, it is good; 
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, then put a needle through all the thread above;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and be it next to the edge of the paper or where the hair grows near these hairs, and pull the thread upwards all over the paper, and turn it back to the razor; 
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	Then make in the part below the paper, below the hairs adjusted, all over the spatula cutting, from the large tear to the small one;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	Then pull the thread out, and put below the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth, then place on top of the paper a figure of an arch, like the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see raise the paper which is divided into all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if it needs, one cuts a large quantity of the paper according to what the paper is softened; 
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	Then make on all the spatula above the two lines which you have marked, and begin from the large tear until small.  
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	And let one of the incisions be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the needle in one of the two corners of the heart, and then scrape it completely.  
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	Then assemble the two lips with a suture of a needle with all the finest wool thread, and wipe the blood, and make air the superfluity of the hairs on the two eyebrows to nothing sticky, if you see to do this.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	And if this is not, if you have no care for it, then leave the suture and the hairs until three or four days.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	Then cure the wound without suture with drying and constricting things, because the paper revives at the bottom of the wound and the assembly of it, but the suture is moved (as they say the ancients), and this work without fear. 
et si a une autre maniere:	and if in another way 
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and that you mark the paper with a figure which is as the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, at III ounces wide according to the form which is here.  
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cover what goes over the small forces equally according to the form which is here.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you cannot hold the pliers, and the thing is not equal, take a needle which has thread, and put it into the middle of the figure; 
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and put the other thread near the larger tear, and the second thread near the smaller one, and assemble between your two threads evenly. 
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have marked it, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and treat it until it is healed;  
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointment. 
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	And sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper are converted: 
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	If it is necessary that you use those things that we have said about incision;  
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	But the stitching in one and the other is more artificial. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The cure of bites is according to this form:  
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	And it is that you would convert the paper and the send inside according to those that I have said, and then make II bites by art, and II subtle ties as long as the paper and the width of the spatula is; 
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	And cut as II heads from II parts where you hold the threads;  
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	Then assemble one and the other subtly above those that rise from the paper of the eye, and restrain the II bites from the II parts forming;  
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	And let it so for some days, and the skin which is restrained will die and shrink and pull, as long as it dries by itself. 
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If he delays, if he strikes with force, then treat him until he is healed; 
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is healed, and if the paper has been lifted, and they can no longer prick the hairs; 
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	And this is the form of the two legs that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide. 
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The works are such that you prick a fine needle, and it puts in the silk thread soft and fine; 
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then assemble the shoulders and knot one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; 
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then order in the chase the other silk thread finely, and knot the ends of the thread;  
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	then put the patient's head on your palm; 
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and be in the sun so that the work is clarified, for it is a subtle and fine work, then put the needle to all the chase in the root of the hair joined, and make it pierce into the paper gently until you draw it above the natural hair; 
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	Then extract the hair up to the chase, and put into the chase that hair, if there are one or two or three or more. 
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Then withdraw your hand so that the hairs come out of all the chase onto the paper with the natural hair.  
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then you shall thrust the chase downward to all the thread that you have ordered it, until the chase comes out through the opening above and you see it by the sight of your eye. 
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then you shall draw the chase and the thread, and close your eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair hardens in its place and the flesh grows above it.  
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hairs are small, then accompany one long hair from the natural chevelure, and either raise it with that or leave it, until it is lengthened and then lift it. 
de la porriture de l’oil	of the corruption of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this illness which is called "aleocrati" or rot comes to the eye, there are two ways. 
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and the other unnatural.  
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by suddenness of wound, or incision or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the manner of treating it is that you cut that suture and separate the lips of it, and put inside linen tents, and tie it until it is healed. 
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And it is not fitting that you use in the treatment of it things that dry and restrict.  
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	Because if you do those things, the illness returns worse than the first; 
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but work with softening things, such as fennel; 
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the rose of water or aloe and flaxseed cooked, and melted dragon oil in any oil, and wrap a tent, and treat it with those.  
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasures of your cure is that you take care that it does not weld itself according to the form that it was before; 
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And these works that we have said are nothing but treatments for this illness so that it does not return according to the form that it was before.  
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness which is dislocation is truly called “axacrati,” and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accidents come from wounds and cuts and cauteries and similar things; 
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	And the way of the work in this is that you prick a needle, so that it has a double thread, and you put it into the flesh, and let it pass from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread comes out at both shoulders of the flesh;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Then lift the flesh above the entire needle, and cut it with the spatula wide.  
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what is right, it is good; 
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If it is not so, then take a razor and put it in the split, and turn the paper, and make II slits where it costs inside the paper.  
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	And let the heads of the II slits be at the II angles of the incision that you have cut, and make them so that when they are assembled, that the figure is as the figure of a letter which has no "I greiche";
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	Then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its costs is pulled down, from those which follow the paper, then adjust the II parts severed, and stitch them with a thread of linen;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it with those that we have said about softening medicines, and bandages, until it is healed. 
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the malady comes from a split or a suture or a cautery, then it is necessary that you make a flat slit under the hairs of the papers, and according to what is above; 
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then carefully between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; 
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	And one must perform the work according to the form of the illness, because it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters equip everything of all their power how it makes return the figure to its natural form;  
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And the patient himself, according to what is necessary for work and instruments in many positions. 
dou soudement de la papiere	of the swelling of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this suture happens to men's hands in such a manner that the skin above is joined with the white of the eye, and cannot move or make its natural works, then it is necessary that you put the tip of a razor under the skin, and lift it upwards; 
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	And the extent of the pincers, until you cut what is stuck to the spatula, subtle, which is not too blunt nor too sharp, so that the patient cannot suffer that the spatula too blunt nor pierce the eye; 
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	And let your incision, which you skin that assembly, lightly so that the paper returns according to its natural form; 
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	And is healed all that assembly, and do no times in the eye salt water, and the lift of sweet water, and of collar; 
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	Then put between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on the eye wool moistened in abundance of an egg; 
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	And after the third day use of the collar and things soaked as long as it is healed. 
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the nail is according to II manners:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	It is nervous and resembling the hard syfac, and another which is not at all nervous but resembles white moisture congealed, that when one touches it with iron and one cauterizes it pinches, so cannot one;
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and both of them begin toward the great tear, and cross little by little until it covers all sight and all light and the movement of the eye. 
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand then he opens his eyes; 
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lifts the paper with your hand, then where the angle has pinches of little wrinkles, and it is above. 
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and put in its hair of horse or cow hide, or ox, and the strong thread; 
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a little and put it into the angle, and pierce through with the whole needle, and tie the angle with thread and it is above, and scrape along all the hair the side of the angle which follows the small wrinkle and the silk to the hair until the head, then cut the remaining in the root of the tear throughout the spatula subtle and with small forces, and leave the natural char tear so that by incision does not come the body of tears accustomed. 
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	And sometimes the fingernail comes to the nailbed alone, as we have said. 
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	Then the scraping has all the spatula shaped from this is the form:  
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And keep that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and break it, and that the nail be not pierced; 
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision put in the eye a bit of silk ground, and from the collar made of litharge, and leave it until the next day. 
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure of those that it behoves as long as it is healed.  
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot put the needle, and the nailbeds cannot enter, many times is cured this appearance of a nail of medicines.  
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and they grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, so work the eye of the patient, and take the spatula light bit sharp according to this form. 
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And move the hinge upward subtly, and if you see that it decreases not and the reason hastens, then distill from your mouth into the eye colocynth made of litargire and the red colocynth and seal, and plug the eye until the other day. 
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is completely removed. 
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If no other thing is contrary to you in the eye, such as a boil, then treat it with milk and first cure the boil as well as possible until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh near the eye is harmed by the moisture, then suspend it with the bandage and cut off a part and not half completely, that no tear liquid may come.  
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distill into the eye red collyrium which is made of litharge. 
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the car which is born on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	The eyes of some men are born at times red and cover the white part and hold onto the eyelids, and turn to the outside, and appear like a rose of a balustrade.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	And the work is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then open their eyes, and with all that flesh with bandages suitable to them, and sustain it with force. 
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	Then cut the first flesh, and go all cutting to the end, and take care that you do not wound the eye in the work.
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	And let the incision of the spatula be as we have said in the incision of the angle and the small forces by which one removes the bone, as the form after this chapter demonstrates. 
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	And when the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, then apply oil of silphium ground or distill red coral and similar corrosive medicines, and place on the oil a cloth soaked with beaten egg white, so that it may be assured of a hot abscess. 
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	And if it remains nothing, and the wound still burns, and you doubt a hot abscess, then leave the oil and treat the abscess with things that soothe a hot abscess. 
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Then return to your work as long as it is healed, and thus do until the flesh is joined in the oil by this manner. 
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But nonetheless, it is necessary that you follow the treatment of each weak oil according to natural means.  
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and of the way accident, in work of iron; 
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	And do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member suffers from that work.  
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Those veins are red that are covered above the eye, and they take away from sight their work and weaken the eye all days.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is therefore necessary first that you look at the eye, to see where it is, and if there is nothing else but the pain.  
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	Therefore do it in this manner: 
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Instruct the patient to put his head on your chest, then suspend those veins along the entire spine according to your wisdom, and let the  veins be thin, doubled according to this form: 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two bones be joined by degrees in the body according to this form.
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	Then one should tie those veins tightly and carefully wipe the blood hour after hour, until you see the removal of those veins outside the eye; 
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	And guard that you do not blind the eye with the tips of the spatulas, and do this work at midday in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you only cut those veins.  
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, if distill into the eye collyrium green and red to corrupt what is remaining of the seed.  
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you do not have power to gather all of it in this hour, then make a poultice on the eye of things soothing the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pains are soothed and are assured of a hot abscess, then begin again according to this manner which is before until it is healed; 
et c’est li forme des forces:	and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The mire so named "arissati" fistula: 
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	when you treat it with cautery and medicine burning according to those that I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is a thing in it which you cut on the abscess, where it must die, and treat all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.  
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, then the king has all the tools of what here are the forms. 
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And it is called "rough chief," and it is made of fire iron to the head front, and it is pointed like a file as it is in the present form: 
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little until you know that that corruption is removed; 
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this several times, then restore the place with medicinal excretives.  
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the flesh is soldered, and there is no birth of cartilage, and the body of the bow is soldered, and remains so for 40 days, and it does not renew itself and is not at all an abscess, and a bad accident does not come to it, know that it is healed; 
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If this does not work, if there is no other means than to bring the fistula to the opening of the wound according to this form:  
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and that you uncover the bone a second time with iron and sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take the wood according to this form, and let the head of iron be at III angles, and the staff be thinned to the top as you see here:  
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye slightly, then turn the entire wood until it penetrates the bone and the patient feels it through what comes in this if he holds his hand on his wound;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the place of dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh is born and hardens in its places, then let the matter go into the wound;
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	It is a lighter thing for the patient. 
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are open throughout and all, and they do not come to distort to the nose, nor lessen, then it befits you to bind the patient. 
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	Then the clean, then put suction cups or a vessel without injuring to suck, then put over the eye a poultice made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then restrain the eye, and plasters it with bandages and cloths; 
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	And the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths enough soft, and double each in IV, and then put one over the other according to the quantity that the eye needs; 
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	Then restrain from above with a hard bandage-like thing, and recommence the suction cups to suck without injuring; 
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	Then remove the leeches and let the eye be restrained day and night, and if the ligaments soften, then it is necessary that you restrain it much; 
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	Then remove the ligament after the day and night, and if you see the eye repair, it is good;  
se ce non;	If not; 
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	then begin again the plaster and bandages and the ligament and leeches until it is healed.  
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the dislocation of a web
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When rupture comes in the membrane of the eye, then open it, and come forth papers like as the grain of resin, and is expectable to see. 
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	then if you see it covered, the work is such that you thrust a needle in the root of the lower part until the upper one, then thrust another needle where it has the double thread from the inner part.
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and let it be examined, and leave the first needle according to the disposition 
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then cut its length with the double thread and tie one part of the skin around it, and bind it well, then remove the needle and put on the other eye half in a fold of egg. 
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it until the thread falls with the skin, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed. 
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and at any time the wound is restrained by skin on each side of a circle of cloth, until it is healed. 
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eyes show great appearance, then pierce it with a subtle spatula which comes from the eye, and correct the albuminous moisture and lower the eyelids, and enter them immediately. 
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it until it is healed.  
de la bowe de l’oil	of the ball of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This illness which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but a bow which is assembled in the eye, seeming like water descending, and it is not water.  
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	And the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on an equipped and straight seat, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and move it as much as you see the bow come up to your eyes; 
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	Then so it is fixed, and do not let it descend and be dislodged the light, and the patient sees things as he used to;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	And if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bow is not arranged as we have said. 
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	If you do sit the patient between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and make on the cornea a hole through the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, as much as the bow allows.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when it is out, distill in the hot water mixed with honey, or water or fennel boiled and honey, then be cured of another cure until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	of the eyes
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have taken the appearances of waters in their division, and those that are necessary for inspection;   
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	so in work according to health.  
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you make the sick person sit between your hands crossed, away from the light of the sun, and tie their healthy eye and hold it very tight; 
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then put the paper of the eye on your left hand if their eyes are left, or on your right hand if their eyes are right; 
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand, if their eye is left, the instrument that is called 'almagda', or in your left hand, if their eye is right; 
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	then put the point of the instrument near the crown by the width of a finger in that whiteness of the eye to the part of the lesser tear duct, then push the instrument which is called «almagda» virtuously, and restrain your hand until it pierces into the whiteness of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; 
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is necessary that the measure of the channel almagda be at the forefront of the measure of the space which is from the nipple to the end of the blackness; 
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and that is the crown of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	so you will see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cornea, and then put the instrument up to where the water is, then squeeze it below one way after another. 
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water now descends, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After rest the little bit, and if the water comes back up the second way, put the force with the instrument, and when it is set in and it does not come up, then withdraw almagda lightly by turning your hand here and there;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put back in place a point of seed silk, and leave of those the eye inside. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by means of a poultice or soaked cloth with rose oil and yolk of egg, and bind with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on top a certain crushed thing with an abundance of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter into the eye due to its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, so it is necessary that you prick the instrument which is called "alberit", of this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep into it, but make its location subtle, then put almond as we have said. 
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and at the completion of the work equip the patient with the bed next, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place. 
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and be devoid of all movements, and eat light meats, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be bound according to his disposition until the third day.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	Then the one who is tied up in that same dark house, and he proves his sight, and I make him see some things, and then I put the bandage back on until the seventh day. 
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And it is not necessary that you do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you bandage them because the water rises quickly. 
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	If an abscess comes, that you unbandage the eye before the seventh day, and the address of this who soothes the abscess; 
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	And when it is appeased, then unbandage the eye and put on his face the orilliet to cover for any day, and be again in that dark house.  
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then he comes out of the house a little at a time, and converts himself into his ways;   
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and knows that no disciples should interfere in this case. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they made almagda by perceiving [something], to which water is added, but nevertheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in books of the ancients; 
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and perhaps it's a new thing.  
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the appearances of the forms of almagda, for those who do not know them see it; 
et soient d’arain proprement:	and they are of a certain kind properly:  
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the heads of these same subtlety, and the last one in three angled sharpness.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh around the joint
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	No times are born or made chariots adjusted diversely, for which there are some that seem scorpions with many feet;  
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if there are any of such where it has a chariot incrusted of dusky color, and if to the chariot under of good color.   
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In that one therefore of these chariots which is under-colored, and not incrusted, it is fitting that you make the patient sit between your hands against the sun;   
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	And works his nostrils, and casts the tool to those cars, and the hairs out.  
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Then hold what you can sustain on the subtle sharp spatula of one side, until you know that all the flesh is removed.  
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if anything remains that cannot be held, then open it with all the subtle light instruments so that nothing remains. 
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if without a swelling or abscess,  you saw, so as is convenient;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if it is a malignant abscess, then hasten and cauterize it until the blood is stopped and all the hairs are removed, then cast upon it either oil or wine.   
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the skin works, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy; 
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is new flesh in the bone above, so that the instruments do not come to cut: 
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	therefore it is necessary that you put in it the thread of linen a bit thick, and be soaked with warm hands, and have between each one a space of 1/2 inch or less. 
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the patient's shoulder with the thread in his nape to his power, and pull in gently until it comes through the nap into the mouth; 
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times children do this at school, and it is a light thing to him who wants to do it.  
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	Then hold the head coming from the nap in one hand, and the other head coming from the mouth in the other hand, and feel one after the other with care of those who are or thread. 
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this as much as you know that the new ones have corrupted that flesh, then treat the child, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it straight back to the wound as before.  
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Do this three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of flesh. 
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put on the wound a cake of lead for some days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them. 
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, to which one distills oils and medicines onto the wound:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And let it be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a basin, and conduct it so.
