et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	And if you see it, so make a closed cage, and let the instruments be full to purge the head. 
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And have your hand on the head to hold it when you heat the oil or any liquid.   
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh around the joint
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a disease called "tellus" is born in the head of the newborn, and it grows and becomes very large, so much so that it is a terrible thing to look at.  
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	And for this reason, it is necessary that you cut it at the beginning, and remove all of its bone, then put on top of it the cautery or burning medicine. 
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	And if you delay in cutting it until it is large, then beware that it is hard, of poor color, and of poor sensation.   
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	If you do not touch it with iron because it is an infected abscess, for when one cuts it at any time, there comes great harm to the patient. 
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	And if the abscess is of soft touch, not of a dark color, and you see that one can completely cut it open, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and treat the place with dry and astringent things.  
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and closed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes to one of these worked cartilages, it profits little, because in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is therefore necessary when this happens to anyone, to look if the wound is fresh in all its blood; 
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then adjust the two lips with a suture, and treat it until it is healed. 
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	And if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape all the parts of their core until they bleed, then assemble the two lips with a suture, and restrain them, and powder with dragon's blood powder, and powdered incense;
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put on the powders a piece of strong plaster or other adhering plaster, and let it stay until it falls by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.  
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The manner of stitching is that you assemble the opening: 
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly;  
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or by thread, as I have told you. 
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	In some men, there are hard abscesses within the lips, like poppy seeds, some smaller and some larger;  
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and split them on each side, and take with forceps and cut it in each part;  
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply to the place after the incision of powdered vitriol, until the blood is stopped. 
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it thus, and treat the place with dry things until it is healed.  
de la char des gencives	of the gum
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times on the gums there appears flesh joined, which the ancients call "albulus"; 
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	so it behooves you to support it with tweezers, and cut it at its root, and leave the wound open to bleed.  
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then put on the place powdered vitriol or other astringent and drying powders; 
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if that flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, then cut it a second time and cauterize it. 
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after cauterization;  
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of instruments for cutting. 
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes they are assembled at the root of teeth, within the mouth between the gums, scabs which are ugly and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	And sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green, as long as the corruption comes to the gums, and the teeth are foul-smelling. 
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	So it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his head be in your lap, and hold his teeth or those scabs appearing until nothing remains there. 
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	And thus do of the blackness and of the greenness, and of the yellowness and of the other spots, as long as they are seen. 
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	And if one removes those that are in the first place, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	If not those, then it begins again the second day and the third, until you have pulled out all.  
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	And know that the teeth need diverse forms of instruments to be pulled out, according to what the work shows, because those razors with which one pulls out outer teeth have other forms than those with which one pulls out inner teeth.
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these forms and others be with you prepared. 
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you take out as much pus as you can, because one must not do otherwise. 
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	because it is a very high substance up to the point that we have no excuse to erase.  
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to take milk, it is necessary for you to be certain about the tooth aching.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times despite the pain the patient, and thinks that it is a tooth saint, and makes pus drain from the good tooth; 
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and nonetheless does not depart at all the pain because of this, as long as the bad is remaining, because we have it already seen to do this to their healthy ones;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are well certain of the tooth wanting to be removed, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth on all sides; with a strong spatula to ward the gums from all parts
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then move it with your two hands or forceps subtly at first peck and peck, until it is well loosened, then firmly hold the forceps.  
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the patient's shoulder be in your holy space between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After the tooth is extracted straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take one of these instruments and put it gently inside each side, and move it as you did at first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the tooth is pierced and broken, then it is necessary that you fill it with cloths, where the holes are. 
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you tightly hold it with tongs, that it does not break while being held.  
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary very skillfully to work around the gum to dislodge the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And thus be well warned that you do not break it, and leave a part, and return to the patient by the malice of the root greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And guard that you do not act as the ignorant masters do, who by their haste and boldness break the chariot sometimes and bring nothing of what we have recounted. 
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but bring sometimes by the opening of those great illnesses for the roots that remain there, or for the chariot they break, as we have often seen. 
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is drawn, wash its place with wine or oil and salt.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if bleeding comes, which often happens, apply to the place vitriol ground up. 
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if those do not help, cauterize it.   
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The forms of the instruments, to which we put teeth first, should be with long points and thick handles, that they do not double when you pull the tooth.
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms: 
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let the members be thick so they do not bend when working, and let them be of good iron, well made, and toothed to hold tight.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains in the breast, it is necessary that you put on top a moistened cotton in butter for a day or two, until the wound is healed, then put in pliers called "algefri," so that the shoulder seems like a bird's beak. 
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and be made inside as well as a file and this is the form:  
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tweezers, then it is necessary that you uncover the flesh around the root, and there put the instrument which is called "althali," that is to say a spatula, because this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be thick and big so that it does not break, and if the root jumps through this, it is good. 
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if this one, then help yourself with all your instruments, of which the forms come after this:  
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has II reins, of this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments which are in front in the order of the teeth, and this instrument that seems like great pliers, whose form is here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let this instrument be thick so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not counted. 
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And the most skillful surgeons find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the illness show them, for there are such illnesses where the ancients do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others; and if one breaks a bone or other bones, or it can be broken, then he seeks the instruments that are necessary, as I have told you, and help with gestures, from this is the form: 
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be thick and well-holding to hold the bone so that it does not escape but can hold it and remove it; 
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And then return to their place with medicines suitable to those, and if there is in the bone rot, and it is small, so the key has all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and the form is ugly, and even in virgin women, then it is necessary that you know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot file it or trim it: 
adonques lou raie;	therefore the furrow; 
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is armed with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is here, and it resembles a small beak, and be of sharp iron on top;
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the copy prick and prick in hand days for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be filed, then file with a such as this is form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and also like the file with which one makes needles; 
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and in filing the tooth back and forth in your hands lightly, so that it does not move until it comes to a point; 
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then make it plain at the end with no scraping, and if the tooth is too sharp and it bleeds the tongue, it is necessary to file down the sharpness until it is equal, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt speech.  
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the tooth before loosens, or by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it so that he moves it without pain, and you have treated them with restraining medications, and they are useless;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	If it is necessary to restrain with a gold thread, for the silver threads become green and corrode, but gold never changes.  
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	And let the thread be of medium size, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth. 
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	And if you see the teeth being close together, then take the thread and put it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the chies between the remaining teeth, if there are one or more, until you come sagely to the healthy tooth on the other side.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	Then begin the covering again until the part where you began, and pull your hand subtly and sagely, so that it does not move.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	And let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. 
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the chies of the thread with pliers, and assemble them, and put them between the healthy tooth, and place it so that it does not touch the tongue. 
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	And then let it remain thus tight as long as it can, and if it loosens, or the threads slip, restrain it with another thread.  
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it remains and serves thus its entire term, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two diseased ones, as you see: 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls, it is put back in its place, from fresh to fresh, as we have said.  
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And let no one interfere who is not knowledgeable and skilled, and sometimes the form of a tooth made from the bone of a cow's hoof is made, and it is put in the place where the defect is, and it is restrained as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes this ligament which comes under the tongue or naturally, that is born thus; 
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by an accident of a joined wound;  
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the works are such that you open the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your hand, and lift the tongue; 
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the  nerve of the tongue as long as the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if there is hardness or knotting, and it is from a wound, then put the probe in and cut the nerve on that side; 
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and keep that the cut be not too deep for the artery which is below;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done it, then lift the level of  water and rinse, or with cold water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and every night apply a salve to the patient, so that they may not harden. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if bleeding occurs, put crushed vitriol on the spot. 
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	And if the blood does not stop, cauterize it with the lentil-shaped cautery, which is good for this.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then treat it with other remedies until it is healed 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	And if you see it of fiery color or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, because it is a chancre. 
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	And if it is declining towards whiteness and there is moisture, place the ointment and make it with a fine spatula, and deliver it on both sides.
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	And if the blood does not stop in your work, put crushed vitriol on it until it is cleansed, then return to your work as long as you extract all pus. 
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then lift its place from above and below, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la gorge	Of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes comes from within the throat boils that are called “godath,” and one calls them properly the two almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take care: 
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If they are hard abscesses of small size and dusky colored, do not touch them with iron at all.  
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is large, then do not touch it with iron, nor for the drawing of blood; 
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it be until it is dead, and then you will divide it where it would break by itself;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is of white color round, and the root is subtle, then have an instrument prepared to cut, but first look whether the abscess chills rests and is appeased. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Therefore make the patient sit before the sun, and his shoulders be on your healthy one, and he opens the mouth and the surgeon places the instruments between his hands, and presses the tongue down to all the instrument, from which this is the form;  
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and it be of silver or fine steel as well as a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	And you press the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, if then take the probe and put it into the center, and thrust it upwards as much as you can;  
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and thrust no thing from the fabrics with it, then cover the instrument, from which this is the form, that seems like forces; 
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and nevertheless the head are curved, and one place the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or steel: 
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, use tongs for this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And be sharpened on one side, and on the other side not;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have cauterized one of the almonds, cauterize the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and with hot and sweet water, and if there is a flowing of blood, gargle the patient with hot water, or apple peels cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding is stopped; 
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal it until it is sound; 
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And at no time do other abscesses arise in the throat than the two almonds, so cauterize them thus like the two almonds; 
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman of an abscess that was in her throat, namely the small abscess;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and I had closed the entire throat well, so that the woman could not expire through the passage which was obstructed, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained so for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high raised that it had been driven into two furrows by its two openings.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I therefore took so much, and placed it in one of the incisions, then the thread was pulled out, and a great portion of the gut was drawn.  
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	Then I made another piece in the other opening of the two, and opened the mouth and pressed the tongue. 
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After I placed the incision in these abscesses, and packed a portion, and only a little blood came out. 
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	And thus the woman's throat was cleansed and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting at the abscess for a long time. 
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	And the abscess grew back, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large. 
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	Then I engaged it and cauterized it inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	So it remains without growing; 
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I depart from these parts, and may God do what He will after me.  
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the skin is brought together around the grape, and it is plump and long, then it is called "perpendicular"; 
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is somewhat large and round, then it is called "grape".  
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscess has subsided, and it is thin, then it behooves you to cut it; 
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and the one which is round and gathered together, and is not long.
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	And if it is bloody or of a rusty color or black, then it behooves you to close the incision of it. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril upon the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and its length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument about which we have made mention before;
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then put the awl in the eye, and work it out, and cut with the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds. 
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And you should not cut more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural limit. 
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	For if you cut more, it grieves the voice and speech.  
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of being cut, you should use an instrument to cauterize the senses that cause fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp acute.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient puts his head on your thigh, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said in this chapter of cautery, and applies with very hot water so that it is not too thick nor too light.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And use the tip of this instrument, for that is the form:  
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And have one hair or place the medicine, like the head of a spoon, and put the instrument over all the medicine on the wound;  
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient be lying on his side so that the saliva and muscle tissue from his mouth flows away from the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the neck;  
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand over all the medicine and press onto the wound, the quantity of half an hour, as long as you see it reddened and the irritations of the medicine be appeased;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see it, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton into the channel above, as long as the cotton adheres to the wound; 
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and wait after IV or V days; 
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to restart the cautery of the medicine, then restart it, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with a cotton swab dipped in butter, and purify what is around the medicine. 
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be rinsed with cold water, and be treated with gargles until it is healed.  
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This cure is safer than incision; 
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is treated with fumigation according to this manner, take calamint and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and lavender and similar herbs, and put them all or some of them in a pot, and put oil in it, and let it boil.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well covered with strong earth, and inside the pot have a breathing instrument according to this manner. 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it should be of silver or iron, and one of the ends should be put in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye by the nose, as long as the eye is numbed. 
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	After the wound heals often, as long as the skin is dry, and guard that you do not do this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, for many things happen. 
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And do not do this before except at the decline of the hot abscess. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a dog and put inside its head a wick of wool, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	For the wool does not let the steam heavily bother the mouth, and it is a good cure altogether healthy. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times there are lodged in the throat bones or spines of fish, or any thing
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	So therefore it is necessary that you pull out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see move the thing.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	And that which does not open for you and is placed in the throat, it behoves you to make the patient vomit so that the food may be cooked in the stomach. 
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	But by chance if it gets stuck there through vomiting.  
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of cloth, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread. 
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and to the sponge the thread, and then he swallows it.  
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when she comes to her place, if she dries up, then you will pull forward. 
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	And if she does not come forward from those that we have said, then take the instrument of bronze according to this form. 
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it may more easily enter into the throat, and have the head raised up.
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, that it does not come to life, nor thrust the bone inside. 
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and move so that the patient puts the instrument in, for this reason that he may be moved or the thing is worse.  
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If she pushes down, or he pulls it forward evenly all of the instrument, as long as she is forward. 
de la sansue de la gorge	of the cutting of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	At no time is medicine given to the wound, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	And when this does not help, then look in the throat of the patient to the sun, then that you press his tongue with the instrument that I have told you about.  
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, treat it with all little forceps, or subtle pincers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a dog's hair and put it in the throat of the patient, then put fire at the end of the dog's hair, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient stands of water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then take full of cold water, and open the mouth, and let it enter without swallowing, and move it with your hand often. 
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And as soon as the patient feels the water, he will fall.  
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not fall as we have said, then smoke the patient with asafoetida, to the instrument that I said in the smoking of the grape.  
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for it will fall without struggling. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of the smoking is that you ignite the pot in which there are burning coals, and let it be covered with a perforated cloth in the middle, and in that one insert the head of the instrument.  
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then you place your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not go out, but comes until the throat 
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the throat will now open, and if it does not open, start the fumigation again many times; 
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and let the patient suffer thirst, and chew salty things and others, and do not drink water;  
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it will be necessary that it is healed by this treatment. 
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the throat is, when it can be seen, similar to curved pliers so that they can enter into the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and it has a resemblance to the beak of an eagle, and it has sharpness from lime, so that what it takes, it cannot let go; 
et vez ci la forme:	and see here the form: 
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many resemblances of an abscess are, according to those who remember after here in this book, and differ in perforation and size; 
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two ways one of which is in its resemblance itself, and because of what it holds moisture.  
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the limbs where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess of the head is different from that of the foundation, and the abscess of the fleshy part is different from that which comes in the joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if on abscesses one must not pierce, as long as the boil is ripe according to its fulfillment; 
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are rotten, and do not die according to their fulfillment, like abscesses which are near joints. 
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near the joints, and one lets it be as long as it is rotten, by chance the ligaments and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, by which this is a cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Where the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal limb; 
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or if it is near the foundation, pierce it then as long as it is ripe; 
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not fitting that you pierce an abscess before complete digestion, except that one which is below the base, so that it may not break further, and be lengthened inwards, and a fistula comes.  
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and not be able to heal in a great period. 
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is fitting that you know the time of the perforation of the abscess which is death according to its completion, and this is when the pain has been appeased, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and of the swelling and of the softening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs.
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is fitting that you make the perforation where more dependent the part of the abscess, and where it appears pus. 
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and be the perforation long of the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all their equals where it has no foldings.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that are dislocated, according to the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you leave the puncture open as long as it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce him before these parts, then it will lengthen the body of the venom from him, and it is full of much filth.  
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and perhaps harden the lips and deepen them from him. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess which are perceived according to the breadth of the body, according to what the members have need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you bring in small abscesses, small openings;  
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large openings, and many incisions according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; 
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to burn the core, and cover. 
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	When it has become as a shroud, and is dying, then one should do as with boils:  
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if there are such that are split in three angles, and if there are such which one covers as the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the armpits; 
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are such where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar coverings.  
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who have no head, as superficial abscesses, it is necessary that you pierce them fully; 
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large and has collected much pus, and you pierce it, that you do not drain all the pus in that hour, but drain one part; 
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop up the abscess until the other day, then do not pull anything away from it. 
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this many times in a row, as much as the bowel is whole.  
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	samely if the patient is of feeble virtue, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old man who is decrepit.  
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes bursts forth with the exit of the bowels, which by chance kills the patient, and you are not worried about it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; 
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a flat cut, then administer bandages of linen or old cotton.  
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then it is necessary that you put in each one a bandage so that they come against each other.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	And if you have cut into an abscess a part of the skin and have covered it back over, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or shavings of linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day. 
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound, and its care with ointment as long as it is healing.  
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the flow of blood happens in your work, so administer cold water and ease it, and wet the cloth, and place it on the bleeding spot many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the flow of blood persists, then administer governance and care, and the powders that I have said in this book, and if it is during wintertime, and the place where the abscess or boil is is very sensitive, then it is necessary to put on tents and cloths moistened in wine and hot oil. 
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if it is in summertime, and the place where the abscess or boil is is fleshy, then it is necessary to put on cloths moistened in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said.  
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then unbind the abscess and wipe it and treat it as needed until it is healed.  
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this it behooves to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: 
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	as I have said how one must proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and here see the chapter.  
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where boils on the head come small abscesses, and they are manners of ours that are in cloths, as the joiner of a hinge, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fatty and such ones which have moisture like poultices; 
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if there are those that are hard and stony in shape, and there is no doubt that the artery does not act contrary 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the hip are such that you should consider all instruments which are called "entromissoire," because their form comes here afterwards, what they contain.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, so lift it from above with a long stick.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture has been evacuated, then it is necessary to scrape off without leaving the hair which contains that moisture, for it returns immediately when one leaves it. 
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if this one not, in water and in salt, and then apply to the wound, and leave it until the next day.
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And these correct those that remain of the night.  
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then resume the cotton, as before, the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain of the night. 
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound with ointment as is suitable, until it is healed.  
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds in the fat, so cut according to this form, of the long. 
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	And it throws its dressings, and the skin off from all sides, and puts all its care to drain under the coat where it lies;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the artery does you the opposite, so do those that I told you after. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do so for the abscess if it is purulent, and with cutting and caring as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cutting above the purulent abscess and the moist one is lighter because they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if to any of these abscesses or chiefs where there is no moisture, and of these were the abscesses that I cut or chiefs of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess also like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not be broken.  
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if one had made no incision, it would have been as well done as with a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming or at the head, those which come at the head of children and at the roots of the ears, let the opening be always at the lowest point, so that pus flows out easily.
et les cure si com il covient.	and the cure as it is necessary. 
des scrophules	Of the scrofulous ulcers
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses happen in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes come in other parts or of the body, and are bad, and are joined together with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula is properly within its own coat, like the boil and the abscess of the head, as we have said. 
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the resemblances of these scrofulas are many.  
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some who contain moisture, and there are some who do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	In that one therefore which you see of good disposition to the touch, and resembles the color of the body, and moves from every side and is not hard against the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the vessel, and is not deep. 
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	If it is necessary that you cut it from above, and the peel of each part, and make the two lips of the heart like incisions, if you need them, as we have said in abscesses of the head; 
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and the train poke and poke, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and be neither the spatula thick nor trenchant, that the hand does not escape, and do not see too far ahead, so that you do not cut what you should not. 
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound powdered vitriol, or any powders that restrain blood, and extract the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to heal.  
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the wound is cleansed, return to your work, as long as you complete it. 
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Then if there remain any small pustules at the tip of your finger, cut them and remove them. 
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein at the root of the pustule, it is not advisable that you cut the pustule at its root, but tie it with a strong doubled thread and let it hang down without annoyance.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then apply to the wound old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then the dressing. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut all the scrofula, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then that there is no longer any superfluity for the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and milk the juice, and the count as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofulas that hold superfluity, pierce where it opens more; 
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	And pierce it thus as the one before said, depending [it], then administer compresses with ointment and similar things, so that it rots what remains of the corruption; 
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the wound is well cleaned, then the dressing of ointment preventing flesh, until it is healed.  
de squinance	of dislocation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke of cutting the throat; 
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I have never seen anyone in our land who did it, and it is the scripture of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	To those who have squinancy, it is necessary that the opening of the throat called "epiglottis" be opened;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	And one does not make help by those, for those that all the veins and the pores of the patient are at those who have abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the almonds. 
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the channel of the throat, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid death that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore it is fitting, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three circles or four a small opening through, between the two circles or by the quantity of the opening of the syfac, not in the cartilage. 
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And this is suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no cartilage, and the vessels are long enough from it. 
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, it is fitting that he extend the skin of the throat to all the way, then cut open the kernel as far as it comes to the channel.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And avoid the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the syfac, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the channel which jumps out of its place which is broken, and by the lack of voice. 
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open a piece.  
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour is passed of which one doubts the strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew it all alone without the cartilage. 
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is sound.  
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one should not do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the defect is in the lung.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore cut on the epiglottis for those that the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death. 
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And for this commanded the ancients to let the wound open until the malice of the illness is passed, and it is passed in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew the wound and cure it, until it was cured.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I see. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I see that a young lady took the knife and thrust it into her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe; 
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called by her healer, and found her as dead.  
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had come from it, and knew well that it had not been cut vein nor led forward except to the throat, and the veins flowed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hastened and sewed up the wound, and cured it until it was healed; 
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and it happened to the young lady that she returned to her voice, and returned to her condition afterwards;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for because of this I say that in cutting the epiglottis there should be no fear.  
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in color like a boil, and it is much in women; 
et est selonc II manieres:	and it is according to II manners:  
naturez, et accidens;	Nature itself, and accidents; 
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or Nature has no engine.   
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accident is according to II manners, one of which is similar to fat for us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery. 
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there is fear, and it is not proper to work fiercely except in that which is small, and the proof and search into all the intruder: 
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it like our fat, and cannot into any vein, if you cut it, as we cut the fat, and treat all its head, if there is any.  
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And enclose well soon, and treat it as it is proper, until it is perfectly healed. 
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many manners of us are there, of which I will say all the resemblances;  
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now it is necessary for me to say all the difference which is between our and issue. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that an issue is sometimes feverish and hot, as long as the boiling (of pus) has passed, and is complete with rot; 
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Then rest the fever and heat.  
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the our (our) there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and contains the pus, which is its own bag and is according to the color of the body, and begins also like a boil, and becomes large; 
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and are according to II appearances, or gray, or moist, and many of colors are as I have said in the division. 
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of this type of ailment, that you examine and inquire first about all the instrument which is called "entromissoire," according to its shape and chapter which is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of incising (of) the abscesses of our is that you prick or more moist their place than you find in the abscess, and turn your two points and points, as long as you know that the instrument has pierced the heart, then it shall be according to the greatness of the abscess; 
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then remove the instrument, and take care of those that may jump. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs forth short, what color it has, treat it as I said with other abscesses; 
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the instrument no moisture comes forth, know that it is fatty, so treat it in a cross shape, and take it with pincers, and lightly scrape it from each side and guard the coat where it lies so that you may draw it out healthy with the nut; 
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out healthy, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.  
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it returns to us many times; 
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a little remains and the wound grieves you, use some sharp corrosive powders on the wound, and strain the wound, and place soothing things on top of the hot abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; 
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if it is large to us, then we sew the two lips of the wound, and care for that which generates flesh 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the bleeding vein is contrary or other, then hurry and apply the place of powdered vitriol, and leave it for two or three days, as long as the wound suppurates, and rest the boiling of blood; 
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to cover that which remains of the new.  
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the forms of the intromitting instruments, and they are in three ways. 
grans et moien et petit;	large and medium and small.  
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three squares that are called 'albaret,' and one which is called 'breb,' and there are of three ways.  
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistula; 
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are also like the needles that one sews with for sorcerers, and are of citrine gold, or iron, or silver, and most valuable are those which are yellow, and are more experienced to be used against black pimples in order to enclose the borders of a fistula; 
et sont de III manieres:	And they are of three ways:  
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the perforations. 
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The forms of the needles are of many resemblances, as you see here:  
grans, moiens, et petis;	large, medium, and small; 
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if needles which have two curvatures of three ways also; 
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if needles which have three curvatures, and are also of three ways;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if needles which have two curvatures, and needles of one curvature only, and are of three ways;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And all of these are necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The chief of these things to do are cutting, and there are some that don't cut more than one side, from which we scrape the flesh because for that reason we don't cut the vein nor the nerve. 
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these introducers are the alembles put back in handles so that the patient doesn't feel them at the opening of abscesses.
et sont de III manieres:	And they are of three ways. 
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	Large, small, and medium, as you see.  
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And one shouldn't use them except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and  groins, and similar places.
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And never is the other instrument made small, seeming like scrapers of fists, according to this form, for which one stanches blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And place it once at its place which is safe from cutting of the veins, and arteries, and never again according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, so that they appear like a woman's breasts. 
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	And remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, he should be according to this form of these lines b. to g.:  
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound preventing flesh from growing back, then stitch together the two edges of the wound, and treat it until it is healed; 
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	And if the breast leans down and is softened by its size as it happens with women, then make two cuts above it, in two similar slits;
