de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one holds onto the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from line b. up to line g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and there administer what we have said of sewing and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed. 
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the loss of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment. 
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it has soaked up the remaining and the fat, then cure it until it is healed.  
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are types of hard scrofulas that have ribs, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those therefore who contain moisture it behoves that they be cut according to this form, from the line .b. up to the line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, apply to the wound old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and cure with ointment thereafter as long as it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofulous sores, then treat it as we said for cutting into scrofulous sores, and if the wound is hollow inward, apply cautery as we said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut, and the skin above it is sealed, then many times abscesses occur, and this also happens to an inflamed vein and an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if you know this is for the artery, then the abscesses are long formed. 
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	And when you feel it at your hips, so you feel a tightening. 
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when this is for the vein, so there are red-colored appearances.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	And it is foolish to cover this abscess, and even when it is under the armpits and arms and neck and in many other places, and it is very large.  
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is therefore necessary to discard the iron treatment, and the one who is at the top should also be discarded, and in the one who is inflamed of an artery felt from above the skin long.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then work the cut like incisions, and beautifully depart the artery from the tissues, until it is uncovered. 
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then put under it a needle, and let it pierce until the other side, and extract the artery with a doubled thread in II leagues, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the II arteries which are in temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then point the place which is between the two ligaments of an intromittor as long as the pus that is there issues, and let be cut open the abscess; 
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then administer the cure that causes a bowel to close, as long as the ligament holds.  
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure those of ointment coming after those, as long as it is sound. 
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, it is necessary that you hold with your hand those that you can from the abscess to all the skin, then put the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and let it pierce, and have the thread double so that you draw it from the other side. 
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess as I told you, or bind of one of the two parts as two arms of the thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the thread is not inserted far, reinsert another needle through all the pus and under the incision of the first needle, and pull the threads in IV (four) lengths; 
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess until the superfluities come out, then cut the superfluity of the core and leave what is tied; 
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on the damp cloth in wine and oil, then administer care of poultices and ointments until it is healed. 
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses come to the nerves when they are burnt or by too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And these happen more often to assistants and to shoulders, and in all places where there are joints, and it is the painful abscess, and its color seems the color of the body, and is in many positions without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one constrains it strongly, the patient feels pain, and it is not felt throughout the body, but only below the heart; 
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and it moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor below nor above, and the one who is at the joints should not be covered with iron; 
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	For by chance there might go a contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and he who is at the head or forehead, makes the skin into a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root. 
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, suspend it with the awl, and flay it, then drain it and stitch the wound together, and dress it until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	of large swellings hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Sometimes in the belly and nowhere else a tumor occurs, and it is a disease called "fungus" because of its appearance like a boil, and the root is subtle, and the head is large.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	And there are some small and some very large ones; 
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw a man who had two in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and they were slightly split, and pus flowed from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found in one eighteen ounces weighing, and in the other six ounces, and the work in the incision is that you look if the patient is moist, and the color of the tumor is white and moist and with fine roots;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if the cup on the spatula is wide, and be in your presence the cautery to fire. 
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For at the hip joint often comes too great a flow of blood, and if it does not stop, then hasten to cauterize. 
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient is frightened and fearful of the incision of iron, then take a thread of wool well made, and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for days.  
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then restrain it, and do not cease restraining the thread of wool until it closes the artery, and ceases by itself through labor. 
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are large, you fear to close them entirely for the belly, but you can well close half of it, then cauterize it so that it does not return.
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then cure the wound, and guard that you do not close the vessels which are of red color and poor in feeling and milk-colored. 
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is a festering abscess, and I will come to the cure of the ulcer afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the tumor has increased
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the wound comes from cautery of a cut or splitting of the flesh, and is on the belly and in some places like those that occur in other cuts, or of blood which flows from veins or arteries according to what was said before, or of windiness. 
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is from the rupture of the flesh and the exit of pus, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens from various exits. 
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it to its sides, it rebounds, and then returns, and perhaps it is scarred, and grows much at the entrance of the bath and for hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, nor does it constrict at all.  
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to blood, then abscesses open by these signs: they are large and hard, and are filled according to a quantity. 
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is for windiness, so feel to the touch, and the works are that you see if its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	So it is necessary that you leave the care.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear about it, as I have told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if its appearance is for the intestine or the bowel, then you must command the patient to hold his arm, and be stretched straight, then grasp all around the abdomen. 
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then command him to groan softly between your hands, then go around the place that you have marked with the spatula, then extend half of the abscess upward to the entire large incision; 
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread, or a strong silk cord firmly, and let the us be bound by the linen; 
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then open half of the abscess extended over the linen, and put your index finger into it, and search for the intestine; 
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught in the cord, if untie it, and put the intestine out through the opening of the belly; 
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find the boil, take it with the pincers, and cut off the excess;  
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery or vein goes against you, then go well around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two threads through them, and put the two needles around what you have done in a cross so that you make it pierce; 
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess onto four places on the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave them in place as long as it pusses, and let the dead flesh fall away by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	Or you cut it when it is subtle and pusses, then treat it as needed, and close the abscess as we have said. 
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place of it as is fitting, and solder the place.  
dou chancre	of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have said in the division the likenesses of sores, and how one must work on them with medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron. 
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and let us say the sore originates in the marshes, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and ancients said that when sores are in a place where one can scrape it like a sore that is in the armpits, and in the groin, and in similar places, and must be entirely removed when it is at the beginning; 
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is large and old, it does not behoove you to approach it, because I can never heal any of them. 
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	no one has ever healed any of them before me.  
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the works, when it is in place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge any time the patient of black mucus. 
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	Then make him healthy if there is manifest swelling, then set the patient in a good place to do the work; 
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	Then throw your pins or ulcers, and the hair from all sides, and the bone from all sides with nothing left.
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And let the blood flow completely out, and press well the place with your hand or any thing, and if the bleeding of the blood is contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it as long as the bleeding is extinguished;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the cure of other cure until it is healed. 
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure which is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron.  
si est eclites soulement;	if it is illuminated only; 
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one should not touch with iron in these II similarities: 
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	that is to say, tympanites and hydropsarches, because it is a mortal thing;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	therefore when you medicate this similarity of dropsy which is called "illuminated" with medicines, and the cure does not profit, look at if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as flux and solution of the belly and similar things. 
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	If there is doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other disease than dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then do as follows: 
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	lift the patient straight up with your hands, and the ministers press the belly pushing the water to the lowest part of the stomach, then take the spinal spatula according to this form: 
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be trenches of II parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	at the point, and anyway do not be so far in that it can come to the intestine when you put it in, and you cannot bleed him; 
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then look if the dropsy is increased towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	if it is necessary that you cut under the belly three fingers right below the navel; 
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if the dropsy is from the disease of the liver, then let your incision be on the left side of the belly three fingers;
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is for the middle, whether to the right, and it is not fitting that the patient lie on the split so that the superfluities do not run to that weak place; 
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push it through, and lift your hand to the entire spatula between the skin and the fascia as in scraping to the quantity of a fingernail or until it enters; 
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	then pierce the fascia as much as the spatula comes to the view, and that is the place of the water, then pull out the tool, and push this instrument from where it is in this form: 
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it resembles a thin silver chain, and is made of brass or archaut light metal, and at the bottom part there is a small hole;
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and on one side, three holes;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and II from one side, and I from another; 
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the form of the incision that scribes cut the quill. 
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	At the top above is the edge, so that when the instrument comes to the point, it descends now onto the instrument.  
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	Empty therefore half or a third part, because if you empty more than is proper in that hour, by chance the patient may die for the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls senseless, or he approaches death. 
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	But empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulse.
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	Then treat the instrument and hold the point, and it is held now by the heart which stops the opening which is on the leaf, because of this I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner.  
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then begin again the instrument the other day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and treat with water a small quantity.  
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	do this no day, and guard yourself from pouring in so long as there remains but a little of water.  
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt about the patient, and you give him a lot of water, so he cures of the grave or hot sand, and by much sweat or bath and in the sun, and he stays pale.  
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and he cures of drying medicines as long as he is well, and cauterizes on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who have no holes in their penis, or the hole is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If this is necessary, then he must quickly be able to pierce all with a very fine spatula according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then put or pertu the subtle clo of plum, and tie it and hold it thus for III days or IIII and when he wants to make urine, so be removed the clo, and makes urine, and then put it back.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and perhaps it is not necessary, for the urine that comes forth does not leave it closed. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	The one whose hole is small, if it is medicated with the clo of flint as we have said, it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the prepuce in its place are pale, because none are born with the prepuce at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they raise their penis.  
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come to the urethra, and this is a bad illness. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies supine on his back, with the head of the penis and the scrotum extended as far as the width of a feather, so that the prepuce falls in the middle, as it should.  
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard yourself against the flowing of blood which often comes, and if it happens, use the bandage of those who bandage blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.  
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Many times these albations come in the vein, and it is an appearance of ugly flesh; 
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and some are malignant and some are not.  
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	So it is necessary that you prick them at the origin with a subtle needle, and cut and clean them all, then put soft cotton on top with Egyptian ointment.  
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it with Diafinicon ointment until it is healed. 
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the abscess is bad, of foul color and pus-filled, then you must bring a cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have cut it, and if the albation is in the vein, and has part inside the skin and part outside, it is necessary that you remove the albation which is inside first. 
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	and when it is fused together, then treat it with fire.  
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you cure it together, be sure the head of the bone is not pierced, and comes blackness and corruption in its shaft and groin. 
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	so it is necessary to shave all that is black and corrupted, then cover it with a paste of honey and flour made from the bark of quince trees and vezies, then cure it with other cures until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, administer the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cautery helps in two types of arrangements together:  
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	that is to say, for the removal of blood and for corruption. 
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the head of the bone is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you put or lead a chain of lead into the bone and urinate the patient among.   
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And when the skin is raw at the head of the penis which has not been circumcised, or where there is a wound or abscess, then it behooves you to scrape it with the sharp instrument, until the bonds are untied, and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides; 
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	And if it is a painful thing to discuss these, then it behooves you to scrape it with the spatula on no point of the head of the penis and of the skin; 
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	then carefully separate them, and place there the subtle cloth of linen moistened in cold water, so that it does not become raw again;
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not a wound of continuous healing like the others.
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	However, when we perform this work of our will, and properly on children, then it is necessary that we do the best work, and the lightest for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we have nothing more than what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen most of the masters and surgeons who performed circumcision in the city, and with force, and with a whole knife; 
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	since it was common for the foreskin to be two layers, and by chance if one cut above and the lower remained; 
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Then it is necessary to cut again, and the pain is doubled, and at the purification which is done in the city, the tip of the member is not well assured; 
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and at the purification of the penis by chance the iron escapes and the work is ruined, and many times they are born so that they do not need purification and I have seen it. 
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the modification which is made by force to the whole line of filament I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if they are equally sized throughout the whole soul it tightens;  
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the child be well stretched over the skin; 
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	And let the manner of the first work be that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only doing to him tying the thread around the penis so much, and then make him rejoice in all the ways that you can; 
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	then make him stand straight between your hands, and put the forces between your hands or under your feet that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; 
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	then put your hand to the penis and blow or heart, and pull it upward until the head of the penis is in. 
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	then clean it well of the filth which is gathered there, then tie the place with a double thread, then tie it under the one to the other lien;
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and hold it as you will by the second tie to the pouch and the index finger, and cut between the two liens, then lift the head upward gently and pull the head of the penis; 
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let blood flow drop by drop, because it is the purest 
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on and on the powder I drape it with a cloth of egg cooked without tempering with rose water, mixed with rose oil good and fresh, and let it stay until the next day, and treat it with other treatment as long as it is healed 
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of strength for fortification is this:  
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	the two shoulders should be kept and be sharpened, and the shoulders also as large as the hand equally 
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The error of fortification is when the veins inside are at the incision; 
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	therefore it behooves you to extend it to your finger, so that the pus forms an abscess;
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with pliers, and then cut it. 
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they pass three days, and what is below the penis is swollen, let him leave it until the abscess is calmed, and lightly scrape it. 
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If you cut it as much as you can move, and keep away from the part of the penis, it will not harm him at all. 
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Treat the wound then with powders from things we have said or treated of, and if you cut too much out and it goes above, it will do no harm. 
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat it then, as we have said, until it is healed. 
dou retenement de l’urine	holding back of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is from an obstruction of stone, or blood clotted, or bowel, or flesh growth, or similar things that we have said in the division; 
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	And if the urine is not released and you see that it is retained because of the stone which is in or at the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to be bent on his knees; 
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and let his feet be placed on his back, and extend his belly from the part above his back, and restrain the patient's arms as much as he can. 
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and then the neck of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the stone above, so that the urine flows freely.  
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer an extraction to him with all the instrument which is called "syringe," of which this is the form:  
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it should be of silver, finely worked and light, like the feather of a bird. 
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and let the handle be a palm long and a half, and let it be thin at the head. 
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the manner of extracting the urine is that you take a double thread and tie it to the head with a bit of wool or cotton, and put the end of the thread inside the syringe. 
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And cut the superfluity of the fleece and put it to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and aubin from egg, and make the patient sit on the seat, and raise his bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and tepid water; 
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	Then put the syringe gently on the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the belly; 
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then push the syringe forward to the bladder, and let the patient feel it come until the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order unless for those who lead or where it goes is twisted;
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then the thread is put to all wool piece by piece, and the urine follows the wool, then it is extracted, and correct the urine. 
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And begin the syringe again until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is aligned. 
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When sores or blood come in the bladder, or there is rot assembled there, and you see them distill liquids and medicine, then do to all the instrument that is called “clepsedre,” and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if it has three perforations:  
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	Two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; 
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the leaves are sewn together so that the medicinal ointment is such that it stops the member well without addition, if one can draw out moisture from it, and push when necessary; 
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see to place your medicines in the bladder, put the head of the catheter into the moisture, and treat with the syringe that is inside;
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	If you draw the moisture with the catheter, and then push the syringe back in strongly;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	If moisture enters there, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it;  
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the subtle form of the enema with which one enemas the bladder: 
si est ci:	here it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is made of silver or brass, and the head is higher.  
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and beneath to the groin where the limbs fall; 
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture with which you wish to enema the bladder in it, then tie it between the two breasts forming a band with a double thread, and heat the pot containing that moisture on the fire; 
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	then put the head of the enema into the penis, then strain your hand on the bladder with all the moisture coming out, until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make a circle in it, and pierce it roundly around. 
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then put the strong thread into these pierced holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a dial, and put inside it what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument.  
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do as you have done with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder. 
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have just said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; 
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and we have said the difference between a stone embedded in veins, and all the signs, and in what kind of stone one must work with a saw;
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the penis;  
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell it to you plainly and briefly. 
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder often happens more to children, and this is a sign that the water leaps from the bladder seeming like water in its subtlety.  
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and it opens the hare, and greatens the patient’s penis, and he often penetrates it, and then bends over. 
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	And with many of these leaps, the foundations are broken.  
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	And it is light for the healing of children until they are four years old, and it is very grievous in old men, and it is as much the middle, to those who are between youth and old age.
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	And the cure is lighter for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one. 
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to purify the patient by enema, in order to draw out all the mucus that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet, and thrust them out and move them downwards, so that the hip descends to the bottom of the bladder, and it protrudes from its high place. 
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	Then make him sit between your hands, supported, and his hands below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely inclined downwards. 
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	Then place it and touch it inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	If you feel the hip in the space, then hasten now to cut into the hip.  
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not fall to the touch at all, then moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adolescent.  
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and thrust it into its base, and place the hip, and when you feel it with your finger, then move it towards the neck of the bladder;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	Then press on your back, and thrust it out to where you want to cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And command the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the testicles upward, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the testicles in the part where one makes the cut. 
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then he thrusts the spatula cutting, which is its shape:  
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And make between those that are between the testicles and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left hip.
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And be straight over the stone, and your backsides be close or foundation, and be the cut through so that it is wide outward, and inward narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large. 
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	By adventure the press if the back which is or foundation, that it jumps out without work.
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and know that there are such stones which have angles, and edges:  
si est griés a issir;	if they are cut to be removed. 
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there is one that is soft, resembling a gland, and round, whose passage is light.  
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	To those then which have angles and edges, make the cut larger; 
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not come out, then you must extract it with tweezers which are also like a file at the head, in order to extract the stone so that it does not escape. 
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you put below the instrument subtle bent at the head;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot manage it this way, then enlarge the opening of the wound, and if the blood does not come out, then strain with vitriol. 
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there are more than one stone, then put the largest one first at the neck of the bladder, then cut above it, then the tract, and the smaller ones afterward if there are more. 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it must be sewn up, and a larger wound must be made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the patient: 
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	or he dies, or his urine comes back through where his bowels cannot hold it.  
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but nonetheless, you must try to treat him, or to break up the pliers, as long as you pull it apart in pieces.  
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, apply to the wound frankincense and aloe and dragon's blood, and restrain it, and put on top of it a cloth moistened in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; 
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	then bind the patient's neck, and do not untie the band until the third day.  
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you reduce it, then arise well its place of oil and water, then the cure of diaphynicon ointment and basilum ointment, until it be healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if an abscess arises in the wound and corruptions, and blood clots in the bladder, and as a result the urine is retained, which is known in this manner that it does not flow with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Therefore put your point in the wound, and extract the blood, for if it remains there, it will corrupt the bladder, and cause it to rot. 
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift the wound clean and dry and of silk, and help it in all the ways that you know, until it is healed.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And it is necessary that every hour that you treat it, you tie its two thighs together, and apply the medicines on top of the wound. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is in the passage leading from the penis, and caught there, and urine cannot pass; 
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	then treat it as I say now, that you cut it many times, and excuse the cutting through this treatment. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take one piece of iron in this form, and let it be shaped like three angles fastened to one stick.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder. 
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	Then push the forest onto the rod lightly, until it reaches the stone. 
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	And turn the forest in your hand at the stone poke and poke, as long as you can feel the stone on the other side; 
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	If then comes forth the urine, then press your hand on that which remains of the stone which is within the rod. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it then breaks, and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is healed;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you cannot do this because of any obstacle that prevents it, then tie one thread below the stone and the other above, then make the rod straight against the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the threads, and cleanse the coagulated blood which is in the wound; 
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure it until it is healed.  
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It sometimes happens that a stone is lodged in women, and if it ever happens, the treatment is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons: 
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a woman well-knowing who discovers herself to her midwives, even when she is chaste. 
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third reason is that perhaps one cannot find a woman well-knowing in this art of hands;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth reason is that the stone of the woman is more deeply embedded than the stone of a man, for which it is necessary to make a deeper cut, and there is great fear. And if necessity demands it, then you must procure a midwife well-knowing, and at pains find one, and if you cannot find one, then take no unchaste midwife;  
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and present to him a woman who is well-versed in the lives of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her that she do what you command him concerning the inquiry of the stone; 
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look carefully if the woman is a virgin:  
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it befits him to put his finger or foundation and seek the stone; 
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, then she forces it under her finger, and he recommends that she put her finger or on the patient, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder forming. 
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If she finds it, then it befits that she move it from great to great from the entrance of the bladder until below, as long as it comes to the root of the thigh; 
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then stop on the stone in the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the buttock, where it is seen to appear, and feel the stone in that part; 
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move his hip above or below the stone, and let the waist be at first small;  
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then push the loin in the waist, if you feel the stone so close to the wound as long as the stone can pass out, and know that many kinds of stones are there:  
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	that is to say, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and which have veins. 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the stone does not come out, put in its place powdered vitriol, and hold it there for an hour as long as the wound is stained;  
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, as long as the stone is out, and have instruments that I told you about in extracting the stone from men to help you in your work;
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if the vein is injured and it's from the artery that is cut, then put powder on the place and bind it with bandages and don't start again with this, and leave the stone and don't milk it at all, lest the patient die by chance.  
puis cure la plaie.	then heal the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the parts are dried, return to your work, as long as the stone remains in place.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	White viscous is nothing else than an assembly of moisture or white phlegm that is from the center of the bowels, which contains the egg; 
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and is called "phlegm," and it is properly found in the lining of the egg if one thinks that this is the other egg; 
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and this is the skin of the bowels between the white phlegm that we have said;  
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and these do not have a similar name. 
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this branch is of weakness that comes from the genitals, and that matter is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the bowels, and this moisture can have many colors;
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or when it is colored declining to jaundice, or without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more.  
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, because if it is white as we have said, then the abscess is ripe,  it is long like the figure of an egg, and does not open the edges, because it has moisture all around. 
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in the proper skin, then the abscess is ripe with a part of the egg, and for this reason people think that it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if the moisture is between the skin of the edges and the white like that, then one feels it well. 
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, you should probe at all the intercessor quarreling, from which its form is before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this then which comes after the introducer, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his ability and the replenishment of his body; 
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then place him on his back, on a thing a little high, and put under him many cloths;  
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart of the bones;  
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spoon-shaped tool, and cut the skin of the bones along their length up to near the armpit, and let your incision be entirely straight dividing the skin of the bones until you reach the white bone, and gently peel it according to your ability;  
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	then pierce the white bone plainly with water at the large opening, and draw out all the water, then put your tweezers in, and extend the white bone upwards; 
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the root of the testicles, but only the scrotum; 
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	cut all or in parts the  ribs with subtlety, that if you do not cut them wisely, the fluid will return. 
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the bladder is in your work, place it back when you have completed the work of the scrotum. 
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then join together the two leaves of the root of the testicles with one stitch, then treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the bladder corrupted by another illness, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels which are suspended, doubting the discharge of blood.
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	then cut the testicle with all its suspender, and extract the bladder, and treat it as we have said.  
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if the fluid is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two veins. 
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	if you strike the other part just as you did the first equally, then wipe the blood, and put in the wound a soft cloth moistened with rose oil. 
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put another woolen cloth moistened with wine and oil on top, and place the two bandages on top, and put doubled cloths above, and tie it over the entire bandage according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths and employ them with wool fleece according to this resemblance and they should be assembled by stitching in the groin of the breeches, and one of the shoulders rests on the foundation until the back, and the other at the armpit; 
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two chiefs over the two arms, and be all assembled the restraint in the buckle of the breeches; 
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and at no time is medicine this cauterization in place of an iron scalpel, and it is that you take the cultellary cautery subtle, and strike the skin of the groin, and be heated as we have said, so that the white syfac containing the water is uncovered; 
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	if you take the cautery according to this form, and pierce it at once at that point, and burn it with this subtle cautery hot: 
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And cup in all ways you can, as long as you scrape everything clean; 
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and keep that the fire does not touch the eye;  
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and know that this work is more healing; 
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and make sure guarding against blood loss, and cut the work of size;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing else goes against you, or an abscess forms or blood loss or anything else, then cure what opposes you according to that which is said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work because of its horror, then administer perforation as I told you, and it is that when you are well certain by the significations that we have said that the aquatic root is there, then make the patient sit on the elevated seat; 
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	Then pierce the abscess in the area below to the entire width of the spatula, and place the perforation through the length of the body. 
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	And let the opening be wide so that all the liquid flows out.  
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then put cotton on the spot, and tie it, and allow the remaining liquid to drain, then treat it until the wound is healed.  
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	And if the white cloth does not allow the liquid to flow out of the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you pour a quill or instrument used to treat water in dropsy, whose form is described earlier.  
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And enlarge the opening of the wound, and know that the liquid returns, and is assembled after six months or until then, and when it is assembled as before, so will the patient's days pass.  
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this branch there is fear in many positions, for which it seems to me better one leaves it. 
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and appearances of the abscess.  
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I therefore say that many abscesses come from the body, and even from the genitals; 
et c’est par mout de cas.	and this is by many causes.  
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	That is to say by excessive sour and sharp humors which are spread to the genitals, or from percussion;   
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; 
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and does not feel pain, and it is a grievous abscess;   
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by adventure there are some grievous abscesses porous and pithy, and of a dark color, and sometimes comes from the outside of an artery, or from an inflammation of a vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is through an artery, then it is known by the arrangement of a hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers.  
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	And it does not behoove you to touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	The one who is made from the swelling of a vein is known by its arrangement at the touch of the fingers, and you can well do the incision on this resemblance, and on the other veins.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	And it is that you cut the core of the veins, then the point is on top, and the thread of white sephac, and deliver the suspensory from all sides of the point.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the point is already joined with these veins, then it behooves you to draw the point, and cut.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is attached to the sephac, or in what is inside the vessels, then you must deliver all that vein, and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the cartilage is or their rear, then you must cut it all out and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your works are completed, so apply the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess enveloped in a covering resembling the burgeon, with the softening of the boils, and it moves painfully when the patient walks. 
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and the cure of this malady is as well prepared as fearsome as the one before, and nevertheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It behooves you to make the patient sit on a high seat, then bring the suspensory of the hips down to your knees, over all the vessels which are near the penis, and the masters bind them, and extend them in shape.  
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	then cut with a broad sharp spade through the area of the vessels, until they are exposed, and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries which are in the temples. 
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then he inserts a needle where there is the double thread, and ties it to the first place where the worm came, and ties it straight to the other end. 
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then he cuts them in the middle straightly, according to the length of the body, and pulls out the corrupt moistures. 
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then he cures the wound as with the others where one injures a bowe, so that no vessel spills that nourishes one of the corners.
