car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for by this comes no harm, and if to all the vessels comes life, it is necessary to draw the corners to all the vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment for the incision of the vessels, and dry out and cannot be helped.  
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the thigh
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The happening of this ramic so is by the section that comes or where it is placed, or the extension on the belly in the part of the angles, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the corners.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	And this rupture is either by a blow or from an extension of it, and these two ways come from many causes. 
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	Or from percussion, or from a jump, or from pulling, or lifting of heavy weights, and similar things.  
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	And the signs when it is from an extension of the blow are that they happen poco a poco, over a long time, and do not come suddenly. 
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	And is the abscess even up to the armpit, because the blow tightens the intestines.  
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the sifac, that it brings at the beginning sudden pain, and are the abscesses diverse appearing, under the skin near, and it is for the issue of the intestine and the body to the outside of the sifac.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines are trapped with the bowels, and held in there, and cause great pain to suffer the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron fear, for which it is necessary to avoid it.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of treatment is that you command the patient to push the intestine back into the wound with his hand if he can.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	Then it should be supported on his neck between your hands and lift his hips. 
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	Then is the heart above, and cut all the skin of the nails long. 
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	Then put inside the leaves of the waist needles according to what you need to open the wound, and be such that the eyes can issue. 
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then scrape the skin that is under the skin of the nails, until the white flesh is uncovered on all sides. 
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	Then put your two index fingers in that which follows the nail, in that which is between the white flesh which is under the skin of the egg, and between the second flesh, and depart from what is behind the egg, and between the second flesh.
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	And then move with your right hand inside the heart of the nails, and be the white flesh on top to your left hand, and raise the egg to all the flesh toward the waist.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	And instruct the minister to extend the arm upwards, and untie what is behind the bandage. 
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	And feel his flanks if he has any bowel wrapped or white and hard lump, and if you find none of these things, then bring him to the belly below. 
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	Then take a needle or it has the thick thread made of X threads, and bring it into the back part of the lump, which is after the skin of the groin. 
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	After the waist, then cut the hairs that appear from the threads, until there are IV threads.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	Then join them one upon the other in manner of a cross, and tie the lump, which we have said is below the skin of the groin, with a strong band of two parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then wrap the shoulders with threads, and bind them together from two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter within, lest any abscess come there. 
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and place the strip directly according to the first strip long two times that of the other one, and after these two strips leave down the soft part which is below the breast of the thighs the greatest of a two. 
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	and after all the rest according to the roundness that the egg carries; 
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	then cut in the part which is below the skin of the thighs, as much as the sinew and the bone, as we have said before;
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then administer wool soaked in oil, and put it in the wounds, and place the strip that we have said.  
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes is cauterized the whites (as we have said), after the incision, for fear of  discharge of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	For this happens many times, and leave the strip until it dries by itself; 
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if he delays in sitting, he should be raised with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it heals.  
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then cure the wound with another cure, until it is perfectly healed. 
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I never saw anyone who dared to make the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made like the root that is joined to the living body, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after cutting lightly above or below; 
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	then cut in the middle, and treat the abscess with those who work, as long as the vessels bleed;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.  
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	Sometimes a rupture comes in the bowels, as we have said, and opens them; 
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and do not remove any of the intestines from the bowels, and if they are removed, it is a little, and repair them every hour.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	And nevertheless if it remains too long in this point, the wound or abscess grows, until the intestines descend. 
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	And this happens by the extension of the abscess which is at the angles, as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and swollen its parts and open. 
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	And the cure is thus by cautery, as we have said before. 
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	And sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner:  
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	And it is that the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the rupture inflamed to the width according to the quantity of three fingers.  
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	And then extract the abscess which is under the skin that follows it, then take the rail and put it on the place appearing of the abscess.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And you press to the bottom of the belly, then sew the two appearing parts of the abscess above the head of the rail, and sew both.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then withdraw the head from its socket and do not cover the wound or extend the limb or anything else, as I have told you in the treatment of a hernia.  
puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Then treat it with the treatment for wounds. 
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse and care for the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The incision is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved to this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the genitals
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because those things that are within are softened, and it becomes visible. 
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	And it is necessary, when one wishes to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and one cuts the skin which is softened on the natural skin; 
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	then bring together the two lips with one suture, and if you see it, first sew the excess of the softened skin with three sutures or four firmly; 
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	then cut between the sutures, and treat it like other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the thread. 
dou chastrement	Through chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Know that cauterization is common in our law, and for this reason I would like to not speak of it in this book; 
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and it is only necessary for two manners:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	one of which is that the physician knows how to answer when asked, and in his wisdom cures.
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we often need cautery from some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and calves and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	Therefore, I say that cautery is done according to two manners: 
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	or by traction, or by splitting. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In the one we perform by traction, make the animal sit in hot water until the joints are softened and pliable; 
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then grasp them with your hand, until they are put back and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille:	Of the chastisement of size: 
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	it is necessary that you hold the animal steady, and press the skin of the joints with your left hand, then tie the suspensory, and cut above each opening at the top, when you have well scraped them; 
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and leave no pore through which the soft fat and the fine fat that is on the vessels may escape.
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this manner of chastisement is better than the one done by traction, because in traction, perhaps nothing remains from the joints, so that the animal desires lust;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	then cure the wound until it is healed. 
des hermofrodites	of the hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermaphroditism is according to II manners as men:  
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	one if it is that between the two sexes appears also as the figure of a woman, or he has hair, and sometimes in court the urine.  
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and it is on the pointed part as well as a rod, and they will conceive.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the care of the man and of the woman is that you cauterize the joined parts together, and cure them as other wounds. 
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	in the second manner, of men whose urine leaps through the skin of the genitals, there is no cure.   
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	Tentigene is a joined part above the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; 
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is its cure.  
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	It behooves that you singe the superfluity of the tentigene to your hand or as one does, and cauterize it lightly; 
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not move it too much, so that bleeding does not come, then the treatment of other treatments until it is healed; 
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and to another ulcer that is born at the mouth of the gums, and the lip, and perhaps jumps out, and is according to the resemblance of a cow, and for this they called it in the ancient 'cow disease'. 
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary that you cut it, as we have said the treatment, and the cure until it is healed.
de erratique	of wandering
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	Erratic if it is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small.
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	and is natural by birth, or accidents by illness that came to it; 
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	or it is due to joint disease, or syphilis subtle or thick, and is made by movement in the gums, or ribs, or under, or wherever it may be;
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	and prevent conception, and childbirth, and by chance flowers to have. 
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	and the knowledge of these things is by the regard of the bailey.  
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is appearing close by, if you want to [place it] on either side or to the back.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is subtle of syfac, and it is close to the two books, then you hurry, and say thus: 
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	Put your two finger indices together, and the woman be upon her back, legs spread.  
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	Then are the two books formed, as long as the subtle syfac is round, and be covered the stupor; 
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	Then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and put it upon the place, and lie the woman at home every day, so that she cannot stir.  
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the stylus is hard and thick, it is necessary that you cut it with the spatula seeming to a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the stupor is of flesh born, then suspend it to the onech and the cope; 
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and have the blood-stopping medicines, such as acaice, dragon's blood, incense, and a bundle of egg.  
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	then administer a wide bandage of cloth, so that the wound may not close. 
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and thus it is kept long, and administer a tent of dry linen;  
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then be cured with other dressings until it is healed.  
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh comes a new birth, it is necessary to cover according to this manner, if it is not abscesses inflamed.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the abscess that is inflamed which is in the marsh, one must not touch with fire.
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without usual care, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hardened. 
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	and we have already said in the division the similarities to them, and the signs, and I will say here those which resolve curing. 
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and boils, when they are inflamed in the flesh, and they do not appear to the touch, except for by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, one can feel them, those one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then hold the hardened part with tongs, and cut it at its roots, then powder with blood-stopping medicines such as acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things;  
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	then puts his feet to the wall for an hour, then puts it in cold water. 
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	and if there comes a decorrment of blood, then make him sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and galangal and similar things, and then take barley flour, and confection it with honey and aisil, and make an emplastrum of it on his back.  
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he strains, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If this is not the case, make him apply cupping glasses to the back and breasts without hurting. 
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	Then take linen, and soak it in juice of plantain or in lingonberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the place.  
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess is quiet, treat the place with ointment until it is healed. 
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	And the one called "albathir" is red and is similar to sharp resin, so it should be covered as I have said before.
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then treat until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the marshes
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many ways of abscess come in the marsh, such as boils and cancerous abscesses and herpe and styes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have said in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	Therefore, I must say in this treatise about the abscess that comes in the marrow, which is not like abscesses that boil; 
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you want to know the work of iron, look at whether this abscess is hot at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it. 
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Therefore, do not hurry too much to pierce, but let it mature until the pain is appeased;  
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then have the patient sit on a seat, and have small seats where he leans, and supports his back and brings his legs together towards the sides of the leg. 
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and let his thighs be spread out, and put his arms below his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; 
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	Then succeed the thrust towards the right rib, and there administer the instrument with which one operates the mouth of the channel, so that afterwards comes the form.  
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	And it is necessary that when you see administer this instrument, that you first make the thrust in order to know the depth of the channel, so that what enters within the instrument does not come more deep than it must, and that it does not harm the patient; 
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	And if the instrument is larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the channel with cloths so that the instrument does not harm him; 
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	And it is necessary that he put the cone of the instrument above, and that he holds the instrument.  
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscess opens, and one makes it with a soft hand, then it is necessary to cover it at the head, at the spatula level.  
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	And when the wound is emptied, it is necessary that you put in the wound tender cloths moistened in rose oil, or in green-colored dry oil; 
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	And place the cloth further from the wound to the edge of the margin, and place outside above the margin and on the linen blade net moistened in water or mallows being boiled. 
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then care for it after two days of ointment coming up to this, until it is healed;
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	And at no time lift the margin and the wound by a clyster of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and long aristida being boiled;
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Then return to the ointment. 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is put back in its place, then you should guard against cauterizing with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	It is necessary first at the birth that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs if are when you see the woman pressing down, and desiring to smell the air; 
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	Therefore, the child should quickly move with force  
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	Therefore, know that this infant's birth is according to the natural form, and it is born under its head, and the second follows him; 
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	And when you see these signs, it is proper to gently press his belly so that the child comes out quickly.   
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	Because when he descends upon his head, the second follows him, and the womb is freed of its superfluities by good purification.
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.  
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it comes sometimes on his feet, and comes toward the body or the shoulder, and the hands, or where it comes on his belly, or groin, and is converted by chance onto his neck, and by other bad figures; 
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	so it is necessary for the healer to be wise and subtle in these things, and wary of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help them. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the child comes on his head by natural issue, and the woman gives birth hard, and the virtue of her is weak, then she make her sit on a saddle, or the women hold her;
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and rouse her nature of oil or fennel is cooked, and then put the healer between her thighs the small spatula whose form is here: 
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and split the secondary bone, and cut to its nail until the moisture which is inside it exits. 
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and take the belly of the woman as long as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to clysterize the woman with a mixture of fenugreek with sesame oil. 
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	then make her take and sneeze from condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour:  
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	then now extract the child. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if the two hands come out first, then it is necessary that you gently pull them little by little;
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot go in, then put the woman on a stool, and raise her feet up high; 
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then unseat the stool on the ground, and hold onto the woman so that she does not fall during the unsitting.  
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the hand cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands at the elbow that is before mentioned, and extract the child, and reset it evenly. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes upon its feet, then it should be pushed upward.  
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it back and forth, until it is even. 
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	Then pull it by the feet and extend it back and forth.  
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When he jumps to his hips, then command him to take hold, and make him sneeze from congestion. 
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it were to jump further, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not good as we have said, so turn it back and forth, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Therefore then there is lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if it does not come further as we have, then say take muscle of aloe and oil of sesame, and gum melted, and grind all in the mortar; 
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and put on the woman's inside nature and outside this ointment, then make her sit in a deep well until below the ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	And when it is softened beneath, make a collar of mirr, and put it beneath, and leave it for an hour. 
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	Then make them sit on the seat, then make them sneeze and restrain their mouth and nose, and gently grasp their belly, for the child now jumps. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, put the basin on their hands back and forth;  
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then be sewn to their neck, and let their feet hang down, and lie down on the bed; 
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and bend their hands back and forth, and then take their hands on their belly, and take away the cushions beneath, until she is well prepared down below; 
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not jump, take their feet and move them, then move their belly upward, and then put your hands in.  
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and beat the child peck and peck; 
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and command the woman to prepare herself until the child is born.  
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes out with a hand wide
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to devise a way to bring back the hand: 
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	If one cannot bring it back, then make the woman stand up, and go away.  
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If she cannot go, then make her lie on the bed, and straighten out her legs; 
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the poultice that I have recounted.  
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	And if she does not give birth, then make her sit on the stool, then study how to bring back the hand; 
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and beat the child according to its natural form, and make her sneeze, and command her to prepare herself until the child is born. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the birth of the child on his neck, and has spread his hands, and his face turned toward the back of his mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is necessary that the bailiff hold his hand, then turn it peck and peck, and beat it lightly;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	And when it is even, put on its muscle tissue of altitude and oil, as we have said, then command him to move it a little here and there. 
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	And when you will have done this, put the part on its seat, and command him to feel it.  
et la fai esternuer.	And then make the part sneeze. 
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner to all the spine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to be done in this manner to the whole joint, cut the joint with your fingernail, until the moisture is evacuated.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	And if the child cannot rise on his face and neck, then cut the skin of the wound so that it is not held back, and kill the child. 
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	Then put the child inside, until you have placed him as it is right, and command the woman to feel it no time.
adonques si istra legierement.	Then it will be gently extracted. 
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four.  
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	And this is not a strange thing, and it happens often. 
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are strange things, and do not live, if they are named;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know these, that they be multiplied, and are destroyed by the power that divides them, which is linked to the womb;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they come forth as naturally as one each under, as we have said. 
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they come forth struggling, so the cure as we have said, and let the midwife be subtle, and make quickly and lightly what she does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and make thus as he will cure to health. 
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	No times are formed in the marshes I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more until XV, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of his glorious sage, and it is fitting that the bailiff knows all this because perchance similar things happen; 
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	if made according to what is fitting. 
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure the woman of the dead child or belly, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with hands; 
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	if it is fitting that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and does not have an accident or she has fear of death; 
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	if it is fitting that the woman be supported on her back, and her hips be inclined down, and the legs raised; 
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the minister the braid from the two parts, where it is tied to the bed so that it is not pulled at the descent of the child
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the mare's with moist oils with marshmallow and fennel seeds and flaxseed, then anoint the bailiff his hands with these oils and these poultices
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	then put them in the mare lightly, then quench the place where she puts her hooves to be convenient for them, and take guard if the child is appeared that it descends upon its head 
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	if put the hooves in its eyes or on its neck or in its mouth or under its tongue or beneath the beard or in the groin or near the ribs, and if the descent is upon feet, put it where the pin prick and at the middle ribs 
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is convenient that he braids the hoof with his right hand, and put the crook between his two of the left hand, and put it into all his hand lightly, and put the hoof in any of these places that we have said, as long as it comes to the thing empty
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the form of the onchne: 
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then fit against the other onchne, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal; 
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then make them equal in moving from one side and the other, so that they may slip easily, and let the onchnes be toothed so as to hold well, as it is here the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if one part remains, then oil the root with some of its oil, and put it in that part, and draw the other part; 
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if none remains, then put this onchne or higher up, and do so until it comes all out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be brought back for the tightening, then you must wrap it on the blanket until it comes out all;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	then hold the head in the joint of the foot or on the knife, and thus you must do with the other hand, and at II feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the child's head is large and it is stuck at the exit, or if there is a sharp chief assembled, then you must insert the pointed spatula between your two, and make the head and extract the sharp.  
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you will do it with the instrument that is called "almidach", so that the shape comes with the instruments or chapter which is after this one. 
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus the same if the child has a large head naturally.  
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then pull the bones with the tongs, and if the head jumps out and is strained to the forceps, then it is broken, as long as the moisture which is at or lower exit.  
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot move, cut it up into pieces as much as you can. 
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, it is necessary that you pierce it until the moisture runs out. 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the attraction is light, and the direction towards the mouth of the mare is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is protruding in the belly or breast, it is necessary that you draw it out with the cloth wrapped around your hand. 
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and bind the belly or breast, until the moisture inside runs out.  
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if the other members are broken and the shoulder remains, put the basin in their palm with the mouth of the basin facing up, and draw it up to the mouth of the basin.
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	then put the pincers or tongs into it, and pull it out forcefully.  
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	And if the mouth of the basin is narrowed because of the hot abscess that has come there, it does not need to be worked on. It is necessary instead to administer moist and fatty things
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And the minister plasters, and soak them in softening and moistening water. 
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, administer those that we have said for a living child. 
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if one has no power, then it is treated in pieces, and nothing of the second part is left.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, administer those that we have said for boils that come in the marsh. 
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And if bleeding comes, then it is put in restraining water, and administer other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly a child had been dead, then she conceived another on top of it, and refused death to the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time he came to have an abscess on his head, and it swelled so much that it opened and began to discharge pus greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought long time, and could not solder the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong traction, and out came one bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was much amazed, because this one whose belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I sought the wound, and treated with my hands bones, as long as the woman was in a better state; 
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	And the woman lived for a long time like this, and it came to be a little bump of bone from there.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have recorded this chapter for those who, when the masters find a strange thing, that they may know how to help.  
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the bone back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	Here after comes the form of the pressor, as it is written in books; 
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and to its turning as to the two shoulders of the two limbs.  
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be more subtle of the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and its mouth of the barrel it must be wide, and the edge of the trees it must be long one palm and a half;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two limbs should be two adjustments of this same barrel, which are fastened in one and the other, half a palm long or an inch more.  
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and these two adjustments are put into the mouth of the collar to open when one turns the two horns. 
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, in its appearance more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the resemblance of tongs. 
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and has two arms adjusted, as you see, one palm long, and two fingers wide; 
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	and when you see to open the matrix with the entire instrument, so make the woman sit on the bed, her feet hanging and legs spread apart, then put the two arms adjusted together in the matrix, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; 
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then operate your hand with the entire instrument, as you have done with the tongs equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the matrix, as long as the patient does what she wants. 
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	This instrument is all mounted, and are multiplied their appearances; 
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	And when the mirrors show them clearly, then it is more demanding the work, and higher for men because of their quantity. 
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the tool that you may have prepared it, because their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained in childbirth, it behooves you to command the woman to retain her breath, and then make her sneeze forcibly, and hold her hands at her mouth and nose.  
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	And if she leaps for this, well is. 
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If that does not happen, then take a pot, and make an incision or coverlet, and put herbs there that may open the mouth of the uterus, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury. 
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	All these herbs, or any of them, be boiled or stewed in water on the fire;
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	Then put a cane or opening of the pot, and the other chief in the mouth of the uterus, and keep it so that the vapors come inside the uterus. 
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	then make him sneeze, as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the back of the hip jumps suddenly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this cure and there is no force, command the woman to wet her left hand in sesame oil or in the juice of rue, and then put it into the vagina, and pull on the second time;
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when she has found it, seize it and extend it back and forth gently so that the strings do not tear during extraction; 
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but it should be moved gently left and right, and then pull.
si venra et se desaerdra.	Then it will come out and disentangle itself.  
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the opening of the vagina is too narrow, we have said the cure of sneezing and fumigating with herbs.  
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	And if she is not cured by all that we have said, then beware that you do not pull 
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the uterus, you tie it to the hip of the woman, then the cleanse with ointment tetrafarmascon. 
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	if she endures and puts it back, and comes for; 
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but nevertheless, when she endures this, a bad smell comes to the stomach and head, and paleness occurs to the patient. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	Therefore it is necessary fumes suitable to these;
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of watercress and dried figs. 
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of flowers and of the second is this.
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And is to be seen resembling a dog, and one puts the head subtle in the fire, and the shoulders wide over the fire; 
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be over the embers, and the wool until it is scorched, and begin another one. 
de percier lou fondement	to examine the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation perceived, but rather have it stopped by some subtle syphons;
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore it befits the surgeon to pierce him with that instrument in its place, and do not pierce him at all with a sharp spatula, and guard the bandage so that she does not touch it. 
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place upon the wound half in wine and oil, then the ointment's cure until it is healed.  
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will return, then put or place a piece of wood, and leave them hands for many days, and be removed when the child wants to go into rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And at no time comes this stoppage of a wound or an abscess;  
si covient coper celui soudement:	Therefore it befits to cover that stoppage. 
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	If it is cured, as we have said of the chain of flax.  
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that come from beneath the foundation are nodules, and greater than those that come near the foundation outside, or in the space of the two parts, if there is one fistula or more.   
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	And when that nodule is ancient, it works, and in short moisture white or subtle boils, and at no time are these fistulas pierced. 
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	And they are known by those who have experienced it or by flatulence when the patient defecates, and perhaps in jumping some of them go out.  
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if to fistulas that penetrate up to the bladder, and up to half the penis; 
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and reach up to the junction of the groin, and up to the knot of the scrotum.   
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the fistula penetrating to the base, and not penetrating; 
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you insert your index finger or base, and insert a subtle needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twisting.  
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has twisting, then you insert a tent of fine linen or horsehair until you feel the tent or hair at your finger;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is no coming out of pus or windiness or humors, as we have said: 
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	know that it does not pierce;  
si te haste dou curer.	if you hurry to cure it. 
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced up to the bladder or up to the urinary duct, then the urine leaks out, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced as far as the junction of the hip, then the tendon comes as far as its place;  
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the invention of pain around it, then it is that there is something added below it, and it does not take medicine or treatment by ointment;  
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure except for labor, and vanity of foolish mirrors that intervene. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In the one that is not persistent and not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have proven, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; 
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	And raise his legs up to his hips, and have his hips inclined to his belly. 
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	Then put a tent of lead, or of plaster if there is curvature, until you know where the tent comes from. 
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels it around the base, then it is necessary that you put your index finger on it, if you feel then that the tent has pierced it.
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	And be discovered where you feel between your finger the sifac or the flesh, then you know that she is pierced.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If it does not travel with this one cannot heal it. 
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One says nevertheless that one can heal them well, but this happens little.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	And the aid one does it if one scalds the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	And put all hot in the fistula, until it comes near to the foundation. 
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	And do this two or three times, as long as you know that these charred parts are burned, which look like an owl's feather; 
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	And then cure it with damp tents in butter, until those charred parts are gone, then cure it with ointment containing sulfur and lead. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healed, that is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If this cannot be healed otherwise;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	And if the tent goes in and does not reach to the bottom which is the foundation, and between your finger and the tent there is a thick covering of charcoal or  syphax, and you see the fistula following this covering toward the heart; 
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	Then cut at the beginning of the fistula, and push forward before the tent, and then use the cautery after it until it reaches the top of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and will be delivered the tent, and will fall; 
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	then  remove those feathers that seem like an ostrich feather, and no remaining any.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound festers, and it comes between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For the fire cautery assembles two things good: 
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	that is to say, the burning of those joined hairs, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture. 
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the cure of tents moistened in butter or in ground hazelnuts, until the wound is covered, and if the hairs are burned in the bottom; 
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then cure the wounds of those swollen eyes by applying a hard dry dressing, and they are the dry medicines.  
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up to right through the bottom of it, and is separated from the body, then you cut it at its base or foundation, and ask about those.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the tent and there is between it the linen or the silk or hairs, and it is close to bursting, then there is no other way but by the administration of one of these three ways: 
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put dressings on it and treat it as before. 
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep lest you cut the tissue that holds the foundation, and let the eggs flow by their own volition. 
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat it as we have said;  
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the membrane after it is cut from below its foundation, or by dressing or another pointed instrument.  
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then carefully remove the fatty tissue in the wound as much as you can;   
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then study to restore the wound, and keep the fistula in the part outside the foundation. 
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	so it will be a lighter thing for the patient.  
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And at no time are fistulas in this manner: 
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and it is when you place the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the base near the skin above, then take a perforated tent at the head according to this form:  
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And it puts the thread wrongly into the second, and pushes the tent all along the thread into the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is inserted into the edge of the base inside, then you should extract the thread of the one pierced, as when you put your own or base.  
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and treat the head with thread, and assemble the two shoulders together, and bind them to each other, and let it so for a day or two; 
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it no times, as long as the threads cut these flesh that are between two, and shrink;  
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then cure the wound as long as it is soldered and healed. 
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to make a bandage cover them if they are pierced, and then treat them, as we have said, until they are healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spatula spine from which one makes the fistula is very strong, one part and trenching;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other part no, for this reason one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here: 
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Hemorrhages are according to two manners: 
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	or they are within the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short near blood, and there is one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the top of the foundation;
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are outside have little moisture, and yet inside or a bit of yellow water or a bit of blood, and have the color of flesh; 
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the cure of those who have them inside the foundation, it is that you command the patient to stretch in order to go into chambers, as long as the foundations are gone, and the threads appear; 
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and can hold it with tongs, or you hold it with your finger, then cut it at its roots; 
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the tweezers cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them with cloth, or cotton, or a piece of felt;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them, and powder over some hot powders that are in place of cautery; 
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said or chapter of cautery, then cure them with other treatments until they are healed;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundation cannot come out, then make a suppository for the patient with a biting and harsh suppository to wash what is in the foundation, so that it can come out clearly; 
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	if the patient cannot bear it, and if the threads are far from the foundation, then the treatment is light; 
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and you shall seize them with your finger or pliers and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and he fears the incision by iron. 
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	It is necessary that you administer the suture in this manner:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	Take a twisted thread and put it on a needle, and then pull the thread above and make the needle pass through from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and so be of a wide;
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do so for all others, and leave one to correct the superfluity of blood;
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	Then put on the foundation, a piece of soft cloth in rose oil or cerate, and place it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest.  
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then leave it until they are healed, and when they are closed, cure them with ointment and other cures, until they are well. 
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Of the drying of the veins or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying of humors within the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not work.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If it is necessary to scrape at the point of a spatula or with your fingernail the crust above, so that it does not become moist. 
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	Then cure it until it is cured as it is necessary.  
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	And if it cannot heal, then begin scraping again more strongly than before, until it heals well and becomes scabby. 
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it until it is healed.  
dou fremit	Of trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A foment is a small appearance of pus around the body, and goes well inward; 
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes the vein is found cold, and it feels like death from numbness, and it comes throughout the body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.  
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a stalk of an owl feather, or a strong vulture feather, and put that stalk on the numbness, until the purple circles feel the numbness all around. 
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand on the whole stalk until you wrap all around the numbness, and put it in completely, and scrape the numbness from its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, so make this one of an iron or steel chain according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	Do not pierce it, for if you do it will hold at the vein, and you will squeeze it more.  
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see it, then cauterize the numbness as it is in the chapter of cautery before this one. 
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	Sometimes one makes a clyster of silver or arch-gold, or melted lead or maillet.
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and at times one makes these instruments small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.  
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore those who are given to administer in the care of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the clyster is small and large if it is above wide, or the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and if one has a severance where the belly is tied together, as you see, and the shoulder blade is pierced inside; 
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and has two pierced on one side of the rib cage, and one on the other;   
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and the belly where one puts medicines from a bladder of an animal or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes, and has between each hole one doit of spacing, then put into these holes one strong thread of twisted thread in the shape of an X or otherwise around, and assemble the belly as it is a sheep;
