et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is inside, then tie the end with a strong thread in front, and then clisterize;
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and this is the form of the circle: 
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with clyster of oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then put it in gently;  
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then squeeze the ministers with both hands together until it is all mixed, then withdraw the clyster, and raise the patient's legs to the side, and if the medicine wants to go out, so let it go as much as possible; 
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps all night long, then there is greater help. 
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clench it for a malady of stomach ache, and the medicine comes out quickly, then he starts again until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are at the base or an abscess, let the clyster be as subtle as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle clyster that the skin should be tightened with; 
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have just said in the division the cure of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	Or we will tell you the cures of hands and medicine, according to the accomplishment. 
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to where the wounds are made, and from how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by blows of stone, and the edge of a sword and knife, or spear or club or arrow, or similar things. 
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	Or that are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; 
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And I will tell you the cure of each wound, and will begin with simple wounds of the head, because the remembrance comes in its chapter. 
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, if you guard yourself because it is from a blow of stone or similar things, and the skin is entirely broken and the wound is large, and you doubt greatly an abscess hot: 
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if the head is bled forthwith if it comes little blood from the wound, and let the bloodletting be opposite to the afflicted part
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and avoid the patient's repletion of wine and thick meats. 
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to be bled, then let his meat be lessened, and drink no wine, nor eat any meat; 
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if an abscess comes there, moistened cotton in rose oil only, or in styptic wine; 
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess there, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I shall say a little after; 
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the air has moved it, put on some ointments, until it is healed.  
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large as of a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be assembled by tents, then assemble them by stitching, as I will say for wounds of the belly, of the stitch.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is open to the bone, and hangs, and holds on only by a bit, then cauterize it. 
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	Then heal the wound with medicine, and restore tough flesh in its place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick meats, such as tests and cooked wheat, also pulses, and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rotting skin, and it does not reach the bone, then cauterize all the rottenness, and throw out the pus, then heal it. 
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped without cauterization, and it cannot be stanched by medicine, then cauterize the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if this does not help, then cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then their cure is light:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and it is that you put within this powder which joins as if the fire had melted it. 
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the manner of the powder is: 
pren encens une partie;	Take incense one part;  
sanc de dragon II parties;	dragon's blood two parts;  
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	quicklime three parts, and powder it finely, and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; 
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then bind it well, and leave it untied, if it does not swell;  
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one removes the medicine only when it is healed.   
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with coal alone, when one has neither incense nor dragon's blood, but that the fire has cauterized the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the fire has cauterized the wound, even if it is still open, then one does not put any of this powder;   
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digested ointments or poultices made from barley flour, water and honey, until it heals well.   
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the cure of other cures until he is healed. 
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers; 
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about fractures of the head.  
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this one and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerve, there is nothing else to do but leave it alone and put nothing restraining on it, because it harms the nerve and causes it to retreat; 
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the highest part of the body;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but let the medicine be warm, such as chaulmoogra oil washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cupped laurel also washed in sweet water, and other medicinal stones in this manner, and moist unguents. 
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so sew it together and tie with bandages, then treat until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and she is full of pus, then pierce or lower than.  
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut and blood flows, then stop it, tie it, and cauterize as is necessary. 
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	And if the spine of the throat is cut, or the veins, and the conduit is guarded, so that the flesh goes through, then sew the heart onto the throat bone, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural shape.  
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then restrain it properly, and leave it for a few days, then cure it with soothing ointments until it is healed.  
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then fill it. 
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	And if there are pieces of bone, try to pull out all the ones that you can, and those that you cannot get, leave them until the wound dries up and is aligned properly. 
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wound is fresh, apply the powder as I have said. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if it has bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it's a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, see if air escapes from the wound as the patient breathes. 
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	Then you know that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	And if it is not deep and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put any powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it up so that the blood does not clot, returning to the heart, and killing the patient. 
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	But put on attractive ointment, and reapply it twice a day;  
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	And if you don't have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on their wound for three days, or four, or more.  
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	if there does not come any spasm, nor evil trembling of heart nor straining of wing.  
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good dispositions, then you know that the wound is saved. 
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Treat then with tents and other treatments, as long as it is healing; 
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, and work, then you know that there is a fistula;
si la cure si com on doit.	then treat it as one should. 
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife, and it is simple, or worse, or on the back, treat it as described above.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, suture it; 
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, cover it with powder, and if it is deeply set in the bone, and has broken pieces, then clean the wound, and remove the fragments if they are loose; 
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not severed, let the wound rot, it will lessen the extractions 
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other members judge as we have said.  
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the displacement of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; 
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the great wound sometimes the intestine or the nerves of the intestines come out, by which the intrusion of others; 
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the stitching is more painful, and sometimes the smaller wound is worse than the large one, for this reason one puts the intestines back in with more care, if they are not put back in hot to hot.  
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	for that reason the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, so they go in with more care, and for this reason the middle wound is worse, for this reason one resets the intestine to its place just like the others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to IV manners. 
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The II sutures common occur in the suture of the belly, and the suture of other wounds of the body and II other sutures proper are common to other wounds; 
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And nevertheless they are more clean with the suture of the belly, and I will say one each and declare.  
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine has been outside, and it is necessary to stitch, it is by one of the II manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or for the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is inflated by the cold. 
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	half a sponge or I soft cloth in hot water only, or you cook it in hot wine with cinnamon and cloves, and raise the intestine until the inflammation is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes doing this restraining, it is moved that  it alone for deflating. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling departing, if moist the intestine of water or ale and bad be cooked, for by this it is aligned the entrance to a little thing. 
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a hole in the wound with the instrument of which one cuts hemorrhoids.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first cure is to move the tail, that one should not cut it without great necessity. 
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the tool for splitting it. 
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if trench inside in the curve and outside not, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine has leapt out, set it back in its natural form in its proper place, if you are able, for this is worth doing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part below the belly, then it behooves you to make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; 
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the part below the belly, then put the head and chest higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, put your intention in that the sunken part be higher than the other. 
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it behoves to administer what I say in large and small wounds.  
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	Little wounds are placed where you have appeared, then hold in your hands the minister pitiful that holds all the rupture with his hand, and bring together the lips.  
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	And this is the common way of stitching, and is that you prick a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound one point of space, and there put a needle where it has the good strong thread; 
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	And pierce the two ends of the skin with the two ends of the suture which is under the skin inside, until you make it pierce from that side, and bring together the two heads of the suture the four assembled. 
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then the strain of a double thread around the needle of two parts, then bring together the two ends of the wound in agreement, and then leave one point of space, and there put another needle; 
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then take the thread like you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing so according to what you need needles for, until all the wound is restrained. 
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And let the needles be medium-sized, between fine and coarse, because fine needles cut all the flesh, and too coarse ones cannot enter well: 
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	Therefore, they should be medium-sized.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	And it is not good to put the needles too far from the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	And then trim the ends of the needles so they don't hurt the patient when they sleep, and put tents or cloths on the needle points to keep them in place, and leave them there until the wound is closed; 
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	And this way of suturing with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because only one or two needles are needed. 
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second suture is common, and it is that you assemble the two bones of the skin and the two bones of the jaw together with a needle to which there is a strong medium thread. 
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	And when you have pierced these four bones together, then turn the needle to the part where you began, in the manner one sews the fabrics. 
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each stitch the thickness of a minor vein two;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This suture sews a man, and I sewed a wound on one's belly, which was pierced by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and it had intestines well two palms wide, and the wound was in the middle of the belly. 
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been out for XXIV hours, and the wound was healed up to XV days, and I treated it, and he became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and do not treat him with ointment because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine.  
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and lay on top of the wound cotton old twice a day, and wash it with honey water until it was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing:  
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and pass it from the outside part to the inside; 
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the flesh straight through, lay the head of the thread on the spot where you have passed the needle, and make it pierce from the other side from the inside out; 
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the understanding of this stitching is that you sew as the furrier sews furs, and that you leave the thread on one side once, and take it from the other, until the stitch is completed.  
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second manner of suture, as Galens says properly, is like any wound which joins the two parts together naturally, and applies one end to the other end, in this way: 
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Insert a needle or point of mirache nearby, and have it pierce the place only, and leave the two ends of the suture.  
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle, and have it pierce from the outside part to the inside, with the two ends of the suture. 
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then have it pierce one and both from the outside to the inside, with two other points of mirache that are on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the middle manner of suture and the most common. 
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galens says this word, and no one contradicts it, one must suture the belly with two needles, or there be thread in each. 
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must thrust one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew corrodaries. 
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and know that when the rupture is in the belly, the suture is more grievous than of the other parts of the belly. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as soon as the arterie has moved, then put back the intestine and stitch. 
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put on powder enfearing flesh, and if the arterie has moved, then put on any ointment that is present, as long as the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	And stitch the thread, and join the skin, and the cartilage. 
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then heal the wound as with others, until it is healthy; 
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And if you have no medicines, put on it at once as soon as it begins to fester, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healthy.  
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no need for other medicine in most cases where the wounds are simple; 
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And if you doubt that the wound does not make community with the principal members, it is necessary that you moisten a soft cloth in oil of temperate heat, or rose oil, and put it around the angles, and under the armpits; 
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	And if it feels pain or rot in the bowels, and this happens many times, then you should administer enemas of dark wine, even if the rot comes to the intestines; 
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce it inward, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is torn, and this is because of the placement of the veins that are in it, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the worm jumps from the wound, put it back as far as the intestine, while it is fresh. 
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and has become black or worm-eaten, then you must tie the place that is black so that bleeding does not come from it, for there are veins and arteries. 
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cut what is between the two, and place the two ends on the part below the wound until outside to align the extraction when the worm falls, and the wound bows. 
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people because I have seen a man who was pierced in the belly by a spear;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	And was the wound on the right of the stomach, and was infected and became a fistula, and in it there was evacuation and flatulence. 
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it according to what I could, and did not cease until it was healed, and the edges joined. 
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it join, I feared that the patient had badly in his belly; 
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he felt no pain, but remained in better dispositions, and ate and drank.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And said any experimenter that when it has a small wound in the intestine, that it must be bound in such a manner: 
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	Take fresh strips of linen, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the strip has covered the opening, put it on the two lips so that it pulls its mouth upwards;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	And then the physician cuts the head, and it is held so that it cannot be separated, then he puts the other fragment afterward in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely taken.  
et cout la plaie.	And sew the wound. 
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	That chief if it is ardent in the intestine, and there comes no nuisance to the patient, and one can bind the intestine with a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of a beast, in such manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the chief of this thread of intestine that is well cleaned, and then tie to the chief of this thread the fine linen thread twisted, then put the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it in the rupture.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	And this manner of sewing of fragments is not worse than according to the way of trust and hope; 
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the main intestines, there is nothing nor health, except subtlety.  
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called "fistula," and also when it is closed and goes inward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to truth a knotted fault hard and white, where one feels no pain, and is also pointed like the feather of an eye. 
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in clear bow, and other times thick;  
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small, and other times enough; 
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed and there is no flesh, it is only due to one of the IX causes:  
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the smallness of blood or body. 
ou por sa malice;	or for its evil.   
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the edges, that does not allow new flesh to grow; 
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much moisture.   
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the limbs are spoiled, and the matter is of bad quality. 
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	when the medicine is not good in the cure 
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of pestilence;  
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is tardy for digestion, and tardy for healing, and inflated by nature; 
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones.  
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division. 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is therefore necessary for me to teach you the treatment of fistula which is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; 
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	For there are fistulas that come from the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the sifac, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; 
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it is such that it comes from the property of the principal member, and similar ones.  
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of evil healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance; 
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	And if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you have faith in its cure, and you want to know it, then take a tent of lead or iron, if the fistula is straight, so if it is curved; 
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is twisted, then take a search of a subtle tent of lead, for lead bends and goes around the twistiness;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well search it with tents, then have it clattered through one of the openings, for moisture goes from one opening to another, and purifies it; 
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then search carefully with your power that you know if there is bone or nerve, and it is covered by them, and ask the patient well of the pain that he feels when pressing with your hand, and the place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you will know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the bad matter and corrupted flesh that are within;  
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is well deep from right place, then it befits that you cut it deeper, as much as you can, then put moist bandages in medicinal water, and push them to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity which is lodged at the bottom;  
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put dressings of sound flesh, until it is healed; 
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not healed by these means, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut into it. 
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not touch or principal members, as we have said; 
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, then cover it as long as the corruption is completely removed, then treat with things that create healthy flesh until it is healed. 
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	And if it is not healed and returns bent as before, know that you have not gone all the way. 
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	If it is uncovered and wants to stay bent as long as you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if he is thus healed, it is well. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot reach it.  
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is nothing else to do but leave it to nature; 
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	And if there is a small bone that has rotted, and you can extract it with pliers, then extract it with a suitable instrument for this, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, leaving none behind; 
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	And if the moisture opposes you and there is no error or fear, then cut through both the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, place something on the wound that prevents rotting, and leave it until the flesh around the bones has rotted away, and then they will come out more easily. 
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	And if it is a large bone, such as the leg or thigh, then leave just the corruption until the blackness is entirely removed, then restore the wound. 
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	And if there is a large part of corruption, and it comes up to the flesh of the bone;  
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then it must be cut and covered all the way to the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed. 
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take it as an example and help with your work.   
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, until the substances came to the leg, and it became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no external cause to open it. 
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the mire by their foolishness worked so much that the abscesses opened, and they rotted much matter, and it became a fistula, and there came much pus that all lay raw and moist of the body. 
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many mire they put care to II years, and there was no sage in the art of hands, until I came to them, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they were curing him, and what rotted through the pus to great extent. 
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and it became red the body of the youth, and had a color of citron.   
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I placed a tent in one of these openings, and then I searched all the openings, and found that some came towards each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I hastened therefore, and cauterized in one of the pus until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came up to the inside bone.   
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I was the one who appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and I thought that there was no other corruption, except for the one that I removed; 
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with medicinal sodas for a long time, and it could not heal; 
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I began again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then I took it out, and I was sorry to sew the place together; 
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not more than I sewed around a palm of the bone, and it was brought to its full form, then I restored it with medicines; 
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it was healed and sewed together quickly, and it did not need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who cannot endure, and because of the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For because of the evacuation of blood often, but he was healed entirely, and in the place of the bone grew hard cartilage, and was of good disposition and had no annoyance or contrary from all things, neither to go nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner: 
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take a linen cloth, and tighten it to the head of the bone that is open, and command whoever holds it to extend it upward; 
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	And put another linen cloth larger than the first one, and tie it on the flesh that is above the bone, extending the head upwards, so that you draw the corrupted flesh downward, and uncover the flesh in the place where you want to see, so that the sinew does not cover the flesh;
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And put a splint or a board under the bone to make the corrupted flesh covered. 
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And it must be done as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and to be done again another time.  
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the flesh entirely. 
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then put I tinder underneath, and then silk from one part to the other the corruption, and be the silken thread long as the length of the corruption as we have said; 
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, so cut the corrupt joint, and silk the bone where it contains from the other part; 
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, so there is nothing else than to cut it;  
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is where the finger of the hand, or where the finger of the foot, so it is very strong that thing, but nonetheless you must inquire about that corruption, how it opens to you; 
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and purify it in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or the nerve do not make contrary; 
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the incisors and silks to cover these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of each, and their thickness and their subtlety, and their greatness and their smallness, and their hardness; 
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is necessary to prepare for each kind of work its instrument; 
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of the diseases; 
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so think about the instrument which you have need for according to what is fitting.  
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder can be dislocated either from within or from without; 
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have medicated that corruption with the cure of medicines, and they do not benefit, then it is necessary to cover that limb up to the place where the corruption comes from, so that the patient escapes by this either from death, or by the malice, which is greater, of the lack of the limb; 
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems to be burned by fire, and after the blackness, then comes that corruption of the limb from limb, and takes over the whole body; 
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you hasten to cover it, and if it is by the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and viper and similar ones, if the corrosion is at the head of the arm, then cover it, and do not give him any space to come until the hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes until the hand, then cover it at the joint so that the corrosion does not come to the arm. 
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	And if it comes to the arm, then cover it with the knife.  
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And if it passes the knife, it is death, and there is no use for remedies other than the quantity of its power. 
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	And thus do all this when the corrosion comes or bites;
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	If it comes in the first joint, then cover it after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it comes or bites, then cover the whole bite. 
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up the leg, cut at the knee joint; 
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes from above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the patient die;  
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the way to cut or saw the limb is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister on the lower lien, and others ministers the other lien above, and you sever the flesh which is between the two liens at the spathume width, until the bone is uncovered; 
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cut or saw, and put on each side the drapery of linen so that the saw does not touch the healthy place, and comes to the patient another lesion and abscess caused. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the place heavily, or put on some powders restraining; 
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healed. 
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	And I will tell you that it happened to the man in his foot:  
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	He had a blackness that seemed burned by fire, and that corrosion first came in his heel of the foot, until it spread throughout the whole foot; 
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover the foot, and was healed;  
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And long afterward the corrosion returned to his heel of the hand, and he came to me, and I put on him things that were applied after the purification of the body, and it could not cease the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and it is said that I should bind his hand, and I do not want, unless I have hope of returning the matter. 
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also doubted that if I cut his hand, he would not die, because the virtue of the man was weak; 
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he despaired altogether, and returned to his land, and hastened to bind his hand, and became healthy.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I do not recount this tale for any other reason than that one should do otherwise if one has need of it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes in its fleshy place and remains so long that it makes a great assembly of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and pierces, and out jumps the pus, and remains its vessel, just like a vial.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin that is on top is as subtle as a fine linen cloth, and does not reach down to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called 'healthy', and is not called 'fistula';
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so lengthened that it comes to the bone and makes a hole, then it is called "fistula";  
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure for this is that you cover that skin all around, and also when it is thin, like a cloth;  
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not let it be exposed to its corruption. 
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you have a suspicion that the skin is exposed, and the corruption is not in full depth, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it thus with a clyster:  
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	look if the breast is large, and the bow that surrounds it smells foul, then administer a clyster of Egyptian medicine which is made thus:  
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take equal parts of resin, oil, and litharge, and put them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine becomes red and as thick as honey; 
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And then take of these according to your need, and make it in vinegar and honey, and in suppositories the breast, and restrain the opening.  
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	And let the medicine stay in for II hours, then withdraw it by squeezing. 
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this many times, until the breasts are calmed, and the pain is removed. 
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	And no time is it a suppository of water from ashes, when this medicine is not present, and that you take ashes from vine wood, and pour water on top, then let it drain, and in the suppository, as long as you know that the breast is well calmed. 
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	And if the patient cannot suffer it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water from ashes, then the suppository of water and honey or where there is a bit of litharge ground.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you cleanse it with honey and sweet wine, that the honey may have the property of purifying and washing, and the wine makes the flesh air. 
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the intestines is well purified, then cleanse it with that which causes flesh to be born in it, and that you take a plaster diaphinit, and make it with rose oil and wine; 
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you cleanse it with some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken the properties or treatment of ointments;  
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the opening of the intestine is small, and the tube of the enema cannot enter, then enlarge it with an iron a little, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basil ointment, as long as it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too large, then sew it up and leave only as much room as the enema can enter, and if the opening that spits out blood is above, then cut or more lower where it is.  
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowel is in its proper place, do not let flesh encroach. 
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cover the breast below as you wish, then arrange it in such a manner that the bowel goes to its lowest point, for when the bowel is in place, do not let flesh encroach, and if you cannot cover the breast below as you wish, arrange it in such a way: 
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	that the bowel runs gently downward, and do not leave anything of the bowel; 
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidating medicines to put on the breast, and be above the linen sheet that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cover as forcefully in the place of the opening of the breast a little larger than the first, then be ointment on top of the other sheet according to the quantity of the opening, and put it on the opening of the breast to align the bowel, and do not remove the large sheet outside except after many days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and he who is on the chest through the lung, bone often to remove the bowel, and knows those that run from the bowel, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digestible, or indigestible. 
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take guard if the patient feels pain or none, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been in this manner extended and you see the nature that leaps on the lung through the chest, then know that the breasts are already healed, and approach the saints. 
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then untie it in the morning, or the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other bandage, and renew the ointment.  
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast lies bowed improperly after many days, know that the breast does not heal well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons are cut after a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are men whose healing of flesh in their wounds is slow, and some who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested bowel leaps from the chest after many days, know that the breasts are not healed.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the breasts are slow to heal and are swollen, apply drying medicines moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as ointment diaphinit, because it has a great part of vitriol, and that is the last medicine. 
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take the ointment diafinit, and make it with rose oil, and the aroma of old wine equal in substance;  
puis le confit et en use;	then boil it and use it; 
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and the same way make honey boiled and mixed in, when the ointment diafinit is not present, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it on the honey when it is off the fire; 
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then put it in a cloth and place it on the breast, and at no time is administered one aristeloge long, and roots of lily celestial, which is also as flour of rice and hundred-flower;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and in the use of simples or composites: 
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	grind them and make powder, and put on the honey I have said, and use it;  
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the wound is prolonged, and is not cured by this treatment, then know that the corruption has gone deep, and makes an impression on the bone, or in hard members, or limbs; 
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure of the fistula, as we have said before.  
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the angle
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panaritium is an abscess that arises below the fingernail of the hand, or foot, or by chance may arise in other places;  
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is neglected, and one does not take care of it, then the abscess comes, and rots and breaks open so much that it corrodes the root of the nail, and by chance corrodes the whole nail; 
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And comes the corrosion to the bone, as long as there comes pungent pain, and the head is of the two large, and the color is pale. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, then you must cut away all the superfluity that is remaining from the wound, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy; 
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And if the nail presses against the flesh and begins to prick, and bleed, it is necessary that you put a little cloth under the nail that does not touch the flesh, and push it upwards, and cut that flesh subtly and lightly, and put on the remaining flesh medicines hot and corrosive in order to remove everything;  
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure with ointments until it is healed. 
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it and treat further, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal;  
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the joint is corrupted, cut it with the knife as it has been said before, then treat it until it is healed; 
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is broken and bruised, and the patient feels great pain, then you must heal it first;  
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the joint with the sharp spade by cutting across from above, and guard that the cut does not reach to the flesh which is below the joint, because the patient would feel too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, put something on top that soothes. 
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the shoulder of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints which are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is some where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in any of us of the two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those who are born with no bone in the joint do not move, and those who are born with a joint in the bone may sometimes move;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The waist of a fleshy person is light, in such manner: 
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	the waist at its root with a broad spatula.  
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	He who is born at the root of the joint is grievous to cure: 
si te tien dou coper.	if you hold it to cut.   
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or must be at the last our, it is fitting that you cut first the flesh roundly up to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable line for it, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The seizures that come to the two joints come by birth, or by wound welding, or by burning of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cut that suture so that the limbs repay according to their natural forms;  
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not fuse together;   
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two pieces of fine lead until the joints are fused, as is necessary.  
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a seizure comes upon one of his two hands with the palm, so seize that seizure as it befits.
des vils	of evils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large vessels wrapped full of melancholic superfluities, that come into many members of the body; 
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they happen more in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things, than in others. 
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary for you to administer once purge of oil, and then heal with the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The cure of iron is according to II manners: 
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is that one cuts them and draws out the black blood;  
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you open the vein and draw it all out. 
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The cutting is done in this manner: 
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First, raise the leg in hot water very strongly, until the thick veins are softened, then restrain the leg of the sick person from above the hip to the part below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein in I place, or in II or in III, with a wide incision, then  draw out and draw all of the black blood by hand from one end to the other, as much as the virtues of the sick person can endure.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it, and command him to stay on meats avoiding black coal; 
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And recommence the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and harms the patient. 
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The raising of the limb is according to this manner: 
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Rub the leg of the patient, if there is a lot of hair, then put it in the bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; 
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you have no bath, then heat it at the fire, and then cut the spot on the vein of the long in the knee joint, or below in the part of the ankle;  
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then work the skin with the awl, and peel the vein on each side, until it appears when you feel it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems like a white cord; 
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then push the point below, until it is lifted from the skin, and then you put it on the awl lightly, then cut it in the other place above 3 fingers.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it to the root, as you have done, and place it on another needle, as you have done first.  
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then cut another piece, or more if you need them, then lift it, and cut it at the double point of the foot, then treat and lift it until the second piece.  
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then extract it piece by piece, until it is all drawn out, then cut it.
