et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you cannot draw it and lift it, then put a needle into the whole strong thread double, and tie it and pull it, and put it below the root, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it comes out. 
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and keep that it does not cut, because if it cuts, then one cannot draw it nor lift it, and it comes to annoyance for the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have treated it completely, place on the wound site wool soaked in wine and rose oil; 
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and tend to it until it is healed.  
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and enveloped all together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it crosswise, but do not completely cover it;
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have previously said.  
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to cut the vein should be curved and not straight so that it does not cut into the vein; 
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of a large curve because if it were subtle, it would cut into the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is the shape: 
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in soil that has no moisture;  
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance it is born elsewhere than in legs, and this happens because of rot that comes under the skin, as it comes inside the body serpents and worms, nestled between skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes to the leg a very great inflammation, then it changes its color, and the vein begins to swell out as much as the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the shoulder is open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of plank from one and a half to two finger widths, and knot it, and leave the plank on the leg, and every time there is a point at the outside, wrap around the plank, and knot it. 
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, so you cut a part of it, and wrap around the remaining, and do not cut it at its root, as long as it is all out. 
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, so it goes back into the flesh, and brings forth an abscess and rot there, and bad illness. 
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore for that reason it is necessary that it be treated piece by piece until the head, and nothing remain in the body. 
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And sometimes this vein when it is treated with V palms of long, or X, and one man came to me once whose it was X palms long, and when you cut it, it throws out I rays or porous, and it pierces until the bottom, so that all flows through; 
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And be emptied of the matter which is within, and administer at the place medicines preventing rot any day, then cure it as the abscesses. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes at this vein main veins, and also when it opens in the joint of the foot, or foot, and there comes out much of porous, and from which it leaps out. 
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Cure therefore as we have said before.  
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land “disease of the ox,” because it happens many times to oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body up and down, and one feels it well at the edge of limb to limb, until it reaches the skin where it goes, and leaps out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by the rotting of some humors, such as come to worms and rubbish and roundworms in the belly 
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one doubts its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance it enters, and destroys the eye; 
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens many times.  
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cured and milked, one cannot flee except when it goes: 
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so it behooves you to tie the place above and below with a strong linen tightly, then cut on top and milk it forth, and if it goes into the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrodes the eye, as we have said; 
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it coming or near the eye, then restrain under it the eyebrow form, then cut above, and the wound treat. 
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And it is necessary to use the patient with purification of body and medicines solvent for the ill humors corrupted, and avoid foods that cause putrefaction. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This illness is called in our land "vakir", and is a pain that comes in some members, and then moves from member to member; 
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I see what I tell you.  
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; 
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and I poked after, and I saw it rise as a worm to the shoulder, faster than any thing, like living silver when it cuts from its place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain departs from that place and goes into the shoulder, and then a little while after it spreads throughout the body, until it comes to the other arm.  
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then she told me that it returned again around her body, as I saw it. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I never had seen this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I wanted to move the pain from that place to another, but I didn't want it to happen, as I saw it in the woman. 
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins were exposed, and for that reason appeared that constricted windiness.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and did not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate and have moist bodies and veins covered. 
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see curing this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then place the hand on top and below gently, and then cup over until that constricted windiness in its place is gone. 
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the place; 
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat it with those who drive out wind, such as foul pills and  seraphim pills, and similar others. 
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are some with large points, and small ones, and hairy, and soldered; 
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those which have two angles, and those which have tongues, and those which have pieces; 
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and those which fall in any member if they fall according to two manners:  
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in principal member such as brain, heart, liver, womb, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members.  
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls therefore in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I shall tell you hereafter, appear to you:  
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	Then it is necessary that you guard yourself against the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many cases; 
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then treat it, and cure the wound.  
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and leaps the syphax which is above the brain, is when there is scotomia and sode and esvertin and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and permixtion of understanding, and vomiting of phlegm; 
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps it is without being stuck in the nostrils, or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps loses speech and voice; 
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jumps from the wound moist white like to poultices, and jumps also as if burned flesh;  
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, so hold from the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not inside.  
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it lies in the chest, are that it is near the left nipple, and it feels as if it were lodged in a hard thing, not hollow. 
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the arrow moves as if it were the finger, and a dark blood comes out, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore know without doubt that death ensues. 
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that pierces low is that without plains of foam jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the hip, it is near the small ribs.  
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and throws great pain and great suffering and sighing; 
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and it moves all the members of the shoulders.  
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls or stomach, by chance it jumps from the wound any thing of undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and there is no point of sinew by the intestine rout, then there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine leaps out and comes out, and the patient feels great pain: 
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Know that the wound is mortal.  
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arms and neck and throat and shoulder and auxiliary and spine of the back and thighs and hips and legs, and similar members, are safe according to more dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for that you do something else.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man with an arrow which fell into the root of his nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and I drew it from the other side beneath the fat of the ear, and it was cured without feeling at all. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I drew it with a tool an arrow that fell in the fat of the eye beneath the paper and beneath, and the arrow was renewed, and I could not reach more than the tip toward the shaft, and the arrow was large as a Turkic bow, to all the iron light without ears; 
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The wound was healed, and he did not have any bad accidents.  
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And treat an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears:  
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I removed the barbs, and skillfully extracted it as much as I could, and the Christian was healed. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And treat an arrow to the man, that he had in his belly, and thought he would die;  
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after XXX days, he did not improve his condition; 
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, and I gripped it, and extracted it fully, and there was no bad accident.  
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if this man who had an arrow lodged in his back, and the wound was closed above; 
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and remained the arrow inside him, and did not change his natural conditions, nor felt annoyance in any of his natural works. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And behold another man, to whom an arrow struck his face, and his wound was closed.  
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and he remained thus enduring great pain; 
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar things. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And there happened an arrow to the prince's man,  the king, who was lodged in his neck, and was slightly declining toward the right side; 
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was wholly embedded. 
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to the cure after it had been lodged for three days.  
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I sought it with a very subtle probe, and did not feel it at all; 
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and there was a feeling of prickling and pain below his right ear.  
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought that it was from the point of the arrow. I placed upon its place a plaster atractive and digestive, for that the place did not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and appeared to me the wounds of the arrow. 
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put the plaster on that day, and sutured the wound directly, and kept the patient there for a long time, until he felt the arrowhead inside his flesh. 
et il le me dist.	and he told me.   
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put on the wound a corrosive medicine for several days until it was open, and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow which hardened in place; 
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I adjusted in the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow appeared visibly;
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it took four months to penetrate well, and then I widened the wound so that I put in pliers, and grasped it on both sides, and it couldn't issue;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	then I did not cease to devise and engineer ways of instruments, until I took the day with pliers well made, according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, until I drew it out, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the wise judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: 
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you apply your cure to those things which I do not say, because the books cannot contain everything. 
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But the wise masters compare with very little things, and on those which are present and lacking, find new work, and new instruments, to the advancement of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that the arrows are not from the members where they are fixed further than according to two manners:  
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either by the place where they enter, or by another part; 
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which is further by where it enters, is an arrow entering into the flesh, and never being pulled out at all now. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not move now, let it stay until the pain is gone, and let the wound be cleaned.  
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot move, let it stay so for some days, and move it each day.  
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then if it moves, and if it does not move, pierce around the entire forest subtly, until the area around is enlarged, and then treat it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient:  
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	Do not treat it, but let it stay until it is healed after some days, because if the arrow comes as far as the pia mater, then death will follow. 
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not fixed further than in the bone only, and does not come to its tip, and the patient stays for some days without bad accident, then the machine of the milking.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very tightly fixed like this and cannot be moved further, then administer hot poultices around it as I have told you. 
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the place until it is sound.  
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is returned to its place in the body and if one cannot see it, then cover the whole wound. 
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then treat it with no suitable instrument;  
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot by the widening of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves or veins, then widen it as much as the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears at its base where it holds, then remove the flesh that is stuck from both sides to as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow as much as you can so that you can extract it.  
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful that you do not break the arrow, but that you extract it more easily. 
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then leave it until the surrounding tissue is softened, then treat it, for extraction is easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood is against you, then administer what we have said about its treatment in our chapter;  
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and guard yourself from the incision of the nerve and the vein, and put as much care as you can to extract the arrow without risk, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and put the patient according to the form that he was in when the arrow hit him, for this is the greatest aid that there is, and if you cannot do so, then put him according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, where one sees or feels nothing clearly, or the skin is swollen in that place: 
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Then cut there, as much as the pincers can grasp, and then extract it:  
si saut fuer maintenant.	If it leaps out now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then drive it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be pulled out, leave it still, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out.  
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if the shaft of the arrow is there, pull out the whole shaft: 
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	And if the shaft has broken, and you see to administer medicine, then administer the instrument that is shaped like a hook so that the point of the arrow goes into the curve of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then pull it out, and if the arrow is broken, insert the instrument with its tip entering in to aid in extraction. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the wound is surrounded, it behooves you to cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then cure the wound as it is fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls or in the belly or to the bladder or to the ribs, and it is close, and you can cover above, then hit it; 
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And guard yourself from covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if need be;  
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the care until it is healed. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of an owl, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways of this: 
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	Large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.  
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form of the blunt point is like the feather of a bird, to put at the tip of the arrow, as here it is the form.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tongs for inserting and holding is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Of veins from which one is healed there are XXXI, so it has or head XVI, that is to say: 
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two bats that are after the ears, which are called the two "herbesch";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	And the two arteries that are in the two temples apparent; 
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is removed from the forehead 
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is on the head near the nose;  
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two veins that are on the neck; 
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augueherich"; 
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are below the tongue.   
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins in which one commonly bleeds are  V in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and is on the inner side of the left arm, and the common people call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the vein is called "faste", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilica, and the lay people call it "vein of the heart"; 
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilica is located on the right side of the chest, and the lay people call it "vein of the belly", and it is on the fossa, and it is the one that is used to draw blood, which opens clearly on the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the cephalic vein is the one that is between the thumb and the little finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and foot there are three veins: 
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one of which is under the bend of the pouch on the left side of the chest, and the second saphenous vein which is at the ankle on the right side; 
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein that is called "femoral", which is in the ankle of the other side; 
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and on the other leg there are III veins below those 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bloodletting of the veins that are after the ears so helps with old catarrhs, and migraines;  
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of the bloodletting, as I tell you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then tighten the patient's neck with a rope, until the II veins appear behind the ears in their two dependencies of the head: 
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	which then to your back, and where you feel the pulse below your back, so seize with your hand;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet, and insert it below the vein to the bone, then lift your hand to all the vein above, and cut through both the skin and the vein well two fingers deep, and make blood flow as much as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then restrain and bind, until it is healed; 
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book.  
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The draining of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for old migraines, and for sore eyes, and for habitual eye pain, 
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the drainage are as I said:  
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and that the patient strains his neck until the two veins appear openly; 
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse below his shoulder, and then signs of  it. 
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then gently raise the vein towards your right index finger, and insert the lance below it, and lift the vein upwards, and make the cut, just as you did with the other two veins, and draw out blood according to your need. 
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then untie the patient, and place your right hand over the vein for an hour, then put cotton on top;  
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then form a bandage, and leave it until it is healed; 
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And we have already spoken of their cutting and extraction, as at the beginning of the book.  
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The vein of the forehead is as valuable as the cephalic vein for ancient facial ailments, and for migraine, and for redness; 
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is that the patient strains their neck by twisting it, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument which is called “digger”, whose form is here: 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and steady it with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see; 
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then tie the patient's neck, and tie the vein as long as it is saned and never work with a wide flame. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it does not suit that the flames are too large;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the saining is across, because the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flame when it is subtle. 
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	Staining of the two veins that are in the two tear ducts helps with the eyes, and the nose, and the throat, and at the root of the eye, and with diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the qualities of their staining are that the patient strains his neck by twisting with some lien, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then heal it, and let the healing be through a traverse, a prick of the long flame a little wide, for there is no flesh there. 
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flame is subtle, perhaps it breaks.  
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then make a correction with blood, as much as you need, and then tie it up with cloth, and tie it well. 
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The healing of the vein in the nose is good for a runny nose, and for sore throats, and for face ailments like migraine and redness that comes to the face, and even when it is old. 
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	And the qualities of the healing are that the patient tightens their collar, then strains their nose with their left hand, and takes a subtle long flame, and inserts it between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well in there, and the blood will now begin to correct.  
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not let them move too much, and make a correction of the blood according to your need, then tie it for one night, because it is very quickly restored; 
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And that is the form of the flame: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The veins of the two shoulders help in the treatment of lameness, and in the beginning of rheumatism, and many illnesses, and epilepsy, and corrosions, and herpes, and tumors; 
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the qualities of the vein are that the patient strains their neck underneath both, as we have said; 
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and let the master be standing above the head of the patient, and the patient sitting on a stool, then prick the vein of the long one a little widely, then draw blood moderately, or as much as is needed; 
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then do the other side in the other vein, then untie the bandage, and restrain both veins moderately so that the patient does not strangle; 
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let him rest until morning so that the wound is healed. 
de la sainie des leivres	of the vein of the leaves
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the lips above helps to heal in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and wounds of the gums and tongue.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the healing are to make the patient sit in front of you, and restrain his neck as I have said. 
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by those that are black, and by those that around them have small black veins. 
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Therefore, cut both of them, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest one on each side, and in the same way with the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the vein below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The healing of the veins that are below the tongue helps after the cephalic bleeding, and it is at the stricture of the throat, and to the diseases of the eye, and to the diseases of the mouth. 
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the vein are that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and lift the tongue, and look below on each side a black vein:  
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then prick both, and do not go too deep in, for beneath them are the arteries. 
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the arm which are commonly pricked are pricked according to two manners: 
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or they prick at all the flame of the middle wide, or olive subtle as you cut trenches, and is called 'anesil'; 
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the wideness and thinness of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame is very well known, and is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary for opening the veins with flowing blood that appear large and that contain thick and troubled blood; 
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive trench:  
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more subtly pointed, and is for bleeding the veins subtly, where there is subtly yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with ailments that are under the throat, and neck, and chest, and abdomen. 
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is proper for the one who performs surgery that he operates skillfully, and that he avoids the artery which is below (it). 
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, then it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said; 
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and should not be pricking the flame, but cutting as one would with a knife. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then it is necessary that you restrain it, and change another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you want no vein of it, or you operate in its place the vein in the arm: 
elle apert manifestement;	it opens manifestly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and with the flame cauterize, as we have said.  
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see to know the place of the wound, then it is fitting that you stretch out the arm, that you touch the place as much as you know the pulse. 
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with ink, and then tie up the arm, and cauterize the vein with the flame as we have said. 
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and guard that you do not wound the artery when you see the place inflamed, for it is from the artery.  
eschui la donques.	Therefore avoid it. 
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it surge upward as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery. 
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hasten then, and put your hand on its length, then remove your hand if the blood ceases, which happens many times.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	He raises his arm, and leaves it so, and does not move it the patient.  
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be without fear, and do not move it until it is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the wound is not clean and it hurts, and the medicine is not present, then close the artery if it opens, because the head of the vein. 
et estainche li sans.	and cleanse the wound.  
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a rind of fig, and cut it, and take one half and bind it well until the next day. 
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	If the blade is unstained, this is good; 
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If not, cure it as we have said, with powders that stain blood. 
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stains should not be grazed in more locations due to the small size of the wound and the position of the arm's ligament. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The vein's blood in the middle helps because it treats blood from above and below, due to its composition of basilary and cephalic veins as we have said; 
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it is important for the patient to lie with their leg toward the nerve that is below, and if they are not too far apart, he finds the nerve and it swells and the healthy parts are grazed, and by chance it cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	And this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any man due to its subtlety, then you must feel for it with the instrument; 
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and escape the nerve to your power. 
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The bloodletting of the cephalic vein helps, that it draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes; 
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to bleed by pricking at the olive vein or the myrtle vein, because this is the safest of all veins, because it has neither a nerve nor an artery.   
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lighter spot, and do not worry if one must do it the first time, and one begins again; 
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance it swells the eyes for some men, even if one does it the first time, but it does not harm them.  
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of blood is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing that you must know about bloodletting is that it is administered only to maintain health, and to expel future diseases;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and may the bloodletting be done in one of the III veins which are or count: 
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	That is to say, cephalic, fasted, and basilica. 
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must bleed at the beginning of prayers in the morning, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; 
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one must bleed the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.  
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	Blood letting administered to the sick has no set time, but when need is of day or night, at all hours and in all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it does not behoove to bleed children until fourteen years old, nor women carrying fruit from the fourth month until the seventh. 
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Those over sixty years old should not bleed.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when some want to be bled, in whatever manner, it is fitting that they cleanse the bowels with a light enema, if they have much phlegm retained, so that the veins do not attract superfluities from the intestines harmful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor does he heal well who is too full of meats, nor who is drunk, as long as it lasts, nor the dropsy. 
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if it worsens after pain in the gut, vomiting and rumbling of the belly, and multiplication of labor in women, and childbirth, of watching and fasting, and that which weakens virtue, whether by weapon or by body; 
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then purge the humors, if it is swollen, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the power. 
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then bathe him, if nothing hinders, to purge the blood, and heal the vein around the third (of the body), as we have said.  
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep him from work, and pain, and lust, and similar things.   
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be healthy and joyful, and let the one who is healing be higher than the one who heals him, and rub his arm two or three times, then restrain the bandage on the middle, for when it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct the swelling.   
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the place with your hands, until the veins swell, and you feel them; 
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then moisten the veins with a drop of old oil, then put his thumb of his left hand on that vein below its place one fingerbreadth where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not burst and be injured by the iron. 
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that bulge like cords when bleeding, and some that are full of windiness, so that when one puts the lancet on them, they retract from the lancet, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these. 
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, so that those who bleed should be wise in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens the first time, it's good. 
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If not, if it begins again a little under that place or above gently, if the joints are not swollen 
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the joints are swollen, and the patient is in distress, let him leave it for a day or two, and do not tie up his arm: 
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	for perhaps abscesses will come to appear.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Do not enter into a bath, then resume the treatment if he wishes; 
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that it is not as much blood as you see, then pierce into that opening itself throughout its entire length straightly; 
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work a little gently, so that the joints become swollen;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	because this happens many times when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place swollen, then do not resume the treatment, and put on a little bit of oil from olive, because it heals the body from blood, and is effective in this place, the grease that comes from the olive;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer the linseed in each vein that you bleed them, to stop the flow of blood. 
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	And this same thing is applied and bandaged when it is put back in place; 
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	so subtly the bandage and spread when it is too large.  
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes an abscess large, which happens often, even when it is only bled once and the opening of the vein is small, then hurry, and put on top a sponge moistened in water and some oil a little hot, and restrain it for an hour. 
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And it is necessary that you do this after the bleeding of the vein, and if it remains in place for some days afterwards without any blackness or greenness, it does no harm.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see it, put on top nothing of aloe or frankincense remixed in the juice of calamine,  or similar. 
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times abscesses and appearance to the basilica's healthy:  
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Place your hand then upon it, and if you find the place soft under pressure of the hand, so is that appearance bad.  
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Therefore eschew that you put upon it nothing of what we have said, because by chance it may close without the artery.  
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	But let him cover with dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed. 
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound with blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if it is black, let it be left so until it is red;  
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	And if you see it large, let it be left until it becomes thinner. 
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if it is too hot, let it cool down.  
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for him who is lean and frail, and needs the extraction of blood, one should make a wider wound, and let the flames be wide; 
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it befits him to bleed often, and he must be bled by cutting across, not by pricking. 
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this manner of bleeding is saved from the diminution of blood and cutting of nerves, and it is worth more than bleeding from the long or wide.  
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for him whose body needs bloodletting, it befits to give moistened bread in pomegranate juice; 
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is hot, treat him with bloodletting three or four times. And if he is of a cold complexion, before the bloodletting, give him moistened bread in muzzy syrup, or in honey aromatic syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it pulses at the vein, after the outflow of much blood, it is necessary that he moisten broth of flesh, and fragrant syrup, subtle, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to empty his arm, and bleed another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bloodletting, that he bleeds a little and a little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And he who wants to drain his arm after the first vein opening, and he has strong flesh, then heals VII hours after the first vein opening, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to bleed from another side, they must bleed the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For he has much blood within the body that is already hot, and brings on fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if it is necessary to draw a large quantity, and widen the opening until it falls in pieces.  
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	since you treat all the conditions of its health, and put your hand on his pulse when it is healthy, that death may not come in place of pieces, and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent. 
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it does not become when you see a dislocated arm, and make blood flow the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press hard on it.  
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	but if it is crooked, he should extend his arm as much as possible, because that would be bad; 
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let it remain until it heals the second time.  
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you will prick it with the tip of the flame, until the blood that was frozen at the opening of the vein comes out, and put on the piece of felt laid in sharp, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity is to bleed a second time, then in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein of the arm is bled at the place of the vein of the head because it is composed there.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of the healing is that the patient puts his hand into hot water until the bone is red. 
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then it is bound moderately so that the vein appears well, then the healing now through the middle, neither wide nor long. 
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And let the opening be wide, and be healed well near the joint of the hand, and if he cannot move out, put the hand back into hot water, and leave to draw the blood in the water until you have enough. 
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is in summer, then do not put the hand back into hot water, because one puts it more in winter than in summer. 
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the healing of this vein is safer than all other veins, because there is no artery nor nerve. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The healing of the vein of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, if one sees it. 
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if it heals crookedly, and if you cut it completely through, then it will not cause harm; 
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	And do not move it too much, for the nerves are all uncovered from flesh, and then put the hand in warm water, if the sinew is frozen in the wound, and cannot issue out. 
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you will have treated of the blood as much as is necessary, then put on the vein oil and wool to soothe it well, and thus do for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein of it in the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse, and do as I have told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the sophene is good for all illnesses that are below the body, such as diseases of the knees, and retention of flowers, and illness of the hips, and thighs and legs ancients, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the qualities of its blood are such that the patient puts their foot in hot water and rubs on the vein until it perspires, and ties above the joint of the foot. 
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many veins;  
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Blood therefore flows through the larger vein, or at the ankle, where it merits more. 
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you bleed on the foot, guard yourself from the nerves that are beneath, and the bleeding should traverse as when cutting. 
et soit li flaimes anesil.	And let the flames be applied.  
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the vein cannot be drawn out, then put your foot into the water, and let the vein flow well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the bleeding is necessary the first time, it is recommenced the second time above a bit, because the place is salty. 
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so do of the same sort from the other foot equally. 
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic is at the ankle of fury, and its pain reaches to the pain of the hip when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the qualities of his vein are that the patient enters into or bath, and withdraws above the ankle four times by twisting, for otherwise he does not open the vein. 
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if it opens, so draw the blood in all the ways that you can, and across. 
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is better that you cut it, because the vein is dry, and it is much replenished in men's hands. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, so draw blood from any vein that opens on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and guard against the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	And do so much blood drawing as you see fit, and then untie the ligature, and put on cotton and restrain it.
ele est maintenant sanee.	She is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	of the suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Suctions are made of horns, or leather, or glass; 
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and suction is done in two ways: 
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.  
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this suction which is without pricking is done in two ways: 
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either with all fire, or without fire;  
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and suction that is done by pricking and drawing blood is done in fourteen places on the body, so one is entirely at the top of the head; 
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are in the neck; 
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others on the two ribs of the neck;  
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the suction under the chin; 
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the suction on both shoulders; 
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction cup on the hips 
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the suction cups remove them from the arms
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the suction cups from the two legs; 
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the suction cups from the two ankles;  
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the suction doesn't treat blood, but only small veins that are spread throughout the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken one as much as bleeding from a vein; 
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not proper that it be administered, neither with hot nor cold fire, in any illness that comes from repletion, as long as the whole body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illnesses it is necessary to suction, or for customs, then we administer each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and remove and in every instance;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are some who, when they need to suction, have a heavy head; 
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if to those who have swelling and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in their eyes;  
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and bleed from it;  
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are those who dream, and see through blood and dizziness and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is removed from the month, we command to ventilate after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The vein of the temple helps with the great pain in the head... that comes to the eyes, and it is not proper for this to be after the evacuation of all the body;  
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this ventosaion is in the place of the vein of the cephalic, and it is not proper for those who are of cold constitution to use it, or who have a catarrh, because this does great harm to them;  
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for those it is not proper that the elderly use it, nor who have or cold diseases of the head.  
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it, often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to put the suction cup a little lower down because of the fear of obliviousness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The cauterization of the neck is in the place of the vein of the head and of the basilica, and for that reason it is good for the treatment of the hip, and for cutting open the channel of the groin, and for all ailments, and for suppuration. 
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is proper not to put pressure too hard on it, because if it is held too firmly it can cause blockage in the stomach or heart. 
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The cauterization of the two ribs of the neck is good for pains in the head, and ophthalmia, and migraine, and to relieve strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the vein of the basilica. 
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is proper that you command the person being treated to press their hand on the spot so they don't cut the artery and bleed excessively.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The cauterization below the chin is good for mouth ailments, and gum disease, and similar diseases that are in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and is in the place of the II lips. 
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for illness coming from heat and fullness.
