Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The bleeding of the veins with the knife is as good as three arm veins because it draws blood from these large veins; 
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the patient not to bleed too much with it because the vein is bare of flesh and knows only nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The leech that is on the rump is worth as much as hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for diseases underneath, and it must be that the leech is large, and be of iron, so that it has the need to well suck.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and perhaps, if it were thin, it would break; 
et i fai grans plaies.	and it makes large wounds.  
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The leeches on the legs are applied openly because they draw blood from the whole body, and are worth old pains of the reins, and of the bowels, and of the bladder, and soften tumors;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are located in the place of the two hip joints, and the two ankles, and nonetheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring about pain in many positions. 
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The manner of putting the suction cup is that you put it first empty, and successively, and put it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not cease to do this, until you see the place red and inflamed, and appear the redness of blood. 
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then put it on fire, and replace the suction cups, and take heed to the arrangement of the bodies, because there are some who have tender flesh, and clear pores. 
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	so it is fitting to wound once only, and it is fitting to make wide wounds, and a deep hole.  
et suce legierement.	and suck lightly. 
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the abscess is large, it is fitting to wound twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to subtly open the vein of blood thick 
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to strike the third time;  
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to drain blood little by little, then we prick only once. 
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, we begin again often; 
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the vein is thick, strike it deep, and the end is that the hairs be pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for him who has thick and hard skin, and who has open pores, that you apply to their place the leeches of oil aperitif and dissolving: 
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in this case, of violet oil, or of almond oil sweet, or of the oil of cucurbit seed;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in winter, of watercress oil, or of lily, or of chamomile, or another similar one. 
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are large and cold, then take oil of wormwood, or of balsam, or oil of rue, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one who is being healed has tender skin and large pores, one should not put any oil on it, but it should be washed after ventilation with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, if he rises from it, or from myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large superfluities raise them with old wine, or with their own water, or with a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things. 
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And it is not suitable to draw blood with a cupping glass before bathing nor in the bath, but after the bath for one or two hours. 
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And he should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he get up when he needs to be cupped, and when he has been cupped. 
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware those who are being treated, who are choleric, and if their blood is too thin and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	If it is necessary that they eat cold things, such as pomegranates and chicory and lettuce at the meal, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and minced pigeons, and goat meat, and moist meats. 
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, let him take syrup of honey, and scented wine, which is between old and new, and millet, and pearl barley, and small sparrows, and pigeons. 
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day that he will become feverish, he must drink more than eat.  
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give no man at any time triacle or musket before the fever, or after, in order to comfort the main limbs; 
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And be subtle with the sweat, but it is not necessary that those who are hot drink it.  
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cupping glasses that are put without hurting are those that are put upon the liver and the stomach and gout, and upon the belly and the breast and the hips and the groin, because these members do not suffer to be hurt on their own, and it is done only in order to draw blood from member to member, just as we put them on the nipples when milk comes in. 
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	In order to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just as we put cupping glasses on the belly and breast to reduce the size of the member.  
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and bone pain, when there is an ulcer or stone, so that by its virtue it attracts the ulcer, or displaces the stone from its place.  
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and thus it is done when one puts it upon the liver and upon the stomach when there is wind held back, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; 
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with tepid water, such as in diseases of the lungs, and in this manner one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water where herbs suitable for it have been boiled. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it should be two palms wide and half a palm in length, and have a small hole on the side towards the middle, as if to insert a needle, and be of iron, so that it does not turn cold before putting it upon the member;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And in the middle place a rod of across from iron or rain, to put a candle in it gripped, and be they great and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them. 
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the leeches of children are other than the old, and the thin ones than the fat ones.  
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And thus one must put this leech upon the limb. 
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Taking the candle of wax or linen, and putting it within the leech across from the rod which is within the leech, so that the light be at the bottom of the leech so it does not burn the patient; 
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And then put it upon the limb, and these must be upon the opening that we have said, so that when one wants to, so it goes the vapor, and one removes the leech; 
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And take again the linen as before, and begin it often, if you have need.   
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup therefore which is administered in the illness of pleuresin, to all acute, it has no stalk nor perforation, and is not administered further than when it is full of water, and is placed upon the member only so much. 
et c’est li forme:	and this is its form:  
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suction cups are not administered further than in members where one cannot put suction cups because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar ones; 
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in their wounds of flesh, such as two or nails, and other similar things;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the qualities of the user are that when you find suction cups that are in clear sweet waters without perforation, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them one by one in sweet water, until they become accustomed, and have nothing in their bellies; 
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	And then let it be cleansed by vein-letting and cupping, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on a poultice; 
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are smooth, and fall, if it is their place where one can put cupping, then put it, because it does much good after. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If that is not the case, raise the place with a light hand, and then water, very well, and then sprain it. 
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the place heals too much after the poultice, then moisten a linen cloth in cold water and put it on, until the swelling subsides. 
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the swelling is multiplied, then put on crushed vitriol or gall and similar things, until it subsides. 
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or put on the place half of peeled beans, and let them stay there until they dry out on the place, then it will stop now. 
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more of them, take other bandages. 
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the bandages do not want to be taken, rub the place with fresh blood, or you insert a needle there until the bandage comes out, and then put them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will harden. 
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are sticking, sprinkle a little bit of aloe and flaxseed powder on top, or ash, they will now stick. 
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is restoration of fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear child, that the fools who rely on this chapter will never see any of the ancient books, nor read any letters from them.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason the science is being lost in our land, because I never found any good ones
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing about it, except through the science of ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have mastered the science, and by experience, and by the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and have abridged it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are brought, as I have done in these two chapters before. 
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It therefore behooves us to say in the prologue of this book the sums of the words and the chapters where the sages place their understanding, and remain on the truth so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and learn it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to cure the patient on one side and the other, if nothing prevents it, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; 
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the tension is not very well, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and avoid cold things, that is to say cold meats, and meat of deer and goat, and do not drink wine, and do not eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with meats which fill the veins with blood, as long as you have a doubt of hot abscess or expansion of matter in the limb; 
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient returns to his first governance which he has used.  
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make great nourishment, or which have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and testes, and feet, and entrails of veal, and eggs, and fresh fish, and thick wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such twisting they are renewed and more quickly healed fractures.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones broken of the old and decrepit do not well rejoin nor solder according to their nature for the dryness of the members, nor those also which are too tender, as bones of little children; 
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but never mind, instruct upon the broken bone, the big tendons which hold it together and join the limb together, as long as it enforces itself as it was before; 
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and for this reason, you must feed him with thick meats, as we have said.  
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg, or of the arm, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to a point, and others when sharpening, like the nib of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture to a whole small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And to every manner has his engine, and his instrument proper in the restoration, according to what memory comes in its place. 
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and is known the fracture of the bone by those that the place is twisted, and opens well outwardly, and  is felt at the pressure of the hand. 
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no torsion nor son at the touching, and the patient feels no great pain, there is no fracture. 
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have torsion, or fissure, or small fracture.  
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it does not suit that you move it by hand, but put upon medicines which come after here, and then restrain it subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that goes in a circle, and the two parts are disjointed, it is necessary now to put them together equally, so that an abscess may come at the wound;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if an abscess comes at the wound, then you leave it alone for no day, until the abscess is quieted. 
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then put it together carefully and skillfully as you can, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restoration of that one where there are pieces. 
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then restrain it, as it is fitting here afterward.   
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are pieces broken, and they are two parts, whether it is hand or foot, or in your hand if it is one small limb, or two cords, or to one cord and to your hand; 
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, you move them by all means to their places as much as you can, and keep that by your work no injury or pain comes to the patient. 
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.  
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well by hand if it seems to you that it is not well. 
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if you straighten it well, and do not restrain it too much, nor press as those who cause it to come from their work abscess hot and contraction in the limb, as we have often seen. 
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, instruct the patient well that he does not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor by turning, nor in any other way.  
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take good care that the limb is so assured that it does not feel any pain.  
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, it is not in place, and it should be put in such a disposition that it does not feel any pain.  
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is placed straightly, that twisting does not come when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.  
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in size and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar things: 
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	so it is necessary to wrap bandages of soft and fine linen;  
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those which are large, such as hips and thighs: 
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	so it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and stiff linen, because the broad linens embrace the whole large limb, and restrain it from all sides equally, so that there is no gap;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then bind it with light splints, III turns or IV according to the limb, and restrain your hand a bit on all the length, then go above the break and restrain it less, that the break then move away a bit. 
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the splint little by little, until you feel most of the healthy part, then take the other splint, and turn it back right above the broken place; 
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then go down to the part below the break, and restrain it moderately, neither too strongly nor too weakly, as we have said in the first place above; 
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the splints padding of linen or cloth, until it is all equal, then tie everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made dressings on top, if there is no abscess or swelling. 
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is a swelling or abscess, put on a soothing poultice for the abscess, which takes away the swelling, and leave it so for some days. 
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain a piece of the  half of a good length of chain, or of a staff from which they make the cloaks, or of palm branches, and let them be according to this figure. 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the piece which one puts on the fracture be a bit larger and broader than the others;  
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and let it also be as long as is needed to the limb of small or large size; 
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then strain on the pieces as you did in the first binding, then bind above with a thread evenly, just as in the first binding above the fracture. 
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	more tight is it above, less; 
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the thread be medium, not too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen 
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in works of fools who make their stitches with cords of twisted linen, and that is a great error, for the stitch cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it is not right that there be less than two fingers' width between each stitch. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the bones of the shoulders after the strapping in their healthy parts, then put under them compresses of linen or wool felt so that it does not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the bones are broken, I will say its cure here after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not proper to tightly bind all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the member is large, it is not right to put stitches further than after five or seven days, or more according to your certainty of abscesses appearing hot.  
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and see here the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: 
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take flour that clings to the walls of the mill, and you mix it with plenty of egg, and put this concoction, neither too light nor too thick, on top, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring fracture in many cases, even for women and small children, because it is not too hot nor too cold. 
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another way of a plaster restoring fracture and dislocation and torsion: 
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take one part bardos bark and  celandine and wormwood and asafoetida and arabic gum and  mugwort, each ten parts; 
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloes, each five parts; 
alechil VIIII З.;	and alechyl nine parts.  
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	And make it into powder, and mix it with the white of an egg;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the complexion of the man is hot, so use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones well, and is worth to many men. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another way of plaster that is worth for torsion:  
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take mugwort and wormwood, each ten parts; 
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloes, each nine parts;  
acaice VI З.;	and acai six parts.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Boil Armenian X, grind it well, and confection with water or yolk of egg, and administer. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way to treat joints and bones dislocated from their places, and soothes the pain that arises, and the use of bone, and the fracture: 
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take new linen, and moisten it in broth and oil, and put it on the place. 
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore [the body], but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and properly takes away the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to treat that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dry fig leaves, and earthworm leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of emplaster for the restoration of the broken bone and to lessen the remaining of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of wormwood, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of chickpeas, one part each;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind, and confection with wine, and if the limb is sun-scorched, confection it with moist coriander water, or water, and use it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to set a bone more firmly than the first, when an abscess prevents the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of wormwood, and seeds of flax,  balm, melilot, and saffron, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all one part. 
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind, and confit with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras says in his book that one should put on the broken limb a restorative made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen one must put on the broken limb, to restore, things dry and a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way of plaistering that is good for the wound and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take moth and chaffinch feathers or owl feathers, wormwood, and flax, all equally, grind them together, make a plaster and apply it. 
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then loosen it a little after, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if not loosen it by hand again for several days. 
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching,  lack of rest, or swelling, then hasten and loosen it, and remove the plaster at once. 
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And take a light cloth, and a sponge of wet sea, and dip it in water, and lift the spot up, until the itching stops, and the pain is soothed. 
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry cloth, moistened in water or rose oil, and tie it with a bandage, until you are sure of hot suppuration. 
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	And rest the inflammation of the limb, and the pain is gone, then begin again the subtle poultice, and a little bit of plaster, and do not bind it as tightly as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and continue until it is healed.  
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess has pus and redness and pain and swelling are all there, and you need to apply poultice and linen, if it begins again, just as you did at the first doing.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the limb, then do not unbind it for three days or four or five or seven.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and sometimes leave it for 20 days, according to what one sees, until the fracture sets, and approaches the alignment of the bone above; 
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then restrain it more than before, and thicken its flesh, as I have said before;  
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see it drying more than is necessary, know that numbness cannot come there; 
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	apply then a warm water bath, every time you loosen it, and that be each third day, and slightly remove the dressing; 
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	by this work therefore comes numbness to the limb, and corrects hastily those who foolishly make it stiff again;
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	it is bad, and this work is dangerous, and I see no other thing than to leave it and work it straight.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various manners of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of fractures are, and various figures, and the causes are destined. 
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For there are fractures that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the collarbone every bone up to the side which is below the bone, as it is made high or low; 
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	And for this reason, this kind of fracture is called "haichure".  
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	When the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; 
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And the wound of these two fractures great or small. 
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is impacted percussion, or fissure or of neck of stone, or of heel upon stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a fracture piercing, which approaches up to the membrane that is beneath the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound that is rejoined in the bone as fine as a hair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason, this fracture is called "capillary"; 
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound that is made either by hitting with stone, or by falling, or by similar thing, and makes enter the piece of bone inwards, and is the  place like those who make the braziers when they heat on the cauldrons; 
si entre li piere dedens.	if between the stones within 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have or whose head is moist bones, like that of a child;  
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and happens in all these ways of fracture that small pieces are separated from them like stars; 
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak of it in its place.  
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures by pulling on them, and the questioning with probes, and by the rotten flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair capillary is known by this that when one has uncovered the bone and rubbed above it, the black fracture opens.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of a fracture, take care of accidents in the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of blood, and emission of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever with chills, and eyes red and bulging, and other similar things in more dispositions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an unavoidable accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the latest that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this is the case, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the cloth under the bone does not rot, and the accident we have mentioned comes about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone comes as far as the membrane that covers the brain, then it is necessary for you to split the fractured part thus: 
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and it is that you  press the head of the sick man down and uncover above the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound more gently than you can, and if a discharge of blood comes when uncovering the bone, or an abscess forms, then help them with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the place with cloths soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and make the wound rest until the pus sack is quieted, and be assured of blood clotting; 
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to remove the bone, and it is done according to two ways of work:  
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one way is that you cut at the narrow section in front, and this is the form: 
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he puts another piece larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second manner is that you have a number of cuts of different sizes, some narrow and others wide, and pointed, and some of iron: 
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and in work lightly, so that you do not  break the head. 
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is  hard and strong, it is necessary that you pierce it around, so that you administer cuts with saws, not too deeply so that they do not go beyond the soft part of the bone, and it must have above the point a margin or circle that does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you must have more than one, so that each comes in its place of the species of bone, so that you may have targets for all tests.  
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the form of the three kinds of targets: 
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The qualities for perceiving around the broken bone are that you put one target on the bone, and turn at your two [joints] until you know that the bone is perceived. 
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then put the other target elsewhere a little after, and do this all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do these more subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as forceps, pliers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and keep that you do not touch the brain nor the spinal cord. 
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you will have the bone pierced and treated, it is necessary that you reset the apparatus which is stayed from the bone to all other instruments seeming to an incisor, but it is necessary that it be more strong and more subtle than the other incisor. 
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if there remains nothing of the small bones, nor any scales, then lightly lift the bones with the instruments;  
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then cure the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other manner of work is that which Galen says, which is drier; 
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and it works very well, and that is his word.  
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears moves, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will put beneath the head of this lenticular incision, for this is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut on one side, and let the part be acute in two costs, so that the cutting is towards the bone; 
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike with a small mallet on top, so that you lightly strike the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth that is underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is stuck to the bone, gently remove it, because one removes it well without pain, and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not reach to the skin, and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces, it is necessary to rere that asperity, and remove the scales with a fine rasp which you must have various quantities, to administer in each place the most suitable, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If one shaves before with a large razor, and after with more subtle ones, and does not cease doing so until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair cuts and subtle breakage, it is fitting that you bring a cause according to its arrangement; 
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this thing is not returned to anyone who has put his study into this art. 
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is uncovered, it is fitting that you take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and put it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this more lightly than you can, so that you do not harm the flesh, then administer above the other linen, and do not restrain it more than so that it holds the wound only;  
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and let it so for one or two days, until the abscess is calmed, then untie it, and administer medicines such as roots of lilies, and flour of verveine, and powder of incense, and arnica, and similar things; 
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and of these things make powder, and put it on the wound, and administer additional medicines mixed with no stinging.  
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and guard that the wound be always clean, that you do not leave any ointment, nor allow it to gather pus, because when pus gathers on the cloth of the brain, it corrodes and pains, and brings great evils to the patient; 
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one puts on a biting thing such as this, it stings upward  
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed therefore, if no evil accidents come to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if the blackness does not come out except through the medicine that has been put on, because it has virtue, then you must take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix one cloth with it, and put it on the sting.  
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it in ways of treatment as is fitting until it is healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes the two parts of the kneecap break above or one only, because there are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and the lower part is cartilaginous and does not break except if it is bent or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must put your small finger or the opening of the kneecap, and place each fracture inside your index finger and to the pouch on the outside, until the kneecap returns according to its natural shape. 
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and watch that the patient does not feel pain from your work. 
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the cheekbone and it cannot come to its place, then it is necessary that you put it even with the head of a stick a little thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of two parts, do it again, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can. 
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscess is calmed, then bind to the head with two tents of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part. 
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you bind it on the other side, if the fracture is there.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	And let the tents be so large that they fill the openings of both.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said any restorative one must moisten the tents with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be moistened in the preparation of auburn of an egg and powder of mill. 
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the tent until the bone is hard, and the cartilages hardened.  
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes one puts or lays down goose feathers in place of tents, and if it's soft cloth draping around, and it holds the burn, and blows on the patient. 
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Or do what you wish.  
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the new while you work on it, put a cerote or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in the pock of diaquillon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess comes, put a plaster on the outside, of sesame flour and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk, then put light compresses on top, and bind it not at all.  
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the bone is small and it is broken into small pieces, then you extract it with suitable instruments for that, then suture the opening, and treat it with appropriate things like flesh, and soldering, as well as plasters and ointments suitable for that.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it has no wound inside the bone, treat it with tents and put splints in them until it is healed. 
de la routure de la mandibule	of the jaw fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated down, and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is only outside, and is not broken in two, except that it is splintered inside, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right part, that you put your index finger in the mouth of the patient. 
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is in the left jawbone, put your right index finger there, and gently push the fracture inward, and with the other hand hold it from outside, and make it even. 
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is displaced into two, it is necessary that you administer extension to both parts, until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if movement of the teeth or a rupture occurs, then strain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, and then put a certificate on top of the broken jawbone, and put on a double cloth.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And put on top of the cloth a large bandage well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jawbone, and tie it above as much as you can, and command the patient to rest, and eat light meats. 
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the figure changes, untie it on the third day, and then put back in place what has changed. 
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And put a plaster on it, of powdered mill with plenty of egg or sesame flour, after you have removed the pus. 
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	And put a light linen plaster on top, and if the plasters are dry and the patient's condition does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy. 
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times is healed in three weeks.   
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together,  reward oneself, no piece of bone is removed. 
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if subtlety you have instruments suitable for this. 
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you will have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, sew the wound, if it is wide, and put on its top bandages suitable to those, so that it may hinder flesh, until it be healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The collarbone breaks many times in front, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or she is broken and severed in two, and there are pieces, and it is the lighter to restore.  
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	where there is a fracture with a wound. 
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is so when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the helper who feels the fractured force. 
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the part. 
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then place the fracture equal to your two, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance nor defect. 
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend further, so place under the shoulder of the patient a round ball of cloth, or wool, and be thick according to your need. 
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and extend and lightly the force, and hold the ball in your hand, so that you place the fracture equal, as it should be. 
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the bone out by force because it comes embedded, it is necessary that the patient lie on his back and put below the shoulder the lower edge of the arm, and push the minister's shoulder down, until the bone of the collarbone is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then address the fracture to your two hands, and if you find it fragmented, it is necessary that you cut above; 
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and treat the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join by any raising, then cut with one of the incisors that you have;  
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but that you place under the forceps this instrument, to guard the eye. 
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and seems like a spoon, and is not too pointed, and be also as wide as it is necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; 
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and have two cheeks, as you see, and be one wide, and the other narrower, as it is the break of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; 
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are assured of the hot abscess, so cover the wound, and if the break is small, or you doubt about hot abscess, then apply to the wound of cloths and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses come there, moisten the cloth in rose oil and asel and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The setting of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put on the bone the plaster of the powder of the mill and of albumen of egg, and put light bandages on top, and put a sphere under the saddle, if you need it; 
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	then take a very wide bandage of one palm's width, then put it draped double over the poultices, and bandage them. 
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a strip subtle of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandaged one, so that the head of the bandage hangs down. 
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and put the strip over the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the healthy shoulder, and under the injured shoulder. 
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and bandage each part, and when you see that the strip holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the strip does not move over the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the ligaments loosen, then restrain them.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on his back, and put him when he sleeps a small pillow under the shoulder, to raise the arm. 
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	If you want to lighten the fracture of the shoulder by setting the shoulder, or tie his arm to his neck, and do not untie it unless a bad accident happens, up to 20 days;  
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then re-apply the splint, if you see that he needs it, and restrain him and leave him like this, until he is restored. 
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And it is restored in the most at 28 days, and in less to no one.   
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It happens that the shoulder breaks or its bone does not meet in the middle, and one cannot feel it except by touch. 
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	So arrange it according to the shape of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form, in every way that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then put on its place powder of the mill with abundance of egg, and light dressings, and put on top a double cloth. 
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then put on top a broad and subtle strap, a little larger than the shoulder, and if the strap's edge is uneven anywhere on the shoulder, apply those bandages of linen so that the strap lies evenly.  
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then restrain it with a whole great bandage firmly, so that the strap does not move from its place, and look at the linen each day. 
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time it softens, restrain it, and put the strap evenly if it is out of place, and make the patient lie on their side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	And the shoulder is restored in twenty days or in twenty-five. 
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is accomplished, untie it, and be sure, for it is not bone that is put out lightly. 
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is exposed before and not under the heart, do it like this, and the bone, and do what we have said in the fracture of the collarbone to soothe an abscess hot.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the leg
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; 
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the end.  
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the midst, it falls downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of strength, and cough, and perhaps vomiting blood, and opens the channels in the broken bone, and it feels warm to the touch.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and you put a cushion between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulders together, and assemble the ribs of each rib with your hands, and carefully bring them together in all ways that you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; 
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then put plasters and bandages on top of the broken bone, a subtle salt poultice or some other light substance, and wrap it in cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so that it doesn't move; 
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the bandage around to the back, and tighten it well, and reward every hour the linen, and if it becomes loose, tighten it. 
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it behooves to untie it, for corrosion or for itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten and untie it, and scrape the area, and dress those who have come from ways of care.  
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then reset the area, and restrain it as long as it is healed. 
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the fracture of the ribs comes only in those places after the back, and at the head inside, and they bend only for those because they are brittle.  
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and one feels it well upon inquiry as two. 
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you put the fracture even, as it behoves.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on the splint, and restrain it with a strap if you need it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inward, the patient feels great pain and sharpness, as well as from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane. 
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and along with pains, and coughs and vomits great spitting of blood, and this is of grievous health, and the ancients have put much remedy in it.  
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is necessary to administer meats that swell the belly, to drive the wind outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, except that boils come when they haven't.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes to him, heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they said any one of you put cupping glasses on the place, to suck them strongly, and it seems right.  
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	Nevertheless, there is doubt that the cupping glass does not draw the superfluities to the place for the disposition of weakness.  
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said of each one that one should cover the place with wool moistened in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make even the heat around it, then be cured from the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure because of the bone which pierces the skin, and there is doubt for the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put underneath a instrument to guard the liver. 
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then one must trench the bone, and drain lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with ointments, until it is healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if an abscess comes, then put on a cloth moistened in rose oil, and put it on the place;  
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat while the place of those that it is necessary for an abscess, and lie still on their side where it should, until it is healed. 
de la brisure dou col	Of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a fracture occurs to the bones of the neck, and sometimes it happens that it bends; 
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also to the spine of the back.  
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, if you take heed if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he feels nothing.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.
