Know that it is mortal in many cases, and if they move and feel well when being pulled and straightened, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if one puts care into it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healed or not, then take note whether the feet are softened, and if the limbs that were affected are now in hand, and on the back there is airiness and involuntary evacuation; 
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when one has laid it on its stomach, then there is involuntary evacuation.  
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is placed on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is mortal: 
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if you do not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then it is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that you warm it if there is an abscess hot, so put on the spine rose oil or oil of egg yolk, until it is appeased; 
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters, and tie it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest. 
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.  
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone is broken, it is necessary to cover the wound. 
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And remove the bone, then assemble the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, and then treat it with ointment that helps to close the flesh, until it is healed.  
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	And if the bone of the shoulder is broken, which is called "the bone of the cow," put your fist of your left hand into it and place it even with the other hand at your power, then put the plaster and splint on top, if you need it.   
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then restrain it, and if there are broken bones, do the same, remove the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed. 
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It happens sometimes that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it has happened, it should have been a little bit lessened at the top;  
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and make it long and sloping towards the outside, and comes to the patient pain at the place, and tingling, and swells that which is broken. 
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you stretch your hand above, as long as you are on the breakage; 
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and know which one is the breakage and the form of it;  
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the breakage is only at the top, put straight that breakage, as long as it is in natural form. 
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or it bends inwards, then make the patient lie on their belly, until the restoration of that fracture is apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you would have put it straight, put above the plaster, then put above a splint of wood or of heartwood, and restrain the breakage, so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and place the part under the ribs, until the limb is equal. 
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his healthy side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if an abscess comes there, do not touch it, until the abscess is healed, and put on what we have said before. 
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to restoration, and restrain it as necessary, if there is no bad accident; 
et c’est li maniere.	and that is the way.  
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder is that which is between the shoulder and the head of the shoulder blade, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two ways:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is that you take a piece of smooth wood, according to this form: 
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And bind the two parts with two bindings, and raise them upward, and place the patient on a seat;  
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	Then when the bone of his arm is broken above the armpit, and there is one curvature of stick, then he may lie on any heavy thing or let ministers stretch it down.  
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then put the splints to his fracture even with his hands together, until the fracture returns as it should. 
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that one supports the patient on his head, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands the two ministers that one holds those who are above the fracture with their hands, and the other holds below all the limb, and extends each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, restrain the limb below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the ministers to its side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the fracture is near the top of the shoulder, then it is necessary that you put one splint under the armpit and the other towards the side, below the fracture. 
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And also if the fracture is towards the side, then it is necessary to put one splint lightly, without effort, until the fracture is even on the level, and on the side. 
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then put the fracture even as it should be, and restrain it, if an abscess does not come.  
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if abscess comes there, do not restrain it until VII days, and put on a half linen in oil and rose ointment, until the abscess comes to be appeased. 
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then restrain it, and the manner of restraining it is that you put the splint on the break, then assemble the arm upon the assistant, and put your hand upon the shoulder or upon the breast.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put the sheet, and restrain upon the assistant, and upon the arm, so that the arm be in its place of stars, if no thing prevents you, or if the bone is not moved. 
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone is not moved, then use splints, and put on the break a splint larger and stronger than the others, and have between each splint I do of space, and be each splint so great that it passes the break III does of each part. 
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then restrain upon the bones, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the bruise, stronger and less in distancing.  
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the setting of the bones, and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the heat abscess, then leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said. 
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then look every three days the bandage, that itching or swelling does not come to the place, or the dressings cannot come to the limb because it is too tight. 
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if none such accidents come, then do not unbind it before three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands upon his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and put under the shoulder one cushion of wool evenly, and look each hour of the day or night that the form of the broken limb does not move, or be softened the bonds;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	If it is addressed by the virtue of medicine, and he is given the food that we have put forth, in such a way that the food be at first subtle; 
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And when it begins to recover, let it be thick.  
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be taken back in forty days from all; 
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one must untie [it] and administer bath and medicines of ointments for the place to be addressed.  
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and impeded, it remains to untie for 1 day or II months.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "fossil," because one is small, and that is the one following the pouch; 
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and that is the one below, towards the small toe.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	By chance broken the large fossil only, or the small one, and by chance both together.  
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small bones are broken, restoration is easy, and healing. 
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	And when the large ones are broken, the healing is bad, and more grieved than when they are broken together.  
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then it should be gently extended and made equal.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is the large bone, then it must be pulled harder; 
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and stretch it over the cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small ones lower than the other bones, and let the patient be crossed upon himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, that the patient may not suffer any labor;  
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then extend the ministers of his arm to the lower part towards his hand, or on the limb, and one other minister to the other above.  
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he puts the mirror even, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, place each one in its place, and if any is detached that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, do as we have said before on the bone.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; 
si pren la cure.	Take care of it. 
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if at the beginning of the restoration abscesses come out, then glue the covering of cerate made of rose oil and white wax, that it be neither too hard nor too soft; 
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and tie the covering gently above, until the abscesses are calmed. 
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the cerate, and put the plaster of ground flour with plenty of egg white, then place the bandages, and let the bandage of the crushing be a little more outwards, and one piece wider than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that he must have VI arm or arms in more arrangements: 
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or in II;  
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and restrain more above the fracture than elsewhere, and every day less by moving away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter;  
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the bandages that are on the fracture be soft and moist, and be neither hard nor rough; 
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread, with which it is restrained, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.  
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accident comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then it is necessary that you raise the limb with hot water until the itching is appeased; 
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb not be left too tightly restrained.  
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin again the tightening, and if the ligaments are loosened and the bones dislocated, and similar things, so the address.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care that the nurse can't come to the limb because it is too swollen, then you must soften it a little, and leave it like this for some days until the swelling subsides, and then constrain it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not unbind him until XX days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	Or when he is turning, then he places his hands on his neck, and let his neck be straight, and guard against movement and agitation, and sleep on his back. 
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And know that this sprain is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty, according to the constitutions and complexities of the humors. 
de la brisure de la main	of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and as well the palms many times have a few fractures, and there comes nothing but swelling many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the plant of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient sit crossed and be straight in front of him equally. 
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then he puts his hand on the board extended, and extends the ministers the broken bones, and places them equal the eyes, until they are well joined.  
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	And puts the plaster and bandages, if an abscess does not come, then he puts a splint according to the quantity of the place. 
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and be enveloped in a linen sheet. 
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is at the root near the belly of the plant, make a ball of cloths, and instruct the patient to press it against his broken limb. 
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then fasten it with a long cloth, and let the poultice be as large as the hand of the limb, and bind it as is fitting. 
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the forearm, then you must place a splint on top and another below in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand, and close the ligature between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture comes to any of the bones of the leg, if it is the tibia, set it straight as is fitting. 
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and bind it with the limb, and if you see that it is set a little crooked to raise the fracture, and do not move it. 
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	And if the fracture is in any of the other bones, such as the index finger or another, set it straight and tie it with the healthy limb that is next to it. 
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you bind them all together while he is laying down, or put it on a splint like our pouch 
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and arrangement of a hot, dry abscess, and treat those who come to it, as I have said. 
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the hip is often broken, and one can see this well when it turns front and back; 
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and its restoration is done by tying the part above the break, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his face, then extend each minister his band to his side evenly; 
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the break is set in the bone.  
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the hip, one ligament should be pulled towards the groin and the other ligaments below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is close to the knee, then let the bands be near the knee, and the extension below; 
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Then put the eyes of the bone even with his two hands, until it is according to its natural figure, and then put the splint, and tie it, if abscess does not come there. 
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is an abscess hot, let it heal then return to your work and your cure; 
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The ligature is made in this manner. 
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you envelop on the bruise a doubled bandage hard in two or three, and remove the superfluities, then turn the leg until the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and put the long thread between the hip and the leg, below the knee, and bring the end of the thread upwards; 
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then turn upwards on the leg and on the hip the bandage, then put on the bruise splints, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; 
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then apply the place eight between the leg and the hip of drapes soft to put even the tightness, then commence to tie strongly three or four above the fracture; 
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and when more goes up above the fracture, and less the restraint;  
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then understand as two joints of the thread that you have put between the leg and the hip, and in tie three knots that are above, then return below to the head of the thread, until you come near the foot; 
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and the restraint, so that it does not move from its place, then let him thus, then since there comes no abscess nor swelling nor other semblance.  
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens, then untie it, and address what comes, as we have said many times; 
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are pieces of the bone that prick, then it is necessary to cover them, if one can;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot, then it is necessary to split the place and draw out pus. 
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And treat it as we have said, until it is healed.  
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes the thigh bone is broken in this way, as in the shoulder and arm; 
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	However, with this restoration made, it does not harm the patient.  
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the  hip is restored in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the varieties of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee there are few fractures, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is no longer but a fracture, or opening, and it happens to all wounds, without wound, and everyone feels this well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is this: set equal those things that are broken to their halves, as long as they can be assembled and moved together;  
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then put the splint on it, and put a round plaster over it if you need it, and restrain it as is necessary, then follow all the precautions that we have said in other fractures, such as hot poultices and similar things.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and apply to each accident what is fitting for it, until it is healed.  
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, because one is called by right "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; 
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and there occurs all the fracture as it comes to the arm, and for that reason the restoration is like that of the arm equally, and the work is all similar. And if the two bones are broken together, the leg turns in all directions. 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, turn it back.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it can be seen well;
et torne desoz.	and it turns downwards. 
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Therefore administer extension, and put it straight, and tie the splints equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but nonetheless, it is necessary if the fracture is bad, and there are many pieces, that the extension be less and lighter. 
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and the splint according to its virtue.  
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two fasces of felt that wrap the leg on one side and the other, and be long from the knee to below.  
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	Then wrap them in two bands above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this juncture, the leg will not be able to decline to the right or left, and thus it is well. 
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	And none administer one bears along the length of the leg, and if it is felt, and it put on the leg to prevent movement, and properly made these in the fracture or where there is a wound. 
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	And move each day the leg, to see if there is a hot abscess or other accident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if it cures as long as it is sound.  
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the breaking of bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but at the bones of the foot there is sometimes a fracture and at the two toes, and there have been very few in more dispositions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if it happens that the bones of the foot are broken, and you see these bones overlap each other, then put the patient's foot on the ground, as if he wanted to walk, and then put your foot now on his, where the bones are raised, then press it until they return to their places;  
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then put the splint and pads above it, and place under the belly of the foot a small board at the shoulder plain, then restrain it to the foot evenly, then that you have wrapped bandages around it, and other things that you need. 
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when III days or IIII will have passed, untie the linen, because you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there are any of the bones broken, restore them, as we have said about the bones of the hand.  
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then put on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the bone, and be a little wider, then put under the foot that board that I have said, and restrain it evenly. 
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	And if there are two or three, or more, broken, put on each bone a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in one linen cloth, and restrain the board under the foot.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And let it be standing on the top of the board above the belly of the foot so that it holds it well. 
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said.  
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And take care of each accident as it is necessary. 
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of the woman's body is broken, make it sit wide open, then incline it to the back part, and be held behind. 
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	Then fill the hollow of the patient's body with cotton, and put in as much as there is space for it.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	Then untie the woman, and raise her back up and down, and then push the cotton inward until it reaches the entrance of the body, and return the bone with it.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has finished, put it back in, and do this for seven days or so. 
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	If the fracture will be restored, and if you see, take a bladder of lamb, and tie to the wound a chain, and put all the bladder into the nature.  
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the chain's opening, until the bladder is inflated inside: 
la nature si revenra li brisure;	Then nature will return the fracture; 
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then fill it with cotton, and leave it so for several days until it is healed.  
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the hand of a man or woman is broken, restore it thus as we have said in the hipbone;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And these fractures near are not concealed from him who puts his study and use to it, and understands my book. 
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture signifies in many positions the right way of restoration:
enten le donques.	Understand then.   
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the shaft, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and put it into the shaft. 
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap bandages around it, and let it be for three days or until healed, and it will be healed quickly. 
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for someone who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bones of the hip or shoulder or similar, that they be healed now, so that the dressings that we have said testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healing, then keep the vitriol, if you have nothing else, and then begin to restore the fracture in the same hour, or that day, if an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses come there, let the restoration wait until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would bring a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is appearing on the uncovered chest, then you must put it back together lightly with your hands, with small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension is not ready for you to put it straight with your hands, then reset it using this instrument which is of iron, which is seven or eight finger lengths long, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound; 
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this purpose the one who works it must dip it in three or four, according to what he needs in each case of a broken bone.
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and it should be round and slightly thick, so that it does not bend under compression on the limb during your work, and it should be wide in front, and thicker from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And is called "palainche", for which it is necessary that the shoulder head be placed on top of the apparent bone; 
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and push it once, until it returns, and be equal one against the other. 
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well take hold of the bone, then it behoves that you cut the head of the bone, as long as the instruments have purchase.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, then with the edge of a suitable instrument, either an incision tool or saw, to your power; 
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then remove what is remaining in the bone of asperity and small splinters. 
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	If you do so until it is in its place, then soak the bandage in dark, astringent wine, and properly this is what happens. 
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put anything on the wound, neither cork nor anything else that has oil, lest it cause rot and corruption.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	Then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not strained with the fracture. 
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times this has been done foolishly, and it has brought about death or corrosion on the patient many times;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and let the strapping be softer and less forceful than for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident may happen there, as we have said, and you find pain at the place, then it is not advisable to put stars on it. 
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	But enclose around it, in lieu of stars, hard cloths, and tie them.  
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two that the wound is starting to bulge, then remove what you have put on top of all wine, and put ointment for healing wounds, such as ointment tetra-formation and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you untie the limb two times a day, the morning and evening, as long as it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be supported in such a manner that the bow be corrected down gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if for many days it does not heal and cannot return to its place, know that there are small pieces of bone, so you must cover the wound with a bandage, and remove all these dislocated pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or any other manner of corruption, then you must treat it according to what he says in his chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the bone of the hip or shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not pull it out, for many times death comes from it, but let it remain until it rots. 
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	Perhaps it will fall out by itself after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can;  
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if you cannot, leave it alone. 
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Of boils which come from the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often come after the health of the fracture, even when it is near the joint, and it is an ugly thing to see the figure of the limb;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and perhaps cannot make the limbs their natural workings.  
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take heed then if it is fresh: 
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	If it is fresh, administer topical medicines such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, a spice, and similar others, in the way you will apply any of these things, or all together, and confit them with astringent wine or with an egg white, or with ash;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	And place it on the wound in poultices, and restrain it well, and do not unwrap it by hand during the day; 
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then remove it, and begin another one, as long as the swellings are removed;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you restrain upon a well-made piece of cloth;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the properties of linen is that it removes all swellings from limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	And if the knot is already converted into hardness as a stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut above it, and make the superfluity appear. 
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And you let her rest on no razor until she is removed, and the care as long as she is healed.  
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the bone fracture is restored, and afterwards the limb remains weak and thin, it happens for many reasons: 
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	because one is because it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should be;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there were too many bandages, and it cannot come to the nourishment of the limb; 
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or for a multitude of dressings;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or for too much movement, not at the right time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because he has little blood in his body, so it is weak. 
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the care is that you make the patient eat, and make the body soft, as long as the blood is multiplied in him. 
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	And administer baths to him, and give him joy and mirth.  
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	Then put pitch on the limb, so that the pitch attracts to the great swelling, and rose water often of tepid water, as long as the swelling corrects to the limb. 
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And returns to its natural shape.  
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of member wrong after the health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after the restoration, and the bones broken apart, and the form of the limb is ugly, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function: 
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	so do not believe fools who say one must break the limb anew, and many foolish people have done this in our land.
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this work is blamed, and brings great harm, and by chance death. 
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	However, if the nodules and pain are fresh, it is necessary that they be soaked in hot water, or herbs softening are cooked, such as leaves of wormwood, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; 
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	And you apply a softening plaster, such as well-made diachylon, and you take the poultice of wormwood, and cook it with lard or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top. 
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	Or you take fat figs, and grind them with flaxseed, and similar medicines that reduce swelling. 
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes is dislocation removed by continuously rubbing and lengthwise with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be exercised movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the tumor is old and hardened, like stone, and the need is to remove it with iron, then it must be covered until the bone, with a sharp scalpel lightly.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put cushions and padding in the treatment. 
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is from any joint out of its place, because of which it cannot move, and the limb is poorly shaped, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, then it is necessary now to bring it back without resorting to splints.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one delays, then the limbs swell, and perhaps if one puts it back in place with pain. 
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	For this reason it is not proper to move it while it is inflamed. 
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	Many times brings on pain and other aches;  
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	Nevertheless, when this happens, if it is healthy for the patient, then let him remain, until the abscess is calmed. 
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and heal each member as it comes back to its place. 
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It happens that the jawbones are dislocated, and these dislocations of both sides are according to two ways.  
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	Or they are a little out of their places, and softened a little; 
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Or they are entirely dislocated and hang towards the chin, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor close his mouth, and surrounds his tongue with speech.   
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by many more disarrangements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is whole and complete, then you must reset it gently, and do not complain. 
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	And in such a manner that the ministers hold the head of the sick person, and put their fist into the root of the jawbone dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; 
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	And the other hand should be outside, to make it even.  
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And instruct the patient to soften his jawbones, and move them in all directions.   
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the broken bone is placed even, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if it is brought back with grief, even if the two jaws are together, then apply hot water and oil, as long as you gently reset. 
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	Do not complain about bringing it back, as we have said.  
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back evenly, and the patient's mouth is tightly closed without softening, put on moistened cloths in a cloth made of rose oil and wax, then tie it gently with soft bandages. 
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient sleep on his back, and his shoulders be between two cushions so that he does not move them to either side or strain himself in any way, but eat light food until the pains are gone and the jaws are joined. 
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then chew what he wants lightly, and do not try to open the mouth while eating and drinking until the jaw is well joined and healed. 
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour, and are not brought back to their places, then fever and accustomed sweats come, and perhaps a solution of the belly, and perhaps vomiting of cold phlegm.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is a perdition. 
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times he who has it dies, in nine days.  
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The harness cannot dislocate from within the side and hip, and it is dislocated no times outward, and it is well felt when it is.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient lies quite on his back, and extends his arms; 
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then presses the place with the palm of your hand, and it will return.  
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put on the splint and bandage, and restrain it; 
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the head which is towards the shoulder cannot dislocate.   
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it does not, and if it dislocates any time, reset it to its place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put on the splint and bandage, and restrain it, and command the patient to rest as long as he is sound.  
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And in the same way is brought back the head of the scapula when it is dislocated from its place. 
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways. 
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	That one is when it dislocates to the side of the axilla.
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	And the second is toward the breast. 
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	And by chance it dislocates upward, and this happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	And it does not dislocate backward for the shoulder, nor inward towards the nerves. 
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	And many times it dislocates toward the axilla, even in those who have little flesh, for at these the bone is easily moved. 
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	In those with enough flesh, it moves hardly, and returns hardly. 
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men percussion or fracture, and swells the shoulder of a hot abscess, and believes that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	Therefore, you must carefully examine it until you are certain.
et adonques encomence la cure.	and therefore begins the cure. 
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known dislocation when it is moved down towards the hip, and make a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a manifest diversity. 
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and below the hip touching the head of the shoulder, as if they were one piece.  
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring their hand back to its nest, nor move from any movement. 
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upward, it is not hidden, because you find it manifestly by touching. 
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this manner of dislocation is not difficult to bring back, when it is new, or if the child is sick. 
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the manner is that the ministers lift the hand of the sick person upward, then put their fists below the hip, and lift the joint forcefully upward to its place. 
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the ministers lift the hand, and extend it up, then put it below;  
si venra hastanment.	if it comes hastily. 
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said in hands just after, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water;  
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the minister put on soothing and softening ointment, such as a decoction of elder and fennel and marshmallow in water, and it be applied; 
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then the patient be laid on his back, and under the  seat a piece of felt even, neither too soft nor too hard, then put the foot of the patient on the stool, and lift the head of the shoulder skillfully, and pull the hand of the patient; 
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another minister hold the head of the patient, so that it does not move down.  
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	That shoulder returns all now, and if you see so reset it according to this manner: 
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and is that you make be present a man who is greater than the patient;  
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and is right toward the side, and put his shoulder under the seat of the patient, and lift the seat up so that the patient hangs in the air; 
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and other ministers pull the hand of the patient down toward the belly.  
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can carry with him anything heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And reset it also in another manner:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and is on place a long stick in the earth, whose head is as high as the bed, and is not too big nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then is placed under the patient, but that it has drapes above, and the patient is standing on the length of the staff;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then extend his hand down on one side, forming, and the joint will return to its place quickly. 
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	And if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this cure: 
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	Take a splint of the arm of great size and four fingers wide, which has the head round so that it may enter through the armpit, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	Then tie above the head of the splint with strips so that the splint does not press on the patient, then put it under the armpit of the patient; 
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	And extend his arm above the splint's long, and tie the shoulder to the splint, and the arm at the hand's head, then put the arm on the step of a wide plank, and let the hands down and let the body hang down on the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joint returns now.  
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever manner it may be, it is fitting that you put under the collar of a sphere of wool equal, then put the plaster parilliet of powder from the mill, with incense and auburn of an egg, on all the shoulder and around, then strain under the collar evenly, and turn the linen on the plaster, and embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he moves little, as long as the limb is fortified, because it will heal faster. 
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then move more after seven days or seven, and move it.  
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And if it is stiffened and it is not softened, then it is healed. 
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come, or for another cause, then it is necessary that you administer cautery to three holes, as it is shown in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all these things, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift his arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; 
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.  
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is toward the buttock, and the breast, or back, it is made by impulse, and stretching of hands, and there it is administered in another place.  
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and care until it is healed. 
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing pain comes to the limb, and slowness in movement, then the patient uses many baths until that pain is relieved, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the arm
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joint of the elbow is dislocated in places, and in places returns; 
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and it has been dislocated from all sides, and even in front and behind, and the dislocation is not returned, because one sees it well and feels it well; 
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and dislocated according to each shape. 
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased knife with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary that you reset it thus as the abscess comes in, because if the abscess came in, it would be grievous to reset it; 
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and by chance it cannot be reset completely at all, even when it is at the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	so it is worse than the other dislocations, and causes more pain, and by chance it comes to death. 
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is, when it is like that one can reset it, that you extend your hand to your two hands; 
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And his arms should be spread out, and the hands should touch each other according to the edge of the knife, above and below, and push the joint into its chest along with, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is to the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and firm at the root of the palm its side which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension.  
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and that two ministers extend the arm, and hold it so that it does not move during the extension; 
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm in each direction, after you have wrapped a long and wide double cloth around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the two hands join the joint to its hand, then anoint it with any oil to soften the joint, then push the joint forcefully until it returns. 
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, put a dry plaster with the yolk of an egg on top, and hold it firmly, and bind the arm to the collar of the patient, and leave it for several days, then untie it. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the ligament, and let it.  
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	And if you see that the joint is not setting well, start again with the bandaging and the ligament, and leave it so for some days, until it is firmly set.  
puis le deslie.	then untie it. 
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels pain after the joint is reset and it moves, bathe it and rub it well, and press until it is soothed.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	or you put a piece of fat wool on the joint, then leave it for one day and night, then remove it, and wash it.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when it sweats, rub the joint gently, then put the wool back on, and then wash it. 
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And thus do it two or three times, until it is healed.  
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	And if you see, so put on a fleece of moist moss heated with butter, and strain it upon. 
si revenra a sa disposition.	If it will return to its place.  
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and its return is lighter than other joints. 
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to bring it back to its place immediately when it dislocates, so that the joint is not swollen, or an abscess comes to the boil hot.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the return is that you put the ailing hand upon a table, and extend the minister's hand, and he places it equal, in such a way that it puts its palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes it until it returns. 
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	Nevertheless, it is necessary that you look if it is well in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Therefore, place the patient's back of their hand upon a table at extension and retraction. 
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then the patient puts their back of their hand on the table, and the one caring for them puts their hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, that is well.  
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then let the patient be bound with soothing ointments to appease the abscess, and leave it so without starting again. 
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, then the joint remains twisted. 
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and does no harm to the patient except that as long as the hand is numb, and cannot strain anything at all:
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	Then you know that the nerve has been cut, or the artery.  
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If there is no other remedy but to restrain by cautery according to the case, and perhaps it is not worth anything else. 
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the splint that we have said, then restrain it and let it be for 5 days, then untie it and leave as is.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no wound, then the hot water cloth, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Never are the two parts of the hand dislocated on either side, never to the back of the palm or the belly;  
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Therefore is the duty, and put the dislocation to your pouches until it returns, then support the head of the shoulder, and the bring toward the part where it is disjoined.  
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	And let him rest for a day, and then put it even that day; 
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	And do not bind it, as we have said, and unbind it each day, and make it move, and bind it again;  
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do this often, until it is straight, and just as well, if it is dislocated at the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is sound;   
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And just as well, when it is dislocated from another place. 
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of the dislocation of the spine
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are more dislocations, there is no cure, because death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that the dislocations jump out without will, and cannot be held, and many times are softened any limb, or both thighs or the two arms or one.  
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And many times the bone moves to four parts.  
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	That one which moves at the back is called "gilbositez": 
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The cure for this is that you reward it if the gilbositez came from childhood:
