si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	If there is no cure nor healing at all. 
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And the one that comes from a fall or blows or similar things, the ancients said manners of cures by great words, which has not in all great profit;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abridged it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in diverse manners. 
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the gilbositez that comes to the shoulder before, there is nothing nor health;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also those that come directly in II ribs, and one cannot cure them except for the one properly that comes to the back, as I say. 
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and that the patient be stretched on his face in the same place even, and have a constraint under him, that he does not bleed. 
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then put the splint at the head in the earth, and the other at the feet, and tie a rope under the armpits of the patient, and the other at the hips, and knees, and ankles. 
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two ministers know the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two splints;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be well fastened, the splints as we have said, and the mire puts his palms on the spine straight, until it comes back. 
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not come back by this cure, then take a board of III arms long, and put it under the patient, and the patient be on his side, and push the head of the board under the patient, then put the middle of the board on the spine; 
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and put the patient's feet on the other end of the table, and press well, until it returns to its place. 
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you see, do it to the turning wheel that turns by hand. 
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And is that you place two irons at the head of the sick person with one arm, and towards the feet the other, and between each iron, above and below, a palm's width of long. 
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and have in each iron one hole, where the turning wheel goes, and that the irons be firmly in earth so that they do not move. 
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each two irons have one turning iron, on which the chain turns, and have in the two turning ones two small irons a palm long, to turn the wheel. 
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the chain which is among the axles to one wheel towards the head, and the other chain towards the feet to the other wheel, and each of the assistants turns his wheel with all the chain, and the master puts the spine even as we have said. 
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is equal, put a drying plaster with an abundance of egg, and then the dressings, and then the splint of a tablet of III fingers long, that pricks the place of the vertebra and the part of the healthy spine, then tie it with a bandage, as we have said, and use the patient of subtle nourishment, until it is healed;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	And if anything comes in the end of the health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the splint that we have said before; 
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	And sometimes one administers a piece of wood, and sometimes the appearance comes in the lower vertebra of the back, and one thinks that it is dislocation; 
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	and it is the bone that opens, for which reason one should not have presumption there. 
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	By chance might come death.  
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come out only with dislocations, and not like other joints.  
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	And the joint of the hip is dislocated in accordance with four parts: 
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	Inside and outside, and front and back; 
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	And more inside then, and less dislocated front and back.  
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens the patient's knee more than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend his knee at all.  
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And it is the leg which is near swollen with a hot abscess, because of that the head of the pelvis comes forward. 
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes to the fever, so is this accident contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of him who has it in front, are that his leg is well aligned according to its completion; 
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	Nevertheless, do not double the knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot before, and holds back his urine, and swells his groin, and when he goes, he passes over his heel. 
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him to whom it happens in the rear, is that he cannot spread his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the hip is at the place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The return of this kind of dislocation is that you look at whether the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its position, if there is no treatment. 
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	And there is no need for him to be presumptuous.  
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in the one whose dislocation is fresh, and this is of the IV manners of dislocation, haste that you return the joint, and the extension inward and outward, and the movement to the right and left; 
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	For by chance it will return, and has no need of other treatment.  
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must apply strong force, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or to the ligament that is tied above the knee.  
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	And another minister stretches his hand above in such a manner that he thrusts his hands below his shoulders, then he tightens with a strong pull upon the hip.   
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another one seizes the chief of the ligament; 
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And extend upwards and downwards all at once, as long as the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remain hanging. 
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to IV likenesses, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If this does not work, it is necessary to put care to its likeness.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is at the armpit, it is necessary that you support the patient on his healthy ribs, then put the ligament on the root of the hip, and the place which is below the groin, then extend the ligament upwards towards the arm, and toward the shoulder. 
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	then grasp with other ministers his arms, and embrace the large part of the diseased hip, and extend it outwards.  
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	then it will return to its place now; 
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner that we have said, then you must tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong band above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the affected leg be extended two fingers more than the other. 
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	Then hang it from the top of a pole, and let it be two arms long above the ground;  
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then command the minister to embrace the head of the hip, and let other ministers stand with the patient, who together embrace the hips, because the joint will now return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is at the back, let the patient lie down, as we have said in the one who has sciatica, and restrain the band on the affected leg properly, and on the foot as well;
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put two splints, one at the head and one at the feet, then place a splint between the hips of the patient to maintain shape. 
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have a plant of wet cloths around him so that the patient does not shiver, then extend each minister toward him, and the one who is watching puts it in place with his hand.  
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If this is not so, place on a [table], and press it as we have said in the chapter on dislocations, and lay the patient on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is visible, then it is necessary to extend the affected leg as much as possible, and according to what I have said;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and put the one who is watching his pain on top of the affected bone, then press with the other hand and move it down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is at the back, it is not necessary to extend the patient downwards, nor to raise upwards on the ground, but rather that it be as if the hip was dislocated backwards, as we have said about the support on the two hips;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and let it be on its face, and the ligament is extended as we have said above, and one must press on the joint to the table. 
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and will be straight when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even;  
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then adjust the hips, and put on the splint, and the strain of a bandage, so that the hip does not move; 
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and rest for three or four days, then untie it, and put the splint on;
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are even, so strain, as before, and let it rest for three days; 
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then untie it, and let him walk well, until the limb is strengthened. 
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The knee is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, inwards and outwards, and backwards; 
et ne desalue point devant.	and do not dislocate again. 
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend their leg at their hip, and if it does not rest at their hip, know that it is dislocated. 
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	And the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend their leg if they can, and place your back on their hip, and put their foot on your feet; 
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take his knee in your palms, and pull it between your thighs, then bend the two bones that form the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	And some other ministers extend his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he can move his leg to his hip lightly. 
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	And put the plaster on top, and make him rest his leg to his hip, and let them stay together for strong III days or IV, then untie it. 
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And do not let the patient work at all to go, until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes sprained, and sometimes dislocated completely, inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the sign of it is that the ankle is swollen, and it hurts before in the part where it was dislocated: 
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The returning of it is light, and one must extend it gently with his hands when he is only feeling pain.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated altogether, it is necessary that you make the patient sit straight, and hold him one minister by the leg, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	Then treat the foot with your right hand, then with your left twice, then upward at the front, and gently push the foot upward. 
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	And do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot;  
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	If it returns, that is good; 
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	if not, begin the work again, for it will return;  
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	And if it cannot return thus, have the patient lie on his back on the ground, and insert a stick firmly into the ground between his thighs, and tie cloths around it, so that the patient does not move. 
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then hold the patient's thigh with one hand, and other ministers extend the foot to their hands or to the stick, so that they tie it above the ankle of the foot; 
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then extend each minister equally, and the stick should be straight between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when we straighten him; 
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then put the mirrors equal to the dislocation with your hands, and other ministers hold the healthy leg at the bottom, and the dislocation will return easily. 
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is set right, apply the plaster and dressings on top, and strain it firmly, and tie the leg to the leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle behind so that the ligatures are not too tight.  
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligatures soften, then strain it again.
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	Then untie it on the third day or the fourth, and forbid the patient to walk for four days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if he goes before this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come there, it is necessary that you soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the hips are dislocated, it is necessary to stretch them well without effort, and it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any knot of the foot or leg, then you must make the patient sit on a hard surface or table entirely straight, and put your foot on what separates those joints, then press with your foot firmly until it returns. 
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	And when it is even and there appears nothing, put under the sole of the foot a table at the shoulder, then strain it firmly, and let it remain for 3 days, then untie it.  
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it rest until it is healed. 
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, many times happens that the patient dies:  
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you are not presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and you have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and patient, nor bold;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	And use at the beginning of things soothing to an abscess hot, and leave the patient in God's hands, if you do not see hope of health; 
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope there, then reset now the limb to its place, so that the abscess hot comes up in it.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is in place, administer soothing things to the heated abscess, and treat the wound as it is fitting, with dried ointment;  
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if the dislocation comes with a fracture, and bones are broken, set them, and do what we have said in simple illnesses;  
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and keep yourself from entering the way of fear, according to what I have said, for it harms you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your limbs and body.
